601 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Hoskins v. Howard


No. 38478


Supreme Court of Mississippi


214 Miss. 481; 59 So. 2d 263; 1952 Miss. LEXIS 492



May 26, 1952, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Opinion on Motion for Appointment in the Place of the Disqualified Judge, June 9, 1952, Reported at 214 Miss. 481 at 502.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the circuit court of Hinds County; M. M. McGowan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and judgment for appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An action in the Circuit Court of Hinds County (Mississippi) for a writ of mandamus to compel the Secretary of State to cancel the registration of appellants and to register appellees as the Republican Party of Mississippi. The pleadings were amended to pray for a writ of certiorari. The lower court held that appellants were not entitled to registration and were improperly registered by the Secretary because they had changed their name.


OVERVIEW: In 1928, appellants perfected an organization which they named the Independent Republican Party of Mississippi. Appellees, prior to that time and since, have constituted an organization which they named the Republican Party of Mississippi. The delegates to the Republican National Convention selected by appellees had been recognized by that convention as representing the party in Mississippi. The court reversed. It opined that the mere change in name of appellants, without any change whatsoever in the organization, was not such a change as justified a rejection of their application for registration. The court noted that if appellants had not adopted a resolution changing their name and had registered under their former name appellees would not have been entitled to register as the Republican Party of Mississippi. The court concluded that the lower court judge was under the erroneous impression that the plain provisions of Chapter 458, Laws of 1950 (Mississippi), were invalid in authorizing the Secretary of State to register the name of the first political party applying for registration.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and entered judgment for appellants.

 

602 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Grenada v. Andrews


No. 38341


Supreme Court of Mississippi


214 Miss. 105; 58 So. 2d 382; 1952 Miss. LEXIS 451



April 21, 1952, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the circuit court of Grenada County; Henry L. Rodgers, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and judgment for appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Grenada County (Mississippi) denying its motion for a directed verdict after judgment was rendered in favor of appellee taxpayer in an action whereby the taxpayer sought recovery of excess payments of privilege taxes wrongfully collected from him by the city.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer, a cab driver, voluntarily paid the city a privilege tax based on an ordinance. The ordinance was later declared void, and the taxpayer filed an action against the city seeking repayment of each amount he had voluntarily submitted for a period of four years. The city admitted that the ordinance was void, but the payments made by the taxpayer were voluntary, and thus were not recoverable. The city filed a motion for a directed verdict, which was denied, and judgment was rendered in favor of the taxpayer. The city appealed the decision contending it was erroneous. The court noted that in the absence of a statute providing otherwise, taxes or license fees voluntarily paid without protect could not have been recovered, although assessed and collected without legal authority. In addition, a payment was voluntary where it was made willingly and without objection, and in all cases there was no compulsion or duress nor any necessity of making the payment as a means of freeing the person or property from legal restraint. Finding that the payment was voluntary, the court held that the city's motion for a directed verdict should have been granted.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court was reversed and judgment was issued for the city.

 

603 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Burge v. Board of Sup'rs


No. 38451


Supreme Court of Mississippi


213 Miss. 752; 57 So. 2d 718; 1952 Miss. LEXIS 422



March 24, 1952, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the circuit court of Pearl River County; Sebe Dale, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review a decision of the circuit court of Pearl River County (Mississippi), which overruled the taxpayers' exceptions and sustained an order of appellee Board of Supervisors of Pearl River County. The Board had overruled the taxpayers' objections to a report of county election commissioners regarding the result of an election for a bond issue.


OVERVIEW: The Board issued bonds for the purpose of constructing a building in which to operate an industry for the manufacture of garments under the authority of Chapter 241, Laws of 1944. The taxpayers had protested against the acceptance of the report of the commissioners as to the result of an election in the three districts of the Board. The taxpayers' objections were overruled by the Board, and the circuit court affirmed. In affirming, the court held that the language of Chapter 241 did not require a showing that two-thirds of the voters in each of the districts voted in favor of the bond issue. Under the terms of the Act, it was sufficient if two-thirds of those voting in the municipality and two-thirds of those voting outside the municipality voted in favor of the issue. The court concluded that all of the conditions set forth in the first paragraph of § 10 of Chapter 241, Laws of 1944, were complied with in obtaining a certificate of public convenience and necessity from the state for the establishment of the industry. The court found that the petition was a sufficient indication of a desire to enter a plan under § 10.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

604 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Wheeler v. Shoemake


No. 38203


Supreme Court of Mississippi


213 Miss. 374; 57 So. 2d 267; 1952 Miss. LEXIS 378



February 18, 1952, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the chancery court of Covington County; Neville Patterson, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Reversed, writ of habeas corpus was ordered as to conviction, and appellant was ordered held under his bond.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile challenged the judgment from the Chancery court of Covington County (Mississippi), which held that the circuit court had full jurisdiction over the juvenile. The juvenile sought review under the Youth Court Act of 1946, Miss. Laws 1946, ch. 207; Miss. Code §§ 7185-01 through 7185-30 (1942). The chancery court dismissed the juvenile's petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court accepted the juvenile's guilty plea for grand larceny and he was sentenced to five years of hard labor. After the plea was entered, the juvenile employed an attorney who filed a motion to set aside the judgment and to grant a new hearing. The motion was overruled and the juvenile petitioned the court. The state argued that the Youth Court Act of 1946, Miss. Laws 1946, ch. 207; Miss. Code §§ 7185-01 through 7185-30 (1942), was invalid. The court held that the Act was valid. The chancery court erroneously held that the circuit court had full jurisdiction of the juvenile. In its analysis, the court gave detailed consideration to the history and purposes of juvenile court. Because of the provisions of § 3 of the Youth Court Act, the circuit court had no jurisdiction of appellant at the time of his conviction because he was then 17 years of age. The original exclusive jurisdiction over him under § 3 was in the youth court division of the chancery court. Hence the judgment of conviction under which appellant was held was void, and the chancery court should have issued the writ of habeas corpus.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that sentenced the juvenile upon a guilty plea for grand larceny. The writ of habeas corpus was ordered as to conviction, and the juvenile was ordered held under his bond pending any further action of grand jury.

 

605 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Quinn v. McComb


No. 38072


Supreme Court of Mississippi, Division A


212 Miss. 730; 55 So. 2d 479; 1951 Miss. LEXIS 503



December 3, 1951, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the chancery court of Pike County; R. W. Cutrer, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Chancery Court of Pike County (Mississippi) dismissed appellant electors' bill to enjoin appellee city from setting up additional low income housing units under the Housing Authorities Act, Chapter 338, Laws of 1938, § 7295 et seq., Code of 1942 (Mississippi). The electors appealed.


OVERVIEW: The electors alleged that they were signers of a petition praying for an election to determine whether the city could extend the units operated by the city housing authority. The election was never held. The lower court dismissed the bill, holding that the electors failed to prove any grounds for equitable relief. The court rejected the electors' argument that the original resolution setting up the housing authority was invalid because it was not published. Under § 7319, Code of 1942, resolutions setting up housing authorities did not need to be published. The court also found that the city had authority to set up the authority, even though there was no provision to do so in its charter because the Act did not exclude cities operating under a special charter. The court found that the city was permitted by its charter to enter into a cooperation agreement because it was expressly empowered to do so by the Housing Act. The court found that a statute had to be construed so as to render it valid, if possible.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

606 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Lumpkin v. Birdsong


No. 38116


Supreme Court of Mississippi, Division B


212 Miss. 616; 55 So. 2d 230; 1951 Miss. LEXIS 491



November 26, 1951, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the chancery court of Hinds County; V. J. Stricker, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, operator and commercial carrier, sought review of a decree of the Chancery Court of Hinds County (Mississippi), which dismissed a bill for injunction against appellee Commissioner of Public Safety who exacted a payment made under protest for a license as an operator of a private commercial carrier under Chapter 408, § 1, Laws 1950.


OVERVIEW: Appellants commenced an action seeking an injunction against the Commissioner who had exacted the payment for a license as an operator of a private commercial carrier-under protest by the operator--pursuant to Chapter 408, § 1, Laws 1950 (Mississippi). A temporary injunction was dissolved upon motion, and the bill dismissed, and the operator appealed. The court affirmed the judgment holding that the decree was proper and that the operator was liable for the license. The court held that the liability applied uniformly to all personal regularly so engaged as operators of private commercial carriers and the attack upon the constitutionality of Chapter 474, § 2(22) of the Laws of 1950 (Mississippi) was lacking merit. It was clear that appellants were, in respect to the use of the truck, a private commercial carrier by motor vehicle and that it was used in the furtherance of the commercial enterprise of railroading.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decree.

 

607 of 825 DOCUMENTS


McComb v. Pike County


No. 38112


Supreme Court of Mississippi, Division B


212 Miss. 90; 54 So. 2d 171; 1951 Miss. LEXIS 431



September 24, 1951, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the chancery court of Pike County; R. W. Cutrer, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the City of McComb, Mississippi, sought review of a decision of the Chancery Court of Pike County (Mississippi), which sustained a special demurrer filed by appellee, Pike County, Mississippi, to the City's bill under § 8367, Miss. Code 1942, to recover one-half of the road taxes levied and collected by the County for the two years on property located within the City.


OVERVIEW: Section 8367 provided that the City was entitled to one-half of the road taxes collected by the County. The County tendered what it asserted the City was entitled to under § 8367. The City contended that a fund levied and collected by the County as a purported bridge fund was actually a road fund, and the City sought to recover one-half of that fund. The trial court sustained the County's special demurrer. On appeal, the court found no error. The court rejected the City's contention that Chapter 104, Laws of 1932 (Miss.), later codified at § 9880, Miss. Code 1942, and under which the levies were made, did not authorize separate levies for roads and bridges. Section 9880 expressly authorized a "levy or levies," which the court construed to authorize separate levies for bridges and roads. The court concluded that the levies, in specifying the Laws of 1932, complied with the express requirements of § 9889, Miss. Code 1942. The court further rejected the City's contention that the County had adopted a device to defraud the City. The court reasoned that the same allegations as were set forth in the City's bill had been held in a prior case to not state a ground for recovery.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision and remanded the case for further proceedings to determine the amount of the road fund to which the City was entitled.

 

608 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Dossett v. State


No. 37947


Supreme Court of Mississippi, Division B


211 Miss. 650; 52 So. 2d 490; 1951 Miss. LEXIS 395



May 14, 1951, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the circuit court of Covington County; Homer Currie, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction from the Circuit Court of Covington County (Mississippi) for unlawful possession of intoxicating liquor under § 2613, Code of 1942. Defendant contended that admission of certain testimony was improper, that the State had no jurisdiction to regulate the possession of intoxicating liquor, that the jury instructions were erroneous, that a search of his home was illegal, and that the statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: A deputy spied defendant from across a creek as defendant emerged from the bushes, walked along the creek for several hundred yards, crawled into a thicket, and left with four bottles that he carried to his home. That same day, the deputy observed defendant and his wife return to the thicket with a sack. The deputy thereafter entered the thicket and discovered a metal can containing nine bottles of whisky in the ground. The next day the deputy and the sheriff hid near the thicket and defendant returned, they heard the sound of the lid being returned to the metal can, and thereafter discovered four of the nine bottles missing. The can and remaining bottles were seized and a search warrant was obtained. Nothing was found on defendant's property. On appeal, the court held that admission of the entire chain of events was proper because the events were so intimately connected that all the testimony was necessary. Defendant's claim that the United Nations Charter divested the State from jurisdiction was without merit, the jury instructions correctly stated the law, and because nothing was seized from his property, the whisky was admissible and the statute was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

609 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Meridian v. Davidson


No. 37905


Supreme Court of Mississippi


211 Miss. 683; 53 So. 2d 48; 1951 Miss. LEXIS 399



May 14, 1951, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the circuit court of Lauderdale County; Jesse H. Graham, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged a judgment based on a jury verdict of the Circuit Court of Lauderdale County (Mississippi) that reversed a decision of the Civil Service Commission (Commission) of the city that had affirmed the action of the city manager, who discharged appellee fireman for drunkenness and insubordination. There was no record of the Commission's hearing.


OVERVIEW: The employee demanded that a transcript of the record be filed by the Commission with the trial court, as required by 1944 Miss. Laws ch. 208, § 10 (the Act), but the testimony taken before the Commission was not transcribed by a reporter. Therefore, the jury in the trial court, which was confined by the provisions of the Act to the determination of the issue of whether the judgment of the Commission appealed from was made in good faith for cause, had no means of knowing on what testimony the Commission had acted when it approved and affirmed the action of the city manager in discharging the fireman on the charges preferred against him. Seven witnesses testified who did not testify at the hearing before the Commission, and it did not appear whether or not all of the witnesses who did testify before the Commission had testified again in the trial court, which made it a trial de novo. The court overruled that portion of the decision in McLeod v. Civil Service Commission, 198 Miss. 721, which granted a trial de novo before a jury. Whether the Commission acted in good faith was a question of law and could not be addressed without the record before the Commission.


OUTCOME: The case was reversed and remanded and the trial court was ordered to send it back to the Commission for the retaking of testimony on the charges against the fireman and to file a transcript thereof in the trial court prior to a rehearing of any appeal in the trial court, which was to be without a jury.

 

610 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Lucedale Veneer Co. v. Rogers


No. 37591


Supreme Court of Mississippi, Division A


211 Miss. 613; 53 So. 2d 69; 1951 Miss. LEXIS 393



May 14, 1951 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reported at 211 Miss. 613 at 623.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Opinion of October 23, 1950, Reported at 211 Miss. 613.



DISPOSITION: Suggestion of error overruled.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer sought en banc review of a decision in favor of appellee worker on his claim for worker's compensation for a hernia under 1948 Miss. Laws ch. 354 § 8(f).


OVERVIEW: The employer's attorneys in their suggestion of error contended that the worker's proof was insufficient to show that the descent of the hernia immediately followed as a result of sudden effort or severe strain, or that there was severe pain in the hernial region, or that such prostration resulted that the worker was compelled to cease work immediately. On appeal, the court first rejected the argument that the court did not have authority to reverse a decision from the Mississippi Compensation Commission where there was prejudicial error of law or fact. It then found that the Commission had misinterpreted the law. The language of the statute required the worker to show that the descent of the hernia immediately followed as the result of the sudden effort. The court interpreted the language "immediately" to mean soon enough and in such manner as to make it appear clear that the descent was the effect of the strain. This was supported by the fact that statute required the hernia be noticed by the worker within 48 hours.


OUTCOME: The court overruled the employer's suggestion of error and affirmed its decision that the worker was entitled to compensation.

 

611 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Love v. State


No. 37978


Supreme Court of Mississippi, Division A


211 Miss. 606; 52 So. 2d 470; 1951 Miss. LEXIS 392



May 7, 1951, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the circuit court of Attala County; Henry L. Rodgers, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction from the Circuit Court of Attala County (Mississippi) for indecent assault upon or violation of the person of a female child under the age of 13 years, as set forth in Miss. Code of 1942, § 2052. Defendant contended for the first time on appeal that the indictment was insufficient because it omitted to charge that he was over the age of 18 years, although that was an element of the offense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of indecent assault on a female child under the age of 13 years under Miss. Code of 1942, § 2052. The indictment charged defendant with unlawfully and feloniously making an assault and stated that the victim was under the age of 13 years but failed to charge that defendant was a male person above the age of 18 years. Defendant appealed, raising the failure of the indictment to allege his age. The State contended that under Miss. Code of 1942, § 2449, the defect in the indictment could not be raised for the first time on appeal. The court rejected the State's contention, holding that § 2449 only applied to defects that could be amended without touching any matter of substance. Because defendant's age went to the very essence of the offense, it could not be waived by defendant. The crime was a statutory offense requiring proof of defendant's age above 18 years as an element, which was an affirmative fact that was required to be charged and proven by the State, and was not a mere formality. Section 2449 was not meant to deprive defendant of his right to have the charge against him clearly and fully stated and the indictment was therefore fatally defective.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction, discharged him, and remanded without prejudice to the right of the State to bring a charge against defendant founded upon a proper indictment.

 

612 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Burns v. Godwin


No. 37900


Supreme Court of Mississippi, Division B


211 Miss. 310; 51 So. 2d 486; 1951 Miss. LEXIS 357



March 26, 1951, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the circuit court of Tishomingo County; Raymond T. Jarvis, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment for plaintiff and defendant appealed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court of Tishomingo County (Mississippi), which upheld an Alabama judgment that found in favor of appellee motorist, in the motorist's action for damages that arose from a collision between his vehicle and the driver's vehicle while both vehicles were operating on a highway in Alabama.


OVERVIEW: The driver and the motorist were involved in an accident in Alabama. Both were residents of Mississippi. The motorist sued the driver in Alabama. The motorist served notice on the driver in accordance with the Alabama Nonresident Motorist Statute, Title 7, § 199 Code of Alabama of 1940. The motorist obtained a judgment against the driver. Thereafter, the motorist filed suit against the driver in Mississippi based upon his duly authenticated copy of the Alabama judgment. The trial court upheld the Alabama judgment. The driver appealed arguing that the Alabama legislature only intended to provide its citizens with a remedy under § 199. The court upheld the judgment. The court held that the Alabama court had personal jurisdiction and subject matter jurisdiction over the action. The court reasoned that the Alabama judgment was entitled to full faith and credit in Mississippi. The court reasoned that the motorist was authorized to file suit against the driver in Alabama, even though both parties were not residents of Alabama. Alabama was the most convenient place for the trial because that was where the accident occurred.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

613 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Davis-Wood Lumber Co. v. Ladner


No. 37797


Supreme Court of Mississippi, Division B


210 Miss. 863; 50 So. 2d 615; 1951 Miss. LEXIS 322



February 12, 1951, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the circuit court of Harrison County; L. C. Corban, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant lumber company sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Harrison County (Mississippi), which held that its agents were acting for it when they contracted with appellee lumber cutter, and that the contract in question did not authorize the charges assessed against the lumber cutter for the rents of the mill, trucks, and tractors used in the production of the lumber.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the issues were (1) whether the company organized and domiciled in Louisiana, was doing business in Mississippi from 1946 to 1948; (2) assuming that it was, whether the trial court acquired jurisdiction over it under Miss. Code Ann. § 1437 (1942) after it had ceased to do business in Mississippi at the time the action was brought, as to an action on a contract arising out of such previous business; (3) if there was jurisdiction, whether, under the facts, § 1437 violated the due process clause of the Fourteenth Amendment; and (4) whether there was sufficient evidence to support the jury's acceptance of the lumber cutter's version of his contract with the company. Upon review, the court held that the company was validly subject to the jurisdiction of the trial court, and that the judgment in favor of the lumber cutter on the contract arising out of the company's previous business in Mississippi was proper. Under the evidence the jury properly accepted the lumber cutter's version of the contract with respect to the rent and the identity of the contracting parties. The statements the company sent the lumber cutter did not constitute stated accounts binding upon him.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment finding that the company's agents were acting on its behalf when they contract with the lumber cutter and that the contract did not authorize the rent charges assessed against the lumber cutter.

 

614 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Planters Wholesale Grocery v. Kincade


No. 37505


Supreme Court of Mississippi


210 Miss. 712; 50 So. 2d 578; 1951 Miss. LEXIS 309



February 5, 1951, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the circuit court of Coahoma County; E. H. Green, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant truck driver challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Coahoma County (Mississippi) that entered a jury verdict for appellee automobile driver who sustained personal injuries due to an accident involving the two vehicles.


OVERVIEW: The automobile driver hit a truck that was parked blocking half of a highway lane, which had no flares or warnings of any kind. When he saw the parked truck he drove into a space between the truck and an approaching car but he was seriously hurt. The truck driver argued that it was error to refuse a requested peremptory instruction and argued that the gross negligence of the approaching car's driver and the gross negligence of the automobile driver was the proximate cause of the accident. The court disagreed and affirmed the judgment for the automobile driver. In order for appellant to be liable for damages resulting from his negligence, it was not necessary that his negligence was the sole cause of the injury. It was the proximate cause when it concurred with one or more causes to produce an injury. The trial court did not err in refusing an instruction that the automobile driver was guilty of contributory negligence. Although the general rule was that a driver must keep his car under control as to be able to bring it to a complete stop, the automobile driver acted as a reasonably prudent driver when confronting an emergency.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the jury verdict that was entered in favor of the automobile driver in his personal injury action against the truck driver.

 

615 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Ex parte Chain


No. 37878


Supreme Court of Mississippi, Division A


210 Miss. 415; 49 So. 2d 722; 1951 Miss. LEXIS 275



January 2, 1951, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the chancery court of Covington County; Neville Patterson, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and prisoner remanded to custody.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sheriff sought review of a decision from the Chancery Court of Covington County (Mississippi), which sustained appellee prisoner's petition for a writ of habeas corpus and ordered him discharged from confinement. The prisoner had sought his release on the grounds that his detention by the sheriff was depriving him of his liberty to the detriment of his health and well-being.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner had been convicted on a charge of unlawful possession of intoxicating liquor. The day after he was placed in the county jail, the prisoner presented a petition for a writ of habeas corpus directed to the sheriff and asking that he be released and discharged from custody on the ground that his detention by the sheriff was depriving him of his liberty to the detriment of his health and well-being and that his advanced age and the condition of his health made it necessary that he be discharged and relieved from punishment. The prisoner did not claim that he had not been lawfully tried and convicted or that he had been deprived of any of his constitutional rights. The court held that it was manifest from the petition itself that the prisoner was not entitled to relief. Under the Mississippi Constitution, the governor had the exclusive power to grant pardons and reprieves, including in cases where the possible effect of confinement on the health of an accused was concerned. The court could not release a prisoner in the absence of a showing of lack of jurisdiction in the trial court or other cause rendering the proceedings void. The prisoner was to be remanded to custody.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment sustaining the prisoner's petition for a writ of habeas corpus and ordered the prisoner remanded to the sheriff's custody.

 

616 of 825 DOCUMENTS


State v. Milam


No. 37595


Supreme Court of Mississippi, Division A


210 Miss. 13; 48 So. 2d 594; 1950 Miss. LEXIS 315



November 13, 1950, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Opinion on Suggestion of Error, January 15, 1951, Reported at 210 Miss. 13 at 26.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the circuit court of Quitman County; E. H. Green, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a decision from the Circuit Court of Quitman County (Mississippi), which, upon motion of defendants, who were indicted for assault and battery, quashed the indictment.


OVERVIEW: Defendants operated a store that was burglarized. They attempted to arrest two suspects. Defendants were charged with assault and battery and kidnapping. The suspects voluntarily signed a waiver of immunity and testified before a grand jury. Defendants were subpoenaed. Before the grand jury, the district attorney showed them the suspects' waiver, advised defendants of their privilege not to testify and that unless they also signed a waiver they could not testify about anything except the burglary. Apparently, the only evidence of the burglary was one suspect's alleged confession, which was allegedly obtained as a result of the alleged assault and battery. Defendants signed the waiver. Defendants were indicted. The court affirmed. The execution of the waiver and defendants' testimony were involuntarily given. Section 26 of the Mississippi Constitution provided that in criminal prosecutions the accused could not be compelled to give evidence against himself. The privilege applied to proceedings before a grand jury. Defendants were compelled to sign the waiver because they believed that their refusal to do so in front of the grand jury would have been seen as a confession of guilt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

617 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Willis Creek Drainage Dist. v. Yazoo County


No. 37622


Supreme Court of Mississippi, Division A


209 Miss. 849; 48 So. 2d 498; 1950 Miss. LEXIS 449



November 13, 1950, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the chancery court of Yazoo County; C. D. Williams, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action by appellant drainage district against appellee county board for injunctive relief to compel the board to make an order for the selling of certain lands in order to pay delinquent drainage assessments for certain years, the district sought review of a judgment from the Chancery Court of Yazoo County (Mississippi), which sustained a demurrer to the complaint and dismissed the action.


OVERVIEW: The bonds of the drainage district were issued and the last four matured in 1945, 1946, 1947, and 1948 respectively. The county purchased tracts of land in the drainage district. The district made assessments against the tracts of land for benefits, and the assessments were approved and confirmed by a court decree. The county paid the assessment levied for 1945 but declined to pay a similar amount for three succeeding years. The district brought an action against the county to collect the amount claimed against the county for the three years or to compel the sheriff to sell the property for the collection of these amounts. The trial court sustained a demurrer to the district's complaint and dismissed the suit. On appeal, the court reversed and held that when the county purchased the lands in 1945, they were encumbered with a judgment lien rendered under Miss. Code § 4695 (1942), which continued until the assessments were paid. The court said that the county was a voluntary purchaser that was not permitted to acquire the lands free of the lien, even if the county intended to use the lands for a public purpose. The court noted that there was no applicable exemption statute.


OUTCOME: The court held that the trial court erred in sustaining the demurrer to the complaint and dismissing the complaint. The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case.

 

618 of 825 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sisk


No. 37706


Supreme Court of Mississippi


209 Miss. 174; 46 So. 2d 191; 1950 Miss. LEXIS 377



May 8, 1950, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the circuit court of Monroe County; Raymond T. Jarvis, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An affidavit was filed against defendant which charged that he did wilfully and unlawfully have in his possession cases and loose bottles of intoxicating liquor, to wit beer, for the purpose of sale. The Circuit Court of Monroe County (Mississippi) sustained defendant's motion for an instruction peremptorily to the jury to return a verdict of not guilty. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The surplus clause, "for the purpose of sale," evidently was intended to negative the exception that defendant was in possession of the intoxicating liquor for "personal use." Such language, "for the purpose of sale," was not in the applicable statute. The State assigned error in the granting of the peremptory instruction and in the exclusion of evidence offered by the State that defendant's place of business had a reputation of being a place where intoxicating liquors were sold. The court affirmed. It noted that § 1153, Code 1942 (Mississippi) did not authorize the State to appeal from a judgment discharging a defendant on the ground that proof was insufficient to sustain a conviction. The court found that it would be difficult for a jury to separate the reputation of a business from the reputation of he who conducted the business sought to be characterized as bad. A place of business was inert, the occupant was substantially the source of its reputation, and its reputation was largely his reputation, during his tenancy. The court did not think that the lower court erred when such evidence was excluded.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

619 of 825 DOCUMENTS


W. A. Sheaffer Pen Co. v. Barrett


No. 37459


Supreme Court of Mississippi


209 Miss. 1; 45 So. 2d 838; 1950 Miss. LEXIS 357



April 24, 1950, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the chancery court of Hinds County; V. J. Stricker, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Complainant pen company appealed the decree of the Chancery Court of Hinds County (Mississippi), which denied injunctive relief to the pen company against defendant jewelry corporation.


OVERVIEW: The pen company entered into trade contracts with certain local retail dealers for the sale of its products such as fountain pens and writing fluids. The pen company sought a temporary injunction against the jewelry corporation to restrain them from selling the pen company's products at prices below those fixed by the pen company in its trade contracts. The jewelry corporation was a majority stockholder of the pen company. The pen company argued that its trade contracts were in conformity with the Fair Trade Act, Miss. Code Ann. § 1108 (1942). The jewelry corporation contended that the Fair Trade Act was unconstitutional because it impaired the freedom to contract. On appeal, the court held that the pen company stated a good cause of action for relief and that the Fair Trade Act was constitutional. The Fair Trade Act applied to "vertical" contracts, which enabled a manufacturer or owner to contract with a retailer as to the resale price of its own product, ensuring fair and open competition.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of the pen company's bill of complaint and remanded for a hearing on the bill, answer, and proof.

 

620 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Ferrell v. State


No. 37316


Supreme Court of Mississippi


208 Miss. 539; 45 So. 2d 127; 1950 Miss. LEXIS 272



March 13, 1950, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the circuit court of Jones County; B. F. Collins, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Jones County (Mississippi), entered upon a jury verdict, rejecting his claim of self-defense, convicting him of felonious assault on his wife's attorney, and imposing the maximum sentence of 10 years in prison.


OVERVIEW: The evidence at trial showed that defendant became angry when his lawyer in divorce proceedings informed him that it was necessary to pay a fee to his wife's attorney. Defendant stated that anyone who would represent her was "sorrier than a dog" and he drew a knife. When defendant made a slash at his own lawyer, the wife's attorney struck him. Defendant then pursued the wife's attorney around the room before stabbing him in the neck. Defendant was convicted, and he appealed. In affirming, the court ruled that his lawyer's eyewitness testimony was not inadmissible because he did not divulge any confidential communication, and because defendant had pleaded not guilty, it was not reversible error that he was arraigned before he retained counsel. The evidence warranted the jury's verdict and the sentence imposed, and the jury was properly instructed. No abuse of discretion was shown in the denial of a pretrial continuance.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

621 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Palmertree v. Garrard


No. 37172


Supreme Court of Mississippi


207 Miss. 796; 43 So. 2d 381; 1949 Miss. LEXIS 389



December 12, 1949, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the chancery court of Leflore County; R. E. Jackson, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged the judgment of the Chancery Court of Leflore County (Mississippi), which found in favor of appellees, commissioners of a municipal water and electric light commission, in the taxpayer's suit for an injunction against putting into effect the disability and pension system for the commission's employees as authorized by H.R. 27, Extraordinary Sess. (Miss. 1947) (House Bill 27).


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer sought to enjoin the disability and pension system as authorized by House Bill 27. The court affirmed the judgment for the commissioners. House Bill 27 did not violate Miss. Const. of 1890 § 87, which provided that no special or local law could be enacted for the benefit of individuals or corporations in cases that could be provided for by general law or where the relief sought could be given by any court. It also prohibited the legislature from suspending the operation of any general law for the benefit of any individual or private corporation. Miss. Const. of 1890 § 87 applied only to private corporations, not municipal corporations. House Bill 27 also did not violate Miss. Const. of 1890 § 88, which provided that the legislature should pass general laws under which cities could be chartered and under which corporations could be created. The city operated under a commission form of government. House Bill 27 could confer an additional right that other cities did not possess. House Bill 27 also did not violate Miss. Const. of 1890 § 96 because the source of the funds by which the system would be made operable did not involve a diversion or application of tax funds.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment for the commissioners.

 

622 of 825 DOCUMENTS


King v. Louisville


No. 37329


Supreme Court of Mississippi


207 Miss. 612; 42 So. 2d 813; 1949 Miss. LEXIS 374



November 14, 1949, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the circuit court of Winston County; J. P. Coleman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and appellant discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant merchant sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court, Winston County (Mississippi), which convicted the merchant of violation of an ordinance adopted by appellee city, which made it unlawful to exhibit and sell fireworks. The circuit court found the ordinance was valid and reasonable, and was proper under the police power of the city.


OVERVIEW: The merchant claimed the ordinance prohibiting the exhibition and sale of fireworks was invalid because it did not charge an offense punishable by the city and that the city did not have the authority to pass an ordinance prohibiting the sale of fireworks. The court reversed. A city had power to pass an ordinance that made any act amounting to a misdemeanor, under the state laws, an offense against the municipality. The state had no statute, however, which made it a misdemeanor to sell, barter, exchange, or give away, or to have in his possession, fireworks. The ordinance was invalid as unreasonable and was not authorized by any state statute. The city could not lawfully forbid what the legislature had expressly licensed or authorized, and could not validly expand or contract the application of a statute that defined a misdemeanor. The ordinance was not a regulation, but was a prohibition of a lawful business. The ordinance was void because it was not in conformity to and consistent with the general law of the state.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was reversed and the merchant was discharged.

Gatlin v. State


No. 37343


Supreme Court of Mississippi


207 Miss. 588; 42 So. 2d 774; 1949 Miss. LEXIS 371



November 14, 1949, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the circuit court of Newton County; Percy M. Lee, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed their convictions by the Newton County Circuit Court (Mississippi) for larceny.


OVERVIEW: Defendants, who were 14 and 15, were charged in youth court and adjudged delinquent under Chapter 207, Laws of Mississippi of 1946. Instead of imposing a sentence, the youth court certified them as adults. Defendants were then convicted of larceny. Defendants appealed and argued that the circuit court lacked jurisdiction. The convictions were affirmed. Section 15 of Chapter 207 allowed the youth court to certify a child as an adult if he committed a felony, and § 19 allowed a child convicted of a felony to be placed in a youth facility. Because the case could be resolved without reviewing the constitutionality of the Act, the court would not pass on its constitutionality.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions.

 

624 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Allen v. Kosciusko


No. 37201


Supreme Court of Mississippi


207 Miss. 343; 42 So. 2d 388; 1949 Miss. LEXIS 346



October 24, 1949, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the circuit court of Attala County; J. P. Coleman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant license holder sought review of a decision of appellee city, which revoked his license to operate a fleet of taxicabs. The Circuit Court of Attala County (Mississippi) sustained the city's motion to dismiss the license holder's appeal from the city's decision. The license holder appealed the judgment of the circuit court dismissing his appeal.


OVERVIEW: The city council revoked the license without notice and without a hearing. While the appeal was pending before the circuit court, the city council passed City of Kosciusko, Miss., Ordinance No. 168 (August 3, 1948), which revoked all outstanding taxicab permits and required persons operating taxicabs to file a written application for a new permit. On appeal, the court affirmed the circuit court's judgment. The license holder contended that he had a vested right in the license. The court held that the taxicab license was a mere personal privilege revocable for due cause because it permitted the license holder to do something that would otherwise be unlawful. It was not a vested or property right in a constitutional sense. The court held that the city had a right to amend its ordinances regulating taxicabs when, by reason of changed circumstances and conditions, the public safety reasonably required it to do so. Therefore, the city had a right to revoke all outstanding taxicab licenses. The court also held that the license holder could not challenge the constitutionality of certain regulations imposed by the new ordinance because he never applied for a permit under the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

 

625 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Greenwood v. Telfair


No. 37173


Supreme Court of Mississippi


207 Miss. 200; 42 So. 2d 120; 1949 Miss. LEXIS 329



September 26, 1949, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Chancery court of Leflore County; R. E. Jackson, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged a decree of the Chancery Court of Leflore County (Mississippi) for appellees in their suit to enjoin the city from exercising its authority under Chapter 738, Laws of 1948. This law was enacted to alleviate the discrimination against adjacent landowners in a current city paving project with respect to the proportion of the cost that they were required to bear, which was more than was required in prior projects.


OVERVIEW: The law gave the city the authority to pay from its general funds into the special street improvement bond fund for the current project such amount as might be necessary to pay the principal and interest on these bonds in an amount equal to the principal sum of the assessments authorized to be cancelled by the law. On appeal, the court found that this special law violated § 100 of the Constitution of 1890, which provided that any obligation or liability of any person or entity held by any city should never be remitted, released, or postponed, or in any way diminished by the legislature, nor should such liability or obligation be extinguished except by payment thereof into the proper treasury. When the city levied the special assessment against the land abutting the streets to be paved under the program, this assessment became final and was a judgment against the land to the extent of the sum assessed against it, and it was liable to the city for the payment of annual taxes sufficient to retire such judgment. To the extent that the plan adopted by the special law would release any portion of this judgment, the obligation to the city would be to that extent remitted or released.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decree.

Flowers v. State


No. 37251


Supreme Court of Mississippi


209 Miss. 86; 41 So. 2d 352; 1949 Miss. LEXIS 473



June 13, 1949, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied and Appeal Dismissed in the Supreme Court of the United States, May 1, 1950, 339 U.S. 946.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the circuit court of Leake County, Percy M. Lee, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of assault and battery with intent to kill following a jury trial in the Circuit Court of Leake County (Mississippi). He was sentenced to a term of imprisonment of seven and one-half years. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed on appeal that the trial court erred in denying his motion for a change of venue and in not directing a verdict in his favor. Defendant also claimed that African-Americans were systematically excluded from petit and grand jury panels within the county and that the indictment should have been quashed. The court affirmed. The court first determined that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying a change of venue. The court also found that the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motions to quash the petit jury panel and the indictment because there was no showing that African-Americans were systematically excluded from serving on petit and grand jury panels in the county. The court noted that there were only two African-Americans in the county who were registered to vote, which was a prerequisite to serving on a jury. The court also noted that one of them served as a petit juror in defendant's case and that the sheriff could not locate the other. Further, the court found that the impaneling of the grand jury was conclusive evidence of its competency and qualifications and that the evidence was sufficient to sustain defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

State v. Cummings


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Mississippi


206 Miss. 630; 40 So. 2d 587; 1949 Miss. LEXIS 288



May 9, 1949, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the chancery court of Yazoo County; M. B. Montgomery, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and decree rendered for appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State sought review of a judgment of the Chancery Court of Yazoo County (Mississippi) entered in favor of appellee property owners in the owners' separate actions in which they sought a refund from the State of taxes paid by them upon royalty interest in their lands.


OVERVIEW: The primary question for decision by the court was whether the owners' royalty interests in their land from which oil was actually being produced was legally assessable for ad valorem taxes in the years 1941 to 1943. The owners contended that no authority existed to assess such royalty interests ad valorem and that, therefore, they did not owe the tax and had a legal right to recover the same from the State. The court reversed the judgment entered in favor of the owners and entered a judgment for the State. The court held that Chapter 127, Mississippi Laws of 1944 applied to the refund of taxes illegally paid before, as well as after, its passage. The court held further that the royalty interests constituted a property interest and were, therefore, taxable. The court held further that the payment of taxes by one of the owners upon the surface above his mineral rights did not satisfy the taxes on his royalty interest in the land.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and entered a judgment for the State.

Mississippi State Board of Veterinary Examiners v. Watkins


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Mississippi


206 Miss. 330; 40 So. 2d 153; 1949 Miss. LEXIS 265



April 25, 1949, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the chancery court of Scott County; Roy P. Noble, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee filed a bill of complaint in the Chancery Court of Scott County, Mississippi, seeking injunctive relief against appellant state board of veterinary examiners on the ground that they had arbitrarily and willfully abused their discretion in refusing him a license to practice veterinary medicine, surgery, and dentistry. A decree granted injunctive relief and mandatorily enjoined the Board to grant appellee a license. The Board appealed.


OVERVIEW: Appellee' application to practice veterinary medicine, surgery, and dentistry in Mississippi was delayed and denied. Appellee filed his bill for injunctive relief. A decree granted the relief prayed for and mandatorily enjoined the Board to grant appellee a license. On the Board's appeal, the decree was affirmed. The court rejected the Board's claim that the denial was based upon a grandfather clause in § 6 of Chapter 371 of the Laws of Mississippi of 1946 that allowed the Board to deny the license under § 8922 of the Code of 1942 (Miss.). The court reasoned that Chapter 371 of the Laws of Mississippi of 1946 was the latest statute, it was complete in itself, and it completely occupied the field of the subject matter of veterinary licenses, so it impliedly repealed §§ 8917, 8922 of the Code of 1942 (Miss.), and Chapter 130 of the Laws of 1914. Appellant was of good moral character, had practiced veterinary medicine for more than ten years in Mississippi, and had paid his license fee to the Board, so the Board had no discretion to deny the license and their act of doing so was arbitrary and in violation of the § 6 of Chapter 371, Laws of 1946 (Miss.).


OUTCOME: The decree was affirmed.

 

629 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Moore v. Grillis


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Mississippi


205 Miss. 865; 39 So. 2d 505; 1949 Miss. LEXIS 472; 10 A.L.R.2d 1425



March 28, 1949, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the circuit court of Hinds County; H. B. Gillespie, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff non-certified accountants appealed from a judgment of the circuit court of Hinds County (Mississippi) that affirmed the dismissal of its action against defendant clients seeking to recover unpaid fees for the preparation of tax returns and denied the accountants' claim that Miss. Code Ann. § 8912 (1942), which prohibited non-certified accountants from preparing tax returns, was arbitrary and violated Miss. Const. § 14 (1890).


OVERVIEW: Non-certified accountants challenged the circuit court decision that affirmed the dismissal of their action against clients in which they sought to recover unpaid fees due for preparing tax returns. The circuit court held that the services provided by the non-certified accountants could only be rendered by certified public accountants (CPA) qualified under Miss. Code Ann. §§ 8905 through 8912. The court reversed the circuit court judgment. The court held that §§ 8905 to 8911 was a valid exercise of police power and constitutionally established the class known as CPAs, and provided for their regulation. However, the court held that § 8912 was unconstitutional, insofar as it affected the making and preparation of tax returns, because it went beyond the power of a state, under the guise of protecting the public, and arbitrarily prohibited the non-certified accountants from pursuing their lawful occupations. The court found that § 8912 did not attempt to provide any code of rules for practice by the non-certified accountants, and destroyed their right to charge compensation for their services in preparing income tax returns, -- which was destruction, not regulation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court judgment that was entered in favor of the clients in the non-certified accountants' action to recover fees due for tax preparation services. The case was remanded.

Craig v. North Mississippi Community Hospital


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Mississippi


206 Miss. 11; 39 So. 2d 523; 1949 Miss. LEXIS 239



March 28, 1949, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the circuit court of Hinds County; H. B. Gillespie, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state treasurer sought review of the judgment of the circuit court of Hinds County (Mississippi), which granted appellee private hospital's petition for a writ of mandamus that sought to compel the state treasurer to allocate funds the legislature appropriated to the private hospital pursuant to Miss. Laws of 1948, ch. 430.


OVERVIEW: The legislature appropriated funds to the private hospital, but the state treasurer would not allocate those funds to the private hospital, claiming ch. 430 was unconstitutional. Thus, the private hospital filed a petition for a writ of mandamus against the state treasurer, and the circuit court granted the writ. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the constitution was not violated by ch. 430. The court held that the legislature had the authority to appropriate public funds out of the state treasury for the care of the indigent sick in the nonprofit, nonsectarian hospitals of the state in accordance with Miss. Const. § 86, particularly where the expenditure of such funds for such purpose was under the supervision and control of a state agency. Miss. Const. § 14 was not violated because the money appropriated to the private hospital was to be expended under the rules, regulations, and supervision of a state agency, and Miss. Laws of 1948, ch. 430 bore a reasonable relation to a governmental purpose. Miss. Const. § 183 had no application because the legislature had not attempted to pledge or loan the credit of the state.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court, which granted the private hospital's petition for a writ of mandamus that sought to compel the state treasurer to allocate funds the legislature appropriated to the private hospital.

Southern Bus Lines, Inc. v. Amalgamated Ass'n of Street, etc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Mississippi


205 Miss. 354; 38 So. 2d 765; 1949 Miss. LEXIS 435; 23 L.R.R.M. 2397; 16 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P64,975



February 14, 1949, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the chancery court of Hinds County; V. J. Stricker, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bus line sought review of a judgment from the Chancery Court of Hinds County (Mississippi), which sustained appellees', unions and officers, general demurrer to the bus line's complaint and granted appellees' motion to dissolve the temporary injunction previously granted the bus line.


OVERVIEW: The bus line filed a bill of complaint against appellees seeking to enjoin them from continual trespass and damage to property arising out of a labor dispute. The complaint alleged, inter alia, that by threats and violence appellees have conspired to stop the general public and patrons from using the service of the bus line. The complaint listed 32 separate acts of violence and damage to property. The trial court authorized a preliminary injunction without notice to appellees. Thereafter, appellees interposed a general demurrer to the complaint and filed a motion to dissolve the temporary injunction. The trial court sustained appellees' general demurrer and dissolved the injunction. The bus line sought review. The court reversed the trial court's judgment, holding that though equitable action was never predicated on the prevention of crime, the fact that the conduct was punishable criminally did not constitute an adequate remedy so as to bar equitable relief. The court further held that state and federal courts had concurrent jurisdiction of suits of a civil nature, except where jurisdiction had been restricted by congress to the federal courts. The cause was remanded.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment that sustained appellees' demurrer to the bus line's complaint and that dissolved the preliminary injunction. The cause was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

Condon v. Snipes


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Mississippi


205 Miss. 306; 38 So. 2d 752; 1949 Miss. LEXIS 433



February 14, 1949, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the circuit court of Hinds County; H. B. Gillespie, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant homeowners challenged a decision of the Circuit Court of Hinds County (Mississippi), which dismissed, for want of jurisdiction, the homeowners' breach of contract action against appellee exterminator.


OVERVIEW: The exterminator, a nonresident of Mississippi, operated a termite control business. The homeowners contended that the exterminator breached a contract to eradicate termites and beetles from the property of the homeowners. Process was issued and served in strict accordance with the provisions of Chapter 246, Laws of 1940 (Mississippi). In reversing and remanding for a new trial, the court held that the exterminator was a conducting business that was subject to State control, Chapter 171, Laws of Mississippi of 1938 (§§ 5061-5011, Mississippi Code of 1942). The cause of action accrued in Mississippi out of the business of the exterminator that was transacted in Mississippi. The exterminator was subject to suit in Mississippi. The exterminator was properly brought into court under Chapter 246, Laws of 1940 (Mississippi). As such, the trial court erred in sustaining the exterminator's motion to dismiss for want of jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for a new trial.

 

633 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Moore v. State


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Mississippi


205 Miss. 151; 38 So. 2d 693; 1949 Miss. LEXIS 421



February 14, 1949, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the circuit court of Jasper County; Homer Currie, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After being convicted in a justice of the peace court, defendant appealed to and was convicted in the Circuit Court of Jasper County (Mississippi) of violating the Mississippi Bad Check Law, § 2153, Mississippi Code of 1942. On appeal, he challenged for the first time the sufficiency of the affidavit upon which he was convicted. Other issues included whether he was entitled to a directed verdict because the check was payment of a previous loan.


OVERVIEW: The State's evidence tended to show that the person who lent defendant money would not have parted with it without the issuance and delivery of defendant's check. The lending of the money and the delivery of the check were practically synchronous. On appeal, the court held that the completion of the transaction did not occur until defendant gave the check to the person. Thus, defendant was not entitled to a peremptory instruction on the ground that the money passed into his hands before he delivered the check. The court further held that the affidavit on which defendant was convicted followed precisely the form set out in § 2154 of the Mississippi Code of 1942 and was sufficient to charge defendant with a violation of § 2153. However, the court held that it was prejudicial error for the trial court to grant to the State an instruction to the effect that a prima facie presumption could be indulged in by the jury in support of and in addition to the evidence for the State. Because all the facts were in evidence the State was not entitled to an instruction upon a prima facie case.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for another trial.

State v. Southern Pine Co.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Mississippi


205 Miss. 80; 38 So. 2d 442; 1949 Miss. LEXIS 414



January 24, 1949, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the chancery court of Marion County; Lester Clark, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and decree for the State.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State challenged a decision of the Chancery Court of Marion County (Mississippi), which overruled the State's demurrers to appellee landowners' action that sought to have assessments and tax sales involving the landowners' land declared null and void.


OVERVIEW: The land in question was assessed and sold for delinquent taxes. The State attempted to purchase the land. The Land Commissioner (Mississippi), which the written approval of the Attorney General (Mississippi), erased and struck the land from the list of lands sold to the State and from the records of title in his office. The State contended that there was no equity on the face of the bill. In reversing and entering a decree in favor of the State, the court held that the chancery court was without jurisdiction in the case. Even though the bill was for the removal of a cloud, the adjudication sought was, in effect, merely a ratification of the legal action of a law official that was lawfully empowered to act. Section 4073, Code 1942 (Mississippi) did not provide for the ratification thereof by any court. The State's demurrers should have been sustained.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and entered a decree in favor of the State.

Hendrix v. Foote


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Mississippi


205 Miss. 1; 38 So. 2d 111; 1948 Miss. LEXIS 217



December 31, 1948 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reported at 205 Miss. 1 at 30.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Opinion of June 14, 1948, Reported at 205 Miss. 1.



DISPOSITION: On suggestion of error the suggestion was sustained; the former opinion was withdrawn; the decree reversed and the cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of the judgment from the trial court (Mississippi), which affirmed the decision from appellee board of supervisors in the taxpayer's action, seeking to invalidate the board's order, approving the assessment rolls.


OVERVIEW: At issue on appeal was: (1) whether the failure of the president of the board to sign the minutes of the meeting invalidated the order of the board, approving the assessment rolls; and, if not (2) whether Miss. Code § 9770 (1942) permitted the separate assessment and sale for taxes of a fractional interest in the oil, gas, and other minerals. Code § 2877 and Miss. Code § 2886 were literally complied with. Further, Miss. Code § 9770 permitted and required the separate assessment of undivided fractional interests in oil and gas to each separate owner of a fractional undivided interest and that the assessments of the undivided interests to the taxpayer were valid assessments and the sale thereof passed to the purchaser.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment from the trial court.

637 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Viator v. Stone


No. 36642


Supreme Court of Mississippi


203 Miss. 109; 37 So. 2d 1; 1948 Miss. LEXIS 236



October 11, 1948 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reported at 203 Miss. 109 at 115.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Opinion of January 12, 1948, Reported at 203 Miss. 109.



DISPOSITION: On suggestion of error. Suggestion of error sustained.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed an order from the Circuit Court of Harrison County (Mississippi) that sustained a plea of res adjudicata by defendant and that denied the taxpayer's request to discharge a final judgment previously rendered by the court. The taxpayer and his sureties on his appeal bond had obliged themselves by contract to satisfy the court's prior judgment.


OVERVIEW: The question before the court was whether § 10122, Code 1942 (Mississippi) had any application to the suit that the taxpayer sought to maintain. The court identified that § 10122 allowed the taxpayer to pay the tax and then seek to recover from the Mississippi State Tax Commissioner the assessment that the taxpayer claimed was excessive. Affirming the circuit court's dismissal, the court found that the prior litigation over the validity of the assessment was merged into the judgment of the circuit court previously on certiorari and the judgment of affirmance previously by the court. The previously rendered judgment was binding upon the taxpayer because of its finality, whether correct or not on the issue of the liability involved. Further, the court had no power to recall the judgment as a valid asset belonging to the State since the court previously overruled the suggestion of error and the court's prior action in so doing was affirmed by the Supreme Court of the United States. The taxpayer had the right to test the enforcement of the collection of the assessment until his right to have the factual issue determined had become merged into the final judgment rendered against him.


OUTCOME: The court ordered that the suggestion of error by the circuit court was sustained and the action of the circuit court in sustaining the plea of res adjudicata and dismissing the taxpayer's suit was affirmed.

 

638 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Kelly v. State


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Mississippi


204 Miss. 79; 36 So. 2d 925; 1948 Miss. LEXIS 344



October 11, 1948, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the circuit court of Jasper County; Homer Currie, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Jasper County (Mississippi), which convicted defendant of murder and sentenced defendant to life in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder and sentenced to life in prison. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's decision, quashed the indictment, and remanded the cause to the trial court. The court found that the indictment against defendant failed to properly state the charged offense because the indictment failed to include the word "did" and defendant failed to demur to the faulty indictment. Miss. Code § 2449 (Recomp. 1942) required defendant to raise any objections to the indictment before the jury was impaneled, but the court considered the adequacy of the indictment despite the failure of defendant to object to the indictment. The court explained that Miss. Const. § 26 required an indictment to enable defendant to prepare for trial, and the defect in the indictment was sufficient to have prejudiced defendant's rights. The court held that the indictment was void, and the conviction had to be reversed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court, which convicted defendant of murder. The court quashed the indictment and remanded the cause to the trial court.

 

639 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Reichman-Crosby Co. v. Stone


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Mississippi


204 Miss. 122; 37 So. 2d 22; 1948 Miss. LEXIS 350



October 11, 1948, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the circuit court of Hinds County; H. B. Gillespie, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant non-resident corporation challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Hinds County (Mississippi), which sustained a demurrer filed by appellee, the Chairman of the Tax Commission of Mississippi (chairman), to the corporation's action that sought to recover the use tax that it had paid under protest to the chairman.


OVERVIEW: The corporation filed an action that challenged the right of the chairman to require the corporation to collect tax from its purchasers at the time that it made sales in Memphis, Tennessee, and delivered the goods to a common carrier for transportation to the purchasers in Mississippi. According to the provisions of the Use Tax Law, Miss. Code Ann. § 10148 (1942), the tax would not apply with respect to the use of any article of tangible personal property sold outside of Mississippi until the transportation thereof finally ended and the article had become commingled with the general mass of property within Mississippi. The trial court granted the chairman's demurrer. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded the case to the trial court for an order that refunded the tax. The corporation was not subject to the operation of the use tax because it was only in interstate commerce, engaged in no local activities, and had no presence in Mississippi such as to constitute doing business there. The Commerce Clause, the Equal Protection Clause, and the Due Process Clause thus barred the application of the Use Tax Law against the corporation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court and remanded the case for an order that required the chairman to refund the use tax paid by the non-resident corporation.

 

640 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Batson v. Pearl River County


No. 36757


Supreme Court of Mississippi


204 Miss. 882; 35 So. 2d 712; 1948 Miss. LEXIS 416



June 14, 1948, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Suggestion of Error.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the circuit court of Pearl county.

Hon. J. C. Shivers, Judge.

For original memorandum opinion see 35 So. (2d) 72.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Pearl County (Mississippi), which entered judgment in favor of appellee county in the landowner's action challenging a tax assessment on his lands.


OVERVIEW: The landowner alleged that the county placed all cut-over lands in the county at an arbitrary per-acre assessment value, and contended that the county knew that his lands were on an average not worth as much as the average of other lands in the same cut-over land classification. The landowner further alleged that the arbitrary classification of his land worked an unconstitutional discrimination against him. The court noted that the evidence showed that the landowner's land was actually worth more than the value at which it was assessed. Moreover, the court held that the landowner presented no authority under Miss. Code. Ann. § 1196 (1942) allowing the court on an appeal of a tax assessment to address the broad constitutional question prescribed by the landowner. On the basis of existing case authority and the fact that appellant's land was not assessed at more than its true value, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court noted that it had not foreclosed the possibility that the question presented by the landowner could be addressed on a statutory appeal, only that no authority for such an appeal had been shown.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.
