642 of 825 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sanders


No. 36780


Supreme Court of Mississippi


203 Miss. 475; 35 So. 2d 529; 1948 Miss. LEXIS 296



May 24, 1948, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the chancery court of Jones county.

Hon. Roy P. Noble, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners filed a bill of complaint to quiet and confirm their title as against defendants, a county, the State of Mississippi in its sovereign capacity, and the State Land Commissioner. Defendants appealed a decree of the Chancery Court of Jones County (Mississippi) cancelling tax deeds and quieting title in the landowners.


OVERVIEW: The proof disclosed that the landowners and their predecessors in title had been in continuous, open, notorious, and adverse possession of the land since 1881 and long prior thereto, and it was agreed that the records disclosed the payment of taxes thereon at least for the period from 1895 to 1930, and that the amount paid for a patent in 1939 was sufficient to cover all taxes from 1930 to that date. The court held that the State has no right, title, or interest whatsoever, either legal or equitable, in the lands. The chancery court had jurisdiction of the suit to cancel tax sales and to quiet and confirm the title of the landowners insofar as the tax sales were concerned. It followed that in such a proceeding that court likewise had jurisdiction to cancel any other alleged outstanding interest claimed by the State in the same land, since equity delights to do complete justice and not by halves. Suit could be maintained against the State in its sovereign capacity for obtaining full relief, solely because of the right which was conferred in that behalf by Miss. Code. § 717 (1942), 1934 Miss. Laws ch. 196.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decree cancelling the tax deed and quieting title in the landowners.

 

643 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Interstate Oil Pipe Line Co. v. Stone


No. 36672


Supreme Court of Mississippi


203 Miss. 715; 35 So. 2d 73; 1948 Miss. LEXIS 316



April 26, 1948, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Suggestions of Error Overruled June 14, 1948, Reported at 203 Miss. 715 at 739.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the circuit court of Hinds county.

Hon. H. B. Gillespie, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and judgment accordingly.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant oil company sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Hinds County (Mississippi), which denied the oil company a refund of taxes paid to appellee, the chairman of the state tax commission. The taxes resulted from a privilege tax for operation of a pipe line system for the transportation of crude oil within the state, and from a use tax on the use of tangible personal property.


OVERVIEW: An oil company paid to the state tax commission a total of $ 25, 325.63, which was divided into a payment of privilege tax of $ 20,296.63, and a payment of use tax of $ 5,030.27. The oil company filed suit seeking a refund of the tax payments from the tax commission. The trial court denied the oil company's request for a refund. The court found that the trial court concluded correctly that the oil company was not entitled to a refund on the amounts paid for the privilege tax. The tax commission's levy of the tax was not an impermissible restraint on interstate commerce prohibited by the U.S. Constitution. The trial court erred in denying the oil company's request for a refund of the amount it paid towards the use tax. The tax should not have been imposed because the fact that certain materials used by the company were procurable through in state sales agents that would have ordered the materials from out of state did not make the materials "procurable in the ordinary channels of trade in the state." The court therefore reversed the trial court's decision in part and affirmed in part.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's denial of a refund on the amounts paid by the oil company for the use tax, but affirmed the amounts paid under the privilege tax.

 

644 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Owens v. Reese


No. 36734


Supreme Court of Mississippi


203 Miss. 322; 33 So. 2d 834; 1948 Miss. LEXIS 272



February 23, 1948, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the circuit court of Itawamba county.

Hon. Raymond T. Jarvis, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff filed an action for a writ of prohibition against defendants, sheriff, district attorney, and county prosecuting attorney, to prevent any of them from taking any additional steps under a proceeding for the condemnation and sale of plaintiff's automobile. The Circuit Court of Itawamba County (Mississippi) dismissed the petition after a demurrer thereto had been sustained and plaintiff had declined to amend. Plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: The sheriff alleged that plaintiff's automobile was seized while in the possession and under the control of plaintiff, and being used by him for the transportation of whiskey for the purpose of sale in violation of State laws. The court affirmed. It found that plaintiff failed to allege what he contended were the real facts as to the circumstances under which the automobile was seized. The court noted that the writ of prohibition would have prevented a court from proceeding with the disposition of the case, and also prevented the officers thereof from performing their official duties in the matter of presenting the case to such court for determination. The court determined that when this petition came on to be heard plaintiff had a full, adequate, and complete remedy afforded him of answering the affidavit of the sheriff as to the unlawful use of the automobile at the time the same was seized. The court concluded that, for aught that appeared from the petition, plaintiff could have obtained a full hearing on the merits so as to recover possession of the automobile, if entitled to such relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

645 of 825 DOCUMENTS


McGee v. State


No. 36411


Supreme Court of Mississippi


203 Miss. 592; 33 So. 2d 843; 1948 Miss. LEXIS 311



February 9, 1948, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the circuit court of Forrest county.

Hon. F. B. Collins, Judge.

See also 26 So. (2d) 680.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Forrest County (Mississippi), which convicted him of rape. Defendant argued that the circuit court from which the case was transferred improperly denied his motion to quash the indictment because the grand jury had no negros serving on it.


OVERVIEW: The crime was committed in another county and the indictment on which defendant was tried was returned by a grand jury of that county, but on a motion for a change of venue the case was transferred to where it was tried on its merits. Before the transfer of the case the circuit court overruled a motion to quash the indictment, the motion alleged that there were no negros on the grand jury which indicted defendant, thereby violating defendant's right to equal protection of the laws guaranteed to him by the Fourteenth Amendment. The evidence disclosed that no negroes were on the grand jury that indicted defendant and that no negroes had served on the grand and petit juries of the county for a long number of years although there were at all times in the county negroes, though few in number, who were qualified for jury service. The Board of Supervisors who prepared the jury lists testified that they did not exclude negroes, but put the names of persons on the list who were qualified for jury service without knowing whether they were members of the white or negro race. The court held that on the evidence it had to hold that the circuit court erred in not quashing defendant's indictment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded.

 

646 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Craig v. Mills


No. 36698


Supreme Court of Mississippi


203 Miss. 692; 33 So. 2d 801; 1948 Miss. LEXIS 315



January 26, 1948, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the chancery court of Hinds county.

Hon. V. J. Stricker, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a state tax collector, challenged a judgment by the Chancery Court of Hinds County (Mississippi) enjoining him from collecting or attempting to collect for any county outside a municipality, and for any municipality, the privilege taxes provided for in the second paragraph of § 143, Chap. 137, Laws 1944, known as the Local Privilege Tax. Appellees, the members of a partnership, had filed the suit.


OVERVIEW: The partnership operated portrait studios. The members challenged the legality of the Local Privilege Tax as an undue burden on interstate commerce, in violation of U.S. Const. art. I, § VIII, and alleged the amount of the tax was unreasonable and discriminatory. In addition to enjoining the collection of the Local Privilege Tax, the chancery court enjoined the collection of the privilege taxes provided for under § 150 of the Privilege Tax Code of 1944 for the levee district. The tax collector was also enjoined from causing the threatened arrest and prosecution of any of the partnership's employees. The court affirmed the overruling of the tax collector's demurrer because the complaint stated grounds for some relief against the excessive demands of the tax collector. The court held that the fact that the negatives of the photographs were sent out of the state to be finished did not make the transaction one of interstate commerce. The court reversed the judgment because the tax collector was entitled to collect a privilege tax for each of the partnership's photographers where the photographers were engaged in taking photographs in the state and developing them outside of the state.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the overruling of the tax collector's demurrer, reversed the judgment in so far as it prohibited the tax collector from collecting or attempting to collect any tax whatsoever from the members anywhere in the state except where they maintained their permanent studios, and remanded the matter.

 

647 of 825 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Corley v. Hines


No. 36575


Supreme Court of Mississippi


203 Miss. 60; 33 So. 2d 317; 1948 Miss. LEXIS 232



January 12, 1948, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the chancery court of Hinds county.

Hon. V. J. Stricker, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state officials appealed from the decree of the Chancery Court of Hinds County (Mississippi), which was entered in favor of complainant licensees in a suit challenging the validity of a certain regulation by the Mississippi State Plant Board that required the inclusion of certain language in the licensees' contracts with customers for termite extermination services.


OVERVIEW: The licensees were in the business of termite extermination, and they held a license for a certain patented process for termite treatment. The licensees used a customer contract provided by the patentee, whereby the licensees agreed to insulate buildings against termites, with a one-year warranty, but the board demanded that the contracts be modified to provide for eradication of termites, not mere insulation. The licensees protested that the regulation was unreasonable and arbitrary, and a decree was entered in their favor. In affirming on appeal, the court agreed that it was not within reason in the administration of this service to demand or expect complete eradication throughout in every undertaking, and the proof was overwhelming that it was a practical impossibility in all cases to eradicate termites on the first treatment. Only an honest, skillful, and diligent effort could be required, as an absolute undertaking in any professional service would be beyond the bounds of reason.


OUTCOME: The decree was affirmed.

 

648 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Richmond v. State


NO. 98-KA-00499-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


751 So. 2d 1038; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 387



December 16, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/17/1997. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT LEWIS GIBBS. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi), convicting him for motor vehicle theft and sentencing him as an habitual offender to a term of five years in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence for motor vehicle theft, arguing that the trial court erred by failing to quash the indictment, by failing to instruct the jury as to the lesser included charge of trespass, by failing to grant a directed verdict, that the theft statute was unconstitutionally void for vagueness and its failure to contain a requisite mens rea, and that he was denied effective assistance of counsel. The court found defendant was not prejudiced by the indictment. A lesser-included trespass instruction would have been improper, and the jury was properly instructed on the elements of motor vehicle theft. Since the theft statute defined motor vehicle theft as a forbidden act, the lack of a mens rea was not unconstitutional. Defendant failed to support either a directed verdict or establish ineffective assistance of counsel because he could not prove prejudice due to the overwhelming evidence of his guilt.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed because defendant was not prejudiced by the indictment, the jury instructions were proper, the theft statute was not unconstitutional, and defendant failed to establish either ineffective assistance of counsel or insufficient evidence to uphold his conviction.

 

649 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Gale v. Thomas


NO. 1998-CA-01234-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


759 So. 2d 1150; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 379



December 9, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 06/30/1998. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ERMEA JACKSON RUSSELL. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed the order of the Hinds County (Mississippi) Circuit Court, First Judicial District, granting defendants summary judgment on plaintiff's tort suit on sovereign immunity grounds.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff sued defendants, a police officer and the municipality that employed him, for gross and reckless negligence after an automobile accident with defendant officer. The trial court granted defendants summary judgment on sovereign immunity grounds, and plaintiff appealed. The state supreme court held that (a) defendant municipality was indeed protected by the immunity of the Mississippi Tort Claims Act, Miss. Code §11-46-1 et seq., for, although an interim version of § 11-46-3 was in effect at the time of the accident, the exception provided in § 11-46-3(3) was inapplicable because the operation and maintenance of a police department is not a function of proprietary nature; and (b) defendant officer was also protected by sovereign immunity, inasmuch as Miss. Code § 11-46-7(2) precluded holding defendant officer personally liable.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. Both defendants were protected by sovereign immunity.

Housing Auth. v. Lampley


NO. 97-IA-00629-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


749 So. 2d 134; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 365



November 24, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/18/97. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JAMES E. GRAVES, JR.



DISPOSITION: VACATED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant housing authority filed a petition for interlocutory appeal from the judgment of the Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which denied appellant's motion for summary judgment. The issue raised was whether proper notice was given under the Mississippi Tort Claims Act, Miss. Code Ann. §§ 11-46-1 to -23 (Supp. 1999).


OVERVIEW: The trial court denied appellant housing authority's motion for summary judgment. Appellant filed a petition for interlocutory appeal. The issue raised was whether proper notice was given under the Mississippi Tort Claims Act (MTCA), Miss. Code Ann. §§ 11-46-1 to -23 (Supp. 1999), where the notice was filed with the then Mayor of the City of Jackson as opposed to the chief executive officer of the governmental agency being sued. Because during the pendency of the appeal the court rendered a number of decisions concerning the notice requirement in the MTCA, it deemed it prudent to vacate the judgment below on the issue and remand the matter to the trial court so that the issue could be revisited in light of those intervening decisions.


OUTCOME: Judgment vacated and remanded. During the pendency of the appeal, the court rendered a number of decisions concerning the notice requirement in the Mississippi Tort Claims Act and vacated and remanded the judgment to the trial court so that the issue could be revisited in light of those intervening decisions.

 

651 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Coleman v. State


NO. 97-KA-01488-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


749 So. 2d 1003; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 357



November 18, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/22/1997. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT H. WALKER.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Harrison County Circuit Court (Mississippi) convicting him of one count of selling a controlled substance, cocaine, and adjudging him as a habitual offender.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for selling a controlled substance as a habitual offender, arguing that the trial court erred in excluding the testimony of defendant's alibi witness, and that he was denied effective assistance of counsel. The court found that defendant withheld alibi witness information from his attorney until a week before trial with no legitimate explanation. Since the risk of an intentional contempt violation would have been trivial to defendant compared to many years in prison on a habitual offender conviction, exclusion of the alibi testimony was justified. Defendant's counsel performed in a competent manner because he diligently tried to locate the surprise witness, and his delay in sending notice of the potential witness was not unreasonable. Counsel otherwise acted in defendant's best interests when objecting to the jury's seeing him in prison clothes before voir dire, and to law enforcement officers' testimony that they knew him through past interaction.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed because defendant's failure to timely inform the prosecution about an alibi witness was evidence of a willful ploy to gain a tactical advantage or of defendant's own contemptuous disdain for the adversarial system, and his ineffective assistance of counsel claim was without merit.

 

652 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Paracelsus Health Care Corp. v. Willard


NO. 97-CA-01494-SCT, CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 93-CA-00021-SCT, CONSOLIDATED WITH 92-CA-01274-SCT, CONSOLIDATED WITH 92-CA-00996-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


754 So. 2d 437; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 343; 15 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1172; 140 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P58,923



November 4, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied June 5, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 3836.


PRIOR HISTORY: DATE OF JUDGMENT: 6/30/97. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. GEORGE C. CARLSON, JR. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: TATE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.

Original Opinion of September 12, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Miss. LEXIS 496.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant corporation appealed from Tate County Circuit Court (Mississippi) jury award of punitive damages to plaintiff former employees in retaliatory discharge and tortious breach of contract action.


OVERVIEW: Defendant corporation appealed from jury award of punitive damages to plaintiff former employees in retaliatory discharge and tortious breach of contract action. On remand after initial award of compensatory damages, the trial court did not err by limiting second trial to issue of punitive damages. Where record clearly showed that reasonable trier of fact could find malice or gross disregard for plaintiffs' rights, the court did not err in submitting punitive damages instruction to jury on plaintiffs' claims. Jury's punitive damage award was not excessive, considering punishment and deterrent effect upon defendant and deterrent effect upon others, defendant's pecuniary ability and net worth, degree of reprehensibility of defendant's conduct, ratio between plaintiffs' compensatory and punitive damages, and difference between punitive damages and possible civil or criminal sanctions. The court properly instructed jury on preponderance of evidence burden of proof necessary to recover punitive damages for tort of retaliatory discharge. The trial court judgment affirmed.


OUTCOME: The trial court judgment affirmed. The court did not err in submitting punitive damages instruction to jury on plaintiffs' claims and, considering several factors, jury's punitive damage award was not excessive. The court properly instructed jury on preponderance of evidence burden of proof necessary to recover punitive damages for tort of retaliatory discharge.

 

653 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Old Canton Hills Homeowners Ass'n v. Mayor & Jackson


NO. 1998-CA-01514-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


749 So. 2d 54; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 332



October 21, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 07/20/1998. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ERMEA JACKSON RUSSELL. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant homeowners' association appealed a Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi) order affirming a decision of appellee city council to approve a conditional planned unit development zoning ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Appellant homeowners' association appealed an order affirming appellee city council's decision approving a conditional planned unit development zoning ordinance. The court affirmed, holding that the conditional zoning ordinance was not "contract zoning," an unconstitutional bargaining away of municipal power, because appellee was not obligated to approve rezoning. The conditions were typical of any planned unit development and were both legal and beneficial. The city council meeting transcript demonstrated that all parties had an opportunity to be heard and there was no evidence that the hearing was a sham. Appellee conducting its own hearing rather than proceeding solely on the record established before the planning board was within its procedural flexibility and did not violate the resident's due process rights. Finally, substantial evidence supported a finding of public need for the project. The appellee's zoning decision was not arbitrary or capricious or not fairly debatable.


OUTCOME: Order affirmed because appellee city council's zoning decision was not arbitrary or capricious or not fairly debatable, and served a public need. The conditional zoning ordinance was not an unconstitutional bargaining away of municipal power because appellee was under no obligation to approve the rezoning.

 

654 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Steen v. State


NO. 1999-CP-00053-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


748 So. 2d 156; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 314



October 7, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/12/1998. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ELZY JONATHAN SMITH, JR. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: COAHOMA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Coahoma County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which denied his motion for post-conviction relief and subsequently denied his motion to reconsider in capital rape case.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from a judgment denying his motion for post-conviction relief and subsequently his motion to reconsider in a capital rape case. Defendant asserted that the trial court was in error when it held that his motion for post-conviction relief was time barred. The court disagreed, holding that the trial court properly dismissed defendant's motion as time barred as it failed to meet an exception under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-5 (2)(Supp. 1999). Thus, the court also found that the trial court did not err in finding that defendant's motion, on its face, failed to show that he was entitled to any relief. The court also held that the trial court did not err in drawing a distinction between forcible rape and statutory rape, because the victim in this case was seven years old. Next, the court found that due to the status of the death penalty at the time of defendant's guilty plea, the trial court had no alternative but to sentence him to life imprisonment.


OUTCOME: Judgment denying post-conviction relief affirmed, because the trial court was correct in denying defendant's motion for post-conviction relief not only as time barred, but failing to qualify under one of the exceptions to a time bar.

Thomas Truck Lease, Inc. v. Lee County


NO. 95-CT-00745-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


768 So. 2d 870; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 306



September 30, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Stay of Mandate Granted March 20, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Miss. LEXIS 73.


PRIOR HISTORY: COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LEE COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 04/20/95. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. TIMOTHY E. ERVIN.

Original Opinion of October 27, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Miss. App. LEXIS 924.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged the judgment of the Lee County Chancery Court (Mississippi), which held that appellants owed ad valorem taxes to appellee.


OVERVIEW: Appellee county tax collector filed suit, claiming appellants owed ad valorem taxes. The chancery court found that appellants owed $ 246,078.78 in ad valorem taxes to Lee County. The court of appeals affirmed the judgment, agreeing with the chancery court's findings that the domicile of appellants' trucks in question was Lee County, based on the facts of the case and the contract between appellants. Further, there was insufficient proof that Mississippi had joined the International Registration Plan, or which of several plans was the actual plan in question. The Supreme Court of Mississippi granted certiorari to consider the constitutional implications of the taxes levied in the case. The affirming court found the taxes were constitutional, and held that the case was strictly one of Mississippi statutory application and did not in any way encroach upon the rights guaranteed by the Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. County's ad valorem taxes not unconstitutional, and did not encroach upon appellants' rights guaranteed by the Commerce Clause.

 

656 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Miller v. State


NO. 96-CT-01085-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


748 So. 2d 100; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 291



September 23, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Miller v. Waller, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 41601 (S.D. Miss., Jan. 31, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/04/96. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. KATHY KING JACKSON. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: GREENE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.

Original Opinion of December 30, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Miss. App. LEXIS 1100.
Miller v. State, 1998 Miss. App. LEXIS 1100 (Miss. Ct. App., Dec. 30, 1998)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant petitioned for writ of certiorari regarding appellant's conviction of capital murder of an infant that was affirmed by the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Mississippi).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of capital murder of an infant and received a sentence of life imprisonment without parole. After the conviction was affirmed, appellant petitioned for writ of certiorari. The court affirmed the convictions. The trial court did not err in declining to grant a mistrial regarding the State's repeated attempt to ask an improper question to a witness. Other witnesses, properly qualified as experts, subsequently answered the question the witness was not allowed to answer. The capital murder statute, Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-19(2)(f), and the felonious child abuse statute, Miss. Code. Ann. § 97-5-39(2) were held to be constitutional.


OUTCOME: Judgment of conviction affirmed, because trial court did not err in declining to grant a mistrial and the relevant statutes were constitutional.

 

657 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Pickens v. Donaldson


NO. 98-CA-00757-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


748 So. 2d 684; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 292



September 23, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 01/07/1998. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. W. SWAN YERGER. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed an order of the Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi) granting summary judgment to defendants under the Mississippi Tort Claims Act, Miss. Code Ann. §§ 11-46-1 et seq., in a case of medical malpractice.


OVERVIEW: The lower court dismissed appellant's medical malpractice claims against three physicians who treated plaintiff's minor child in a state university hospital. The lower court held that plaintiff's claims were barred by Mississippi Tort Claims Act, Miss. Code Ann. §§ 11-46-1 et seq. (MTCA). The court found that there was evidence that the state did not solely compensate staff physicians at the university hospital. The lower court correctly dismissed the claim against the physician who was obviously not a staff physician and for whom the one-year statute of limitations under the MTCA barred the claim. The court held that the other two physicians may have been independent contractors for whom the general negligence statute of limitations may have applied. The court could not consider plaintiff's constitutionality claim against the MTCA because she failed to raise the claim at the trial level and did not notify the Attorney General's office.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed summary judgment against the physician who was obviously an employee compensated solely by the state because the statute of limitations under the Mississippi Tort Claims Act barred the action. The court reversed summary judgment against the two physicians whose independent contractor status was unclear.

Bell v. State


NO. 96-CP-01082-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


759 So. 2d 1111; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 230



July 29, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion For Rehearing Filed: 04/23/99. As Amended July 30, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: DATE OF JUDGMENT: 9/17/96. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. BARRY W. FORD. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LEE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.

This Opinion Substituted on Grant of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of March 18, 1999. Previously Reported at: 1999 Miss. LEXIS 107.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal appellant challenged judgment of the Lee County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which denied appellant's post-conviction claim seeking a reduction or modification of his sentence of two 10-year prison terms as a result of his armed robbery convictions.


OVERVIEW: As a result of his guilty plea to two counts of armed robbery, criminal appellant was sentenced to two 10-year prison terms that the trial court ordered to run concurrently with any sentence appellant received from a federal court. More than three years after entry of his guilty plea, appellant was notified that his federal sentence would not begin until after he had served his state sentences. Appellant sought a post-conviction modification of his state sentences; however, appellee argued that his challenge was time barred. The court held appellant was entitled to an evidentiary hearing to determine whether the notice that his federal sentence would run consecutively to his state sentence constituted new evidence that fell within the exception to the state's three-year statute of limitations on sentencing challenges. The court also noted that the trial court had discretionary authority to order the state sentences to run concurrently with the federal sentence, and as such, the trial court's language to that effect was not surplusage, as appellee contended.


OUTCOME: The judgment denying criminal appellant's motion for modification of his state sentences for armed robbery was reversed and remanded for a determination of whether appellant's motion was excepted from the state's statute of limitations on sentencing challenges.

 

659 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Attorney General v. B.C.M.


NO. 1998-CA-00994-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


744 So. 2d 299; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 232



July 29, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/22/1998. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. MICHAEL H. WARD. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY FAMILY COURT.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state government challenged an order of the Harrison County Family Court (Mississippi) invalidating Miss. Code Ann. § 41-21-77 on the grounds that it violated Miss. Const. art. IV, § 86, which required the Legislature to care for the insane, by conditioning court-ordered mental treatment on a determination by the admitting institution's director that facilities were available for treatment and care.


OVERVIEW: Appellant state government challenged an order holding that Miss. Code Ann. § 41-21-77 was unconstitutional because it conditioned admission of a patient for court-ordered mental treatment on a determination by the admitting institution's director that facilities were available. After the director of a state hospital refused to admit a "delinquent" minor for lack of space, a family court judge held the statute violated Miss. Const. art. IV, § 86, because it failed to provide care for all persons ordered committed. The court had ordered minor committed for treatment after he contaminated his stepfather's insulin, and an evaluation determined he was a danger to himself and others. Appellant argued the court acted ultra vires in ordering the state institution to accept the minor without regard to whether space was available. The court agreed and reversed the order, holding that the statute was not necessarily in "palpable conflict" with the state constitution, since it required the director of the admitting facility to assume responsibility for treatment and care for mentally ill minors even if they were not immediately admitted to the facility as soon as they were committed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed order on the grounds that, while the lower court was properly concerned about the denial of care and treatment to mentally ill minors, it erred in ruling statute unconstitutional where the statute provided that the assigned institution took control of the individual at the time commitment was ordered, even if there was no space available for him or her at the assigned facility.

Sentinel Indus. Contr. Corp. v. Kimmins Indus. Serv. Corp.


NO. 97-CA-00323-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


743 So. 2d 954; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 235



July 29, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/12/1996. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. BILL JONES. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JACKSON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: DIRECT APPEAL - AFFIRMED; CROSS-APPEAL - AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant general contractor and defendant surety appealed from the Jackson County Circuit Court (Mississippi), in which the jury awarded damages in favor of plaintiff subcontractor. Plaintiff cross-appealed from the judgment notwithstanding the verdict granted to defendant chemical company, challenging the denial of prejudgment interest and attorneys' fees, and the refusal of its bad faith claim instructions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant general contractor and defendant surety appealed from the award of damages in favor of plaintiff subcontractor. Plaintiff cross-appealed from the judgment notwithstanding the verdict granted to defendant chemical company, challenging the denial of prejudgment interest and attorneys' fees, and the refusal of its bad faith claim instructions. The court found that defendant general contractor was estopped from asserting that plaintiff could not receive compensation for extra work due to a lack of change orders. Plaintiff was entitled to the jury award in its favor, based upon defendant general contractor's persistent pattern of conduct in requiring plaintiff to perform work outside the scope of the contract, and defendant's failure to act in good faith when defendant contractor refused to issue change orders. Plaintiff presented adequate evidence of its damages. The trial judge was correct in granting defendant chemical company's motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict, because plaintiff's damages were caused by the breach of contract by defendant general contractor, and defendant chemical company did not cause that breach without justification.


OUTCOME: Denial of prejudgment interest was reversed and remanded for a determination and award in favor of plaintiff subcontractor. All other issues were affirmed. Plaintiff had no cause of action against defendant chemical company, its sole remedy being against defendant surety. Denial of plaintiff's requested instruction on punitive damages was proper, because there was a legitimate dispute regarding the amount owed by defendant surety.

Leuer v. City of Flowood


NO. 98-KA-00062-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


744 So. 2d 266; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 216



June 24, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/01/1997. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT LOUIS GOZA, JR. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: RANKIN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the Rankin County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which affirmed his conviction by a lower court for driving under the influence of intoxicating liquor under Miss. Code Ann. § 63-11-30 (1)(a) (1995) and which affirmed his conviction for careless driving in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 63-3-1213 (1996).


OVERVIEW: After being observed by a police officer, appellant was stopped and pulled over under the officer's suspicions that appellant was driving while intoxicated. According to the officer, appellant refused the intoxilyzer. Appellant was subsequently charged with driving under the influence of intoxicating liquor pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 63-11-30 (1)(a) (1995) and also charged with careless driving in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 63-3-1213 (1996). The trial court entered judgment convicting appellant as charged, and the circuit court affirmed. On appeal, appellant alleged that the statutes were facially void for vagueness and thus in violation of the due process clauses of U.S. Const. amends. V and XIV, and of Miss. Const. art. 3 and 14 (1890). The state supreme court affirmed the rulings of the lower court, finding that § 63-11-30(1)(a) was not void for vagueness and that it sufficiently provided fair notice of the proscribed conduct. The court held that the average person was put on notice that drinking intoxicating liquors and subsequently driving a motor vehicle was prohibited. The court also held that § 63-3-1213 (1996) withstood constitutional scrutiny.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the circuit court affirming the lower court's convictions of appellant for driving while intoxicated and careless driving were affirmed. The court found that the applicable statutes were not unconstitutionally vague because they provided drivers with adequate notice of the conduct for which they were subject to be penalized.

State v. Blenden


NO. 96-KA-01339-SCT CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 97-KA-00073-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


748 So. 2d 77; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 219



June 24, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/28/96. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JOHN H. WHITFIELD. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of the judgment of the Harrison County Circuit Court (Mississippi), imposing sanctions on them for discovery violations, which resulted in a mistrial and appellee's retrial on charges of felony driving under the influence. Appellee sought review of his subsequent conviction for felony driving under the influence.


OVERVIEW: Appellee was convicted at his retrial on charges of felony driving under the influence. Evidence from the state crime lab was used to prosecute appellee, and the trial court imposed sanctions on appellant state and county after determining that the lab and the county district attorney committed discovery violations. On appeal, the court affirmed the sanctions and appellee's conviction. The court determined that the trial court did not err in determining that appellants had committed discovery violations because there was sufficient evidence that they had failed to disclose certain information regarding tests on appellee's blood and had failed to list a lab technician on their witness list. The court also held that the trial court had the authority to impose sanctions on appellants for their discovery violations and concluded that the imposition of the sanctions did not violate the separation of powers doctrine. Finally, the court determined the trial court did not err in failing to dismiss appellee's case on double jeopardy grounds because appellee had not shown that the error which led to his retrial was made by appellants with the intent to force appellee to move for a mistrial.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's imposition of sanctions on appellants, holding that the record was sufficient to support the determination that appellants had committed discovery violations and that the imposition of sanctions did not violate the separation of powers doctrine. The appellate court affirmed appellee's felony driving under the influence conviction, holding that his retrial did not subject him to double jeopardy.

Wiley v. State


NO. 98-DR-00588-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


750 So. 2d 1193; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 191



June 3, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Counsel Corrected June 4, 1999. Certiorari Denied June 29, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 4536.


PRIOR HISTORY: COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: DESOTO COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/03/95. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ANDREW C. BAKER.



DISPOSITION: APPLICATION FOR LEAVE TO FILE MOTION TO VACATE DEATH SENTENCE DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed an application for leave to file a motion to vacate his death sentence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of murder and was sentenced to death. He filed an application for leave to file a motion to vacate his death sentence, and the court denied the motion, concluding the issues raised in it were without merit. The court also rejected appellant's contention that he was denied effective assistance of counsel at his sentencing and at the appeal of his sentencing trial. The court concluded that some of the issues raised by appellant were addressed on direct appeal and were therefore res judicata, that appellant was not entitled to a mercy instruction, and that his counsel was not ineffective for failing to appeal the jury's consideration as an aggravating factor the possibility that appellant had committed murder to avoid arrest. Moreover, defendant had failed to prove prejudice from the alleged ineffectiveness of his counsel. The court rejected appellant's contention that he was denied a fair trial, concluding the issues raised by appellant were procedurally barred because they were capable of determination at trial or on direct appeal, and the court further determined that there was no cumulation of error in the case that required reversal of his sentence.


OUTCOME: The court denied appellant's application for leave to file a motion to vacate his death sentence, concluding that appellant had not been denied effective assistance of counsel at his sentencing or at the appeal of his sentencing trial, that he had not been denied a fair trial, and that there was no cumulation of error in the case which required reversal.

McGilberry v. State


NO. 97-DP-00213-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


741 So. 2d 894; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 196



June 3, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by McGilberry v. Mississippi, 529 U.S. 1006, 146 L. Ed. 2d 222, 120 S. Ct. 1273, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 1788 (2000)
Post-conviction relief denied at McGilberry v. State, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 93 (Miss., Mar. 6, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JACKSON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/12/1996. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JAMES W. BACKSTROM.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeal from judgment of the Jackson County Circuit Court (Mississippi), in favor of plaintiff, convicting defendant of four counts of capital murder, and imposing the death sentence, after defendant was found guilty of bludgeoning to death four members of his family.


OVERVIEW: A jury found the 16-year-old defendant guilty of four counts of capital murder, and imposed a sentence of death on all four counts. A total of 19 issues were raised for review on appeal. The Supreme Court held that there was nothing in the record suggesting that defendant's rights were violated or that he was deprived of a fair trial. Defendant stood convicted of brutally murdering his mother, his stepfather, his sister, and his three-year-old step-nephew. The method used, bludgeoning with a baseball bat, was both gruesome and grisly. The evidence showed that the crimes were premeditated and contemplated over a period of at least two weeks. Defendant bludgeoned his family so that he could steal a car, some cash, a money order, and a credit card and then run away from home. The jury decided defendant's fate, and the court found no reason to disturb the verdict or sentence.


OUTCOME: The verdict finding the 16-year-old defendant guilty of four counts of capital murder was affirmed, because nothing in the record suggested that his rights had been violated or that he was deprived of a fair trial, and sentenced to death for bludgeoning to death four members of his family.

Jackson ex rel. Heirs of Jackson v. Daley


NO. 96-CA-00642-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


739 So. 2d 1031; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 186



June 3, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion For Rehearing Filed: 12/17/1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/01/1996. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. R. I. PRICHARD, III. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JEFFERSON DAVIS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.

This Opinion Substituted on Grant of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of November 19, 1998, Previously Reported at: 1998 Miss. LEXIS 569.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the Jefferson Davis County Circuit Court (Mississippi), that entered judgment, upon a jury verdict, in appellee's favor in appellant's wrongful death action. Cross-appellant sought review of an order finding that appellee's insurance policy with cross-appellant provided coverage.


OVERVIEW: Appellant individual's son was killed in a single vehicle accident on a road maintained by appellee county. Appellant brought a wrongful death action against multiple defendants, including appellee county. At trial, there was evidence introduced that employees of appellee had left dirt piles that edged into the road. Evidence was also presented that appellant's son had a blood alcohol level in excess of the legal limit. Appellant successfully joined cross-appellant insurer as a defendant to determine the extent of coverage provided to appellee. Before trial, all defendants but cross-appellant and appellee were dismissed on summary judgment. The trial court also denied appellant's motion to join cross-appellant as a real party because appellee was still in the suit based solely on the policy from cross-appellant. During closing, appellee's counsel implied that his client was not insured. Appellant's objection was overruled. The jury rendered a verdict for appellee. Appellant sought review. On rehearing, the court reversed and remanded for a new trial because the reference to appellee's insurance coverage, or lack thereof, was improper and merited reversal.


OUTCOME: On rehearing, the court reversed the trial court's judgment in appellee's favor and remanded for a new trial because it was error to overrule appellant's objection to defense counsel's statement during closing argument regarding appellee's insurance coverage. The court affirmed appellee was insured by cross-appellant and that appellee's sovereign immunity was waived to that extent because the accident was related to use of the insured truck.

Marcum v. Hancock County Sch. Dist.


NO. 97-CA-00916-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


741 So. 2d 234; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 189



June 3, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Counsel Corrected June 8, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HANCOCK COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 07/11/97. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. KOSTA N. VLAHOS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a minor and her guardians, sought review of a decision of the Hancock County Circuit Court (Mississippi) which granted appellee school district's motion to dismiss appellants' negligence action pursuant to Miss. R. Civ. P. 12(b)(6) on the basis it was time barred by the Mississippi Tort Claims Act, Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-11 (Supp. 1998) (amended by H.B. 778, 1999 Miss. Laws Ch. 469).


OVERVIEW: Appellant minor was injured in a school bus accident when the driver allegedly slammed on her brakes without warning. Appellants, the minor and her guardians, brought a negligence action against appellee school district seeking to recover damages for the injuries. Appellee filed a motion to dismiss pursuant to Miss. R. Civ. P. 12(b)(6) based upon the contention that the suit was barred by the one year statute of limitations contained in the Mississippi Tort Claims Act (MTCA) found in Miss. Code. Ann. §§ 11-46-1 to -23 (Supp. 1998). The lower court granted appellee's motion and dismissed appellants' action. Appellants contended the statute of limitations was tolled due to appellant minor's disability of infancy as prescribed by the minor savings clause of Miss. Code Ann. § 15-1-59 (1995). The state supreme court affirmed, reasoning appellants' claim was without merit as the lower court's dismissal of appellants' claim due to the expiration of the one year statute of limitations was proper because the minor savings clause of § 15-1-59 only applied to actions within that chapter and not to the MTCA.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the lower court dismissing the action of appellants, a minor and her guardians, was affirmed because the statute of limitations contained in the state tort claims law had expired and because a minor savings clause of another law did not apply.

Hester v. State


NO. 96-CA-00532-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


741 So. 2d 229; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 177



May 13, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/23/96. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. GRAY EVANS. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: SUNFLOWER COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.

This Opinion Substituted on Denial of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of November 6, 1997, Previously Reported at: 1997 Miss. LEXIS 615.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Sunflower County Circuit Court (Mississippi), denying defendant's motion to show cause after the parole board held a formal revocation hearing, revoking defendant's parole for an additional 18 months for failing to report, and contending that trial court erred in failing to conduct an evidentiary hearing regarding defendant's contention that his parole was wrongfully revoked.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted and imprisoned in Mississippi, but he was on parole in Missouri. Defendant was granted a travel permit for a specified period, he failed to report as directed in Mississippi, and he did not return to Missouri or contact his parole officer upon expiration of permit. The parole board found there was sufficient reasonable cause to hold a formal revocation hearing. Defendant was arrested in Georgia several years later, he signed a waiver of extradition, and was returned to Mississippi. Defendant's parole was revoked for an additional 18 months. The trial court denied defendant's motion to show cause. Defendant appealed, contending he was being unlawfully held, that he was subjected to an inept parole board, and that the trial court erred in failing to conduct a hearing regarding defendant's contention that his parole was wrongfully revoked. The appeals court affirmed trial court's refusal to conduct hearing because defendant's appeal was without merit. This was because defendant failed to support his assertions with evidence contained in the record, and, on appeal, it was his burden to show reversible error in the record, and he failed to do so.


OUTCOME: The trial court's refusal to conduct an evidentiary hearing regarding defendant's assorted claims of error, including that his parole was wrongfully revoked, was affirmed because defendant had the burden of showing that there was reversible error in the record, and he failed to do so. He failed to support his assertions with evidence contained in the record; thus, his contentions were meritless.

Miller v. State


NO. 97-KA-01221-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


740 So. 2d 858; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 173



May 6, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 07/02/1997. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. MICHAEL RAY EUBANKS. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LAMAR COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for murder in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-19(1)(a) (1972), from the Canton County Circuit Court (Mississippi), where the case was transferred due to publicity. Defendant alleged the trial court made reversible error by failing to suppress statements and a note made by defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-19(1)(a) (1972), and he appealed the conviction. The court affirmed the judgment, making several findings. The amended indictment affected the form and not the substance of the indictment and did not affect defendant's ability to present a defense. The trial court's refusal to give an instruction on deliberate design was affirmed because the jury was properly instructed, and the evidence did not support a manslaughter charge. The trial court properly admitted the victim's photographs because it was probative on how the shooting occurred. Defendant failed to prove that the Mississippi Youth Court Act, Miss. Code Ann. § 43-21-151(1)(a), (b) (1998), violated his rights to due process and equal protection under the United States and Mississippi Constitutions. No evidence supported defendant's claims. Defendant's statements and his note were properly admitted into evidence and his voluntary statements did not trigger Miranda. The note was written prior to defendant's arrest and was voluntary. The court rejected the argument that defendant could not waive his rights because he was a minor.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for murder was affirmed. Defendant failed to prove that the Mississippi Youth Court Act violated his rights to due process and equal protection under the United States and Mississippi Constitutions. The state did not arbitrarily separate juveniles into two classes. Defendant's statements and the note were properly admitted into evidence because they were voluntary admissions before defendant received his Miranda rights.

LINCOLN COUNTY SCH. DIST. v. DOE


NO. 96-IA-01165-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


749 So. 2d 943; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 164



April 29, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected May 3, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/02/96. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. L. BRELAND HILBURN, JR.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a school district and a principal, filed an interlocutory appeal from a judgment of the Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which denied defendants' motion for summary judgment in a suit involving the alleged rape of plaintiff's school-aged daughter.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff argued that defendant school district and principal were liable for the rape of her daughter on school property, by failing to provide adequate security and failing to warn students of the perpetrator's violent propensities. The court disagreed, ruling that the trial court erred in denying defendants' motion for summary judgment. The court explained that plaintiff lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of the retroactive provision of the Mississippi Tort Claims Act (Act), Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-3, because the provision was inapplicable to her, the cause of action having accrued after the Act's effective date. Under terms of the Act, the court observed, the defendants were granted immunity from suit, unless they maintained liability insurance that covered the tortious act; liability could be assessed only to the extent of insurance carried. Because defendant school district's insurance policy only covered bodily injuries, and expressly excluded molestation, the court ruled that defendants were immune. The court noted that the emotional injuries of which plaintiff complained were not the type of physical injuries contemplated by the policy.


OUTCOME: Judgment denying summary judgment motion of defendant school district and principal reversed, because defendants immune from suit for alleged rape of plaintiff's daughter on school grounds, as Mississippi Tort Claims Act barred action when defendants did not maintain liability insurance covering molestation or emotional injuries plaintiff complained of.

Greyhound Welfare Found. v. Mississippi State Univ.


NO. 98-CA-00711-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


736 So. 2d 1048; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 155



April 22, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: OKTIBBEHA COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 06/09/1997. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT L. LANCASTER.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, several greyhound welfare organizations, challenged an order from the Oktibbeha County Chancery Court (Mississippi), which dismissed appellants' replevin action. The lower court ruled that the action was barred by the Mississippi Tort Claims Act, Miss. Code Ann. §§ 11-46-1 to 23 (1998), because appellees, a university and a dean, were entitled to sovereign immunity.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed the lower court's order dismissing appellants', several greyhound welfare organizations, replevin action against appellees, a university and a dean. The lower court held that the action should have been dismissed because appellees were entitled to sovereign immunity. The court held that appellants' suit was not barred by the Mississippi Tort Claims Act, Miss. Code Ann. §§ 11-46-1 to 23 (1998), because the action was in replevin and not in tort, as it did not seek money damages. Rather, appellants' suit sought the return of property that was allegedly wrongfully held by appellees. The court remanded appellants' action for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The lower court's order dismissing appellants' replevin action was reversed and remanded because the Mississippi Tort Claims Act only applied to tort actions seeking money damages. The court noted that the replevin action sought the return of allegedly wrongfully held property.

Veasley v. State


NO. 95-CT-00367-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


735 So. 2d 432; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 159



April 22, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: COAHOMA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 01/20/95. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JOHN LESLIE HATCHER.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Mississippi), which reversed respondent's conviction of five counts of rape because the trial court erred in admitting the hearsay statements of the complainant under Miss. R. Evid. 803(25) without first holding an evidentiary hearing to determine if the complainant was a "child of tender years."


OVERVIEW: The state appealed the reversal of respondent's conviction of five counts of rape. Holding that a child under age 12 was rebuttably presumed to be of tender years, but that the trial court must make a case-by-case determination as to whether an older child was of tender years, the court affirmed and remanded the judgment. With respect to the 13-year-old complainant, the court noted that the trial court did not think that she was of tender years, but admitted the hearsay on the basis of the comment to Miss. R. Evid. 803(25) to the effect that generally, a child under 14 was considered of tender years. The court held that in determining whether to admit statements pursuant to Rule 803(25) the trial court must make a determination on record and based on factual finding as to the victim's mental and emotional age, as to whether victim is of tender years. The court held that if the trial court finds that declarant is of tender years, then it must still rule on the Miss R. Evid. 803(25)(a), (b), factors before admitting the testimony. The court could not conclude that it was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt, because without the hearsay, it was complainant's word against respondent's.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment for respondent and remanded for a new trial, because the trial court erred in admitting the hearsay statements of the 13-year-old complainant without first holding an evidentiary hearing to determine whether she was of tender years. Because the statements admitted were strong evidence of guilt, the court concluded that the error was not harmless beyond a reasonable doubt.

 

672 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Maddox v. Muirhead


NO. 97-CA-01152-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


738 So. 2d 742; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 141



April 8, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Baker, Donelson, Bearman & Caldwell, P.C. v. Muirhead, 920 So. 2d 440, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 59 (Miss., 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/05/97. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JAMES E. GRAVES, JR. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.

This Opinion Substituted by the Court for Withdrawn Opinion of January 14, 1999, Previously Reported at: 1999 Miss. LEXIS 9.
Maddox v. Muirhead, 1999 Miss. LEXIS 9 (Miss., Jan. 14, 1999)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, patron and bar owner, filed notices of acceptance of an additur and motions seeking clarification and correction of the opinion after plaintiff appealed a judgment from the Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which denied his motion for additur or in the alternative a new trial as to damages only in a personal injury action.


OVERVIEW: The court granted the motions of defendants, a patron and bar owner, seeking clarification and correction of the opinion after bringing notices of acceptance of the additur from plaintiff's appeal of a judgment denying his motion for additur, or in the alternative a new trial as to damages only, in a personal injury action. The court found it was reasonable to conclude that the jury did not credit plaintiff's testimony concerning lost wages and overtime. The court noted that the verdict of the jury, before reduction for plaintiff's percentage of fault, compensated him for his medical bills and left a small amount, apparently for past pain and suffering. The court found the jury award failed to compensate plaintiff for medical bills that were uncontested by either defendant. The court concluded that the trial court abused its discretion in refusing to grant an additur. The court held that the jury award was so inadequate as to shock the conscience and was against the overwhelming weight of the evidence. The decision was affirmed after defendants accepted the additur within 15 days of the date of the decision.


OUTCOME: Motion of defendants, a patron and bar owner, seeking clarification and correction of the opinion after bringing notices of acceptance of the additur from plaintiff's appeal of a judgment denying his motion for additur in a personal injury action, was granted. The opinion was corrected and then affirmed after defendants accepted the additur, where an abuse of discretion had occurred in the trial court's refusal to grant the additur.

Hughes v. State


NO. 97-DP-00028-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


735 So. 2d 238; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 131



March 31, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied January 10, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 242.
Writ of certiorari denied Hughes v. Mississippi, 528 U.S. 1083, 120 S. Ct. 807, 145 L. Ed. 2d 680, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 242 (2000)
Reconsideration denied by Hughes v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 556 (Miss., May 20, 2004)
Application denied by, Post-conviction proceeding at Hughes v. State, 892 So. 2d 203, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 1355 (Miss., 2004)
Writ of habeas corpus granted, Writ of habeas corpus denied, Motion dismissed by, As moot, Certificate of appealability denied, Judgment entered by Hughes v. Epps, 694 F. Supp. 2d 533, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 18825 (N.D. Miss., 2010)
Motion granted by, in part Hughes v. State, 2011 Miss. LEXIS 50 (Miss., Jan. 20, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/20/96. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. GEORGE C. CARLSON, JR. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: TATE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Tate County Circuit Court (Mississippi) convicting him of rape and murder in the course of a kidnapping and imposing the penalty of death, alleging numerous procedural, evidentiary, and constitutional errors.


OVERVIEW: Defendant kidnapped a 16-year-old girl and brutally beat and raped her before killing her. He was convicted of rape and murder in the course of kidnapping and was sentenced to death. He appealed his conviction, alleging numerous procedural, evidentiary, and constitutional errors. In affirming, the state supreme court concluded that defendant received a fair, albeit imperfect, trial. None of the errors advanced by defendant amounted to more than harmless error, although it was error to permit the use of local census data to supplement frequency statistics offered by DNA experts and to allow a lay person to comment on the similarity between knives found in defendant's home and the murder weapon. Further, the imposition of the death penalty was proportionate when compared to other capital murder cases. Defendant's victim was beaten, raped, stabbed, and strangled. Her body was then set on fire, and the degradation culminated when defendant dumped her body in an abandoned house and left it to rot. Based upon these facts, the court concluded that the punishment fit the crime.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed where, although errors were committed, none amounted to more than harmless error. Further, the death sentence was proportionate when compared to other murder cases wherein the death penalty was imposed, and based upon the brutal facts of the case, the court concluded that the punishment fit the crime.

City of Gulfport v. Orange Grove Utils., Inc.


NO. 97-CA-00867-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


735 So. 2d 1041; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 127



March 31, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion For Rehearing Filed: 1/14/99.


PRIOR HISTORY: DATE OF JUDGMENT: 06/24/97. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. MICHAEL L. CARR, JR. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY SPECIAL COURT OF EMINENT DOMAIN.

This Opinion Substituted on Grant of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of December 31, 1998, Previously Reported at: 1998 Miss. LEXIS 625.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city appealed a judgment from the Harrison County Chancery Court (Mississippi), which dismissed eminent domain proceedings in which plaintiff sought to condemn the water and sewage facilities of defendant utility company.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff city filed an eminent domain action to condemn the water and sewage facilities of defendant utility company as well as defendant's certificates of public convenience and necessity. The trial court granted defendant's motion to dismiss. The appellate court reversed the judgment in part, affirmed the judgment in part, and remanded. The trial court erred in ruling that plaintiff was required to first cancel defendant's certificates before seeking to take by eminent domain certified areas within plaintiff's corporate limits. According to the plain meaning of Miss. Code Ann. § 77-3-21, water and sewer utilities were excluded from the eminent domain cancellation requirement. There was no error, however, in the trial court's finding that plaintiff was without standing to bring a condemnation action for the area located outside its corporate limits. The court remanded the action because the trial court erred in allowing defendant to introduce testimony and evidence outside the pleadings in a motion to dismiss or, in the alternative, failing to give notice to plaintiff of the decision to treat the motion as one for summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed in part, affirmed in part, and remanded a judgment that dismissed eminent domain proceedings in which plaintiff city sought to condemn water and sewage facilities of defendant utility. The trial court erred in the decision that the utilities were subject to statutory cancellation requirements, but did not err in finding that plaintiff was without standing to bring a condemnation action for an area located outside city limits.

 

675 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Sneed v. Ford Motor Co.


NO. 97-CA-00914-SCT, CONSOLIDATED WITH, NO. 97-CA-00922-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


735 So. 2d 306; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 132



March 31, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 07/03/97. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JERRY OWEN TERRY SR. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, individuals and insurance companies, filed interlocutory appeals from the Harrison County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which granted defendant automobile manufacturer's motion to substitute real party in interest and sua sponte ordered plaintiffs and their attorneys to file statutory champerty affidavits. Plaintiffs moved for reconsideration, which was denied, and plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, injured parties and their insurers, filed interlocutory appeals from the trial court's refusal to grant reconsideration of its decision to require plaintiffs to file statutory champerty affidavits. The reviewing court determined that the insurers had a real and legitimate interest in the individual plaintiffs' claims against defendant car manufacturer. The court characterized the agreement as an attempt by the insurers to see that payment for a loss occasioned by joint tortfeasors was distributed among the tortfeasors. Recognizing the long established policy of encouraging settlements, even partial settlements, the court declared that agreements with potential defendants who had a legitimate interest in the allocation of responsibility should not be declared champertous. The court held that where the settling parties both already had a vital interest to protect, the champerty statutes, including those requiring affidavits, did not have proper application. Plaintiffs did not bring their action due to inducement by or assistance from the insurers, and the settlement agreement at issue was not a champertous contract but was a valid assignment of a chose in action.


OUTCOME: The judgment that ordered plaintiffs and their attorneys to file champerty affidavits was reversed and remanded. The settlement agreement at issue was not a champertous contract and was a valid assignment of a chose in action. Plaintiffs, the insurers, and their attorneys were not required to execute the statutory champerty affidavits.

Manning v. State


NO. 96-DP-00943-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


735 So. 2d 323; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 130



March 31, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at Manning v. State, 765 So. 2d 516, 2000 Miss. LEXIS 161 (Miss., 2000)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 07/30/1996. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JOHN M. MONTGOMERY. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: OKTIBBEHA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.
Manning v. State, 726 So. 2d 1152, 1998 Miss. LEXIS 306 (Miss., 1998)



DISPOSITION: REMANDED FOR BATSON HEARING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Oktibbeha County Circuit Court (Mississippi) finding defendant guilty of two counts of murder and imposing the death penalty. Defendant argued that the judgment should be reversed because of several issues, including a claim that the state intentionally excluded African-American jurors from the jury pool.


OVERVIEW: The court remanded defendant's conviction on two counts of capital murder. Defendant put forth several arguments on appeal, challenging the weight of the evidence, the jury venire, ineffective assistance of counsel, the jury instructions, and several other issues that defendant argued warranted reversal. In particular, defendant argued that the state improperly used peremptory challenges to strike African-American jurors. The court found that when such a challenge was made, the state must show a race-neutral reason for striking the jurors and then the court was required to determine whether defendant had proven discrimination. The court held that defendant failed to prove that discrimination had taken place because the trial court determined that the struck jurors were struck for valid non-race reasons. Nevertheless, the court remanded the case for a hearing on the second venire because the trial court failed to make a determination of whether the jurors in the second venire were properly struck. Therefore, the court remanded the case for a hearing on the exclusion of jurors with instructions to order a new trial if discrimination were found.


OUTCOME: A judgment finding defendant guilty of two counts of murder and imposing a death sentence was remanded for a hearing to determine whether African-American jurors were excluded because of race, as alleged by defendant. The court held that if discrimination were found, a new trial would be necessary.

Lemon v. Mississippi Transp. Comm'n


NO. 97-IA-01480-SCT, CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 97-IA-01481-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


735 So. 2d 1013; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 117



March 25, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JACKSON COUNTY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/20/1997. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. T. LARRY WILSON.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of two decisions of the Jackson County Court (Mississippi), which, pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. §§ 65-1-301 through -347, signed orders granting appellee Mississippi Transportation Commission immediate right and title to appellant's properties and certified the question of the statute's constitutionality for interlocutory appeal.


OVERVIEW: Miss. Code Ann. §§ 65-1-3-1 to -347 permitted appellee Mississippi Transportation Commission to judicially take title to private property before the landowner had the opportunity for a hearing. Appellee asserted that service to the general public necessitated that private property be acquired quickly in order to prevent delays in highway projects and that meaningful means existed to assess the propriety of the taking after title had vested in appellee. Where the state feasibly could provide a pre-deprivation hearing, it generally had to do so regardless of the adequacy of a post-deprivation remedy. Therefore, Miss. Code Ann. §§ 65-1-301 to -347 was unconstitutional as violative of procedural due process. Further, Miss. Const. art. 3, § 17 mandated that a determination of public use be made whenever private property was taken, and §§ 65-1-301 to -347 violated that mandate because the condemnor had the burden of proof on the issue of public use. Lastly, appellant argued that the statutes violated the separation of powers doctrine. However, appellant had not argued that point in the trial court and the court declined to consider it on appeal.


OUTCOME: The decisions of the lower court were reversed because the statutes under which appellee had seized title to appellant's properties were unconstitutional in that a pre-deprivation hearing was not provided and no determination of public use was made.
