Puckett v. State


NO. 96-DP-00867-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


737 So. 2d 322; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 122



March 25, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Direct Appeal of June 1, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Miss. LEXIS 130.
Appeal after remand at Puckett v. State, 2000 Miss. LEXIS 130 (Miss., June 1, 2000)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Knox v. State, 2011 Miss. LEXIS 576 (Miss., Dec. 1, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: FORREST COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/07/96. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. RICHARD WAYNE McKENZIE.



DISPOSITION: REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a Forrest County Circuit Court (Mississippi) decision that convicted him, after a jury trial, of capital murder while engaged in the commission of sexual battery in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-19(2)(e) and imposed the death penalty and denied his motions for judgment not withstanding the verdict or alternatively for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged a trial court decision, after a jury trial, that convicted him of capital murder while engaged in sexual battery in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-19(2)(e) and sentenced him to death and denied him judgment not withstanding the verdict and alternatively new trial motions. Since the trial court erred by failing to conduct the requisite hearing to determine if defendant could establish a prima facie purposeful discrimination case that the prosecution improperly used its peremptory challenges to exclude all available black jurors, the appellate court remanded for such a hearing. There was sufficient aggravating circumstantial evidence to support the jury's finding that defendant's crime was especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel. The trial court did not err in denying defendant's cruel and unusual challenges to the death penalty as the state's death penalty had been previously upheld as constitutional. Defendant's death sentence was not excessive and was proportionate to the crime committed.


OUTCOME: The appellate court remanded after holding that the trial court erred by failing to conduct hearing to determine if defendant, convicted of capital murder while engaged in sexual battery and sentenced to death, could establish a prima facie case that prosecution engaged in purposeful discrimination in using peremptory strikes against all available black jurors. Defendant failed to establish any other trial court procedural or evidentiary errors.

Genry v. State


NO. 97-KA-00861-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


735 So. 2d 186; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 123



March 25, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 06/24/1997. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT H. WALKER.



DISPOSITION: P76. COUNT I: CONVICTION OF RAPE AND SENTENCE OF TWENTY (20) YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS AFFIRMED. COUNT II: CONVICTION OF KIDNAPPING AND SENTENCE OF FIFTEEN (15) YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS AFFIRMED. COUNT III: CONVICTION OF SIMPLE ASSAULT AND SENTENCE OF SIX (6) MONTHS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE HARRISON COUNTY JAIL AFFIRMED. COUNT V: CONVICTION OF SEXUAL BATTERY AND SENTENCE OF FIFTEEN (15) YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS AFFIRMED. SENTENCE IN COUNTS I, II AND V SHALL RUN CONSECUTIVELY WITH EACH OTHER FOR A TOTAL OF FIFTY (50) YEARS. SENTENCE IN COUNT III SHALL RUN CONCURRENTLY TO THE SENTENCE IN COUNT V. THE APPELLANT SHALL SERVE A TOTAL TERM OF FIFTY (50) YEARS, DAY FOR DAY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment on a jury verdict of the Harrison County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted and sentenced defendant for kidnap, simple assault, sexual assault, and rape. Defendant asserted that the court erred in failing to suppress a pre-trial statement and in admitting DNA evidence. Additionally, defendant argued that Miss. Code Ann. § 47-7-3, which restricted parole eligibility, was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended on appeal from his conviction for kidnapping, assault, and rape that his U.S. Const. amend. VI right to counsel was violated when a statement was obtained from him after counsel had been appointed for him. However, defendant never requested the presence of his lawyer either prior to or during questioning. Further, defendant waived his right to counsel after receiving Miranda warnings before his inculpatory statements were given. The trial court correctly determined expert testimony and evidence of DNA testing to be admissible and any error in admitting the evidence was harmless in light of the overwhelming evidence of guilt. Miss. Code Ann. § 47-7-3, which restricted parole for defendants who committed sex crimes, was not unconstitutionally vague. The definition of "sex crimes" was so distinguishable that an ordinary person would know what "sex crimes" meant. Defendant had failed to include the DNA serologist's disciplinary violations in the official record on appeal. Therefore that matter was not properly before the court and would not be considered. Where there was no single reversible error, the case as a whole would not be reversed for cumulative error.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for rape, assault, and kidnapping was affirmed because defendant voluntarily waived his right to counsel during questioning, the trial court correctly admitted DNA tests and expert witnesses, the statute restricting parole was not unconstitutionally vague, and defendant failed to preserve the matter of a serologist's disciplinary violations for appeal.

Croke v. Lowndes County Bd. of Supervisors


NO. 97-CA-01474-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


733 So. 2d 837; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 100



March 18, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at, En banc Croke v. Southgate Sewer Dist., 2003 Miss. LEXIS 557 (Miss., Oct. 23, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LOWNDES COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: October 22, 1997. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JOHN MONTGOMERY.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of a judgment of the Lowndes County Circuit Court (Mississippi), that dismissed with prejudice a bill of exceptions and complaint for declaratory relief on behalf of residents or landowners located within a sewer district. Appellants sought judicial review of certain actions of appellee, the county board of supervisors, and a declaration that the law creating the sewer district was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, who were all residents of a county, challenged the trial court's dismissal with prejudice of their suit contending that a bill allowing sewer districts was unconstitutional and that certain ordinances of appellee, county board of supervisors (board), were unconstitutional. The court, applying a de novo standard of review, looked at the constitutionality of the bill allowing the creation of sewer districts. A local utility district could be organized and exist under a local and private law even when there was a general law respecting organization and existence of such districts, as long as the local and private act furthered the same general purposes and policies as the general act, and any differences were primarily procedural or otherwise relatively minor. The court affirmed the trial court's finding that the sewer district bill, a local and private law, was constitutional because it furthered a general law and because the appellants had not demonstrated beyond all reasonable doubt that the legislation was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the trial court ruling upholding the board's ordinances because the appellants had read parts of the ordinances out of context.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment dismissing with prejudice appellants' actions challenging the constitutionality of a bill that allowed creation of sewer districts and the constitutionality of certain ordinances passed by the county board of supervisors, finding the bill was constitutional and the appellants, taking parts of the disputed county ordinances out of context, had not demonstrated the bill's unconstitutionality.

City of Jackson v. Williamson


NO. 95-CT-01072-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


740 So. 2d 818; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 89



February 25, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected March 10, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JAMES E. GRAVES, JR. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/05/95.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted certiorari after appellants sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Mississippi) that modified a judgment on rehearing and deleted a statutory damages and interest award on the ground that the award was not assessable against a governmental subdivision.


OVERVIEW: The court granted a writ of certiorari to consider the issue of whether a political subdivision may be taxed with post-judgement interest, statutory damages, and costs after the trial court's final judgment is entered and the political subdivision appeals. After a motion for rehearing by appellee city, the lower appellate court entered a judgment that modified its opinion and deleted the statutory damages and interest award. Appellants sought review. The court held that Miss. R. App. P. 37 provided for the award of interest on a money judgement unless otherwise provided by law. Because Miss. Code. Ann. § 11-46-15(2) made no exception for post-judgment interest imposed upon a political entity, the court found legislative intent to allow post-judgment interest. In addition, the post-judgment interest statute, Miss. Code Ann. § 75-17-7 referred to all judgments, and was not limited to claims of individuals. The court also found that the legislature declined to exempt governmental entities from liability for statutory damages and costs. The court therefore reversed that portion of the judgment that denied the imposition of statutory damages and interest against appellee city.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that portion of the judgment that denied the imposition of statutory damages and post-judgment interest against appellee city after holding that the state, its agencies, officers, political subdivisions and municipalities could be assessed post-judgment interest, costs, and statutory damages because there was no statute which precluded it.

Edwards v. State


NO. 97-DP-00566-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


737 So. 2d 275; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 80



February 18, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: CLARKE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/27/97. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT WALTER BAILEY.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Clarke County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which found him guilty of two counts for capital murder, Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-19(2)(e), and one count for armed robbery, in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-19(2)(e), arguing multiple prejudicial errors at trial and sentencing, and thus requiring a reversal and a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Appellant and an accomplice asked the victim and his two-year-old son for a ride at a gas station. Appellant rolled the victim into the woods, forced the victim's son on his father, and shot the boy in the head. The court ordered that appellant was entitled to a new trial, since the cumulative errors required a reversal of the conviction.

Clemons v. State


NO. 97-KA-00373-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


733 So. 2d 266; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 77

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: NESHOBA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 03/12/97. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. MARCUS D. GORDON.



DISPOSITION: COUNT I. CONVICTION OF MURDER AND SENTENCED TO LIFE IMPRISONMENT IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS AFFIRMED. COUNT II. CONVICTION OF MURDER AND SENTENCED TO LIFE IMPRISONMENT IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS AFFIRMED. COUNT III. CONVICTION OF MURDER AND SENTENCED TO LIFE IMPRISONMENT IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner challenged the judgment of the Neshoba County Circuit Court (Mississippi) convicting him of three counts of murder and sentencing him to two consecutive life sentences in prison, to run concurrently with a third life sentence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant prisoner was convicted of murdering three individuals when he was 14 years old. On appeal, he argued that his statement to police in which he confessed to the murders should not have been admitted because, considering his age and education, he could not have voluntarily given the confession and/or intelligently waived his rights. Looking at the totality of the circumstances, particularly the testimony of the investigating officers, the absence of any evidence of mental or intellectual impairment reducing appellant's ability to understand his rights and the waiver thereof, or any special factors attributable to his age, the court concluded that the confession was appropriately admitted. Finally, appellant's argument that the court erred in admitting the admission of a co-indictee was rejected by the court. The court found that the argument was procedurally barred and would also fail on the merits. Thus, the court affirmed appellant prisoner's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant prisoner's conviction, holding that appellant's confession was voluntary and made with an intelligent waiver of his rights, and that the other claims raised by appellant on appeal were without merit.

Robinson v. Singing River Hosp. Sys.


NO. 97-CA-00324-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


732 So. 2d 204; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 57



February 4, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JACKSON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/26/97. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JAMES W. BACKSTROM.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Jackson County (Mississippi) granting appellee hospital and physical therapist's motion for summary judgment in appellant's negligence action because the action was time barred under the Mississippi Tort Claims Act's one-year statute of limitations, Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-11.


OVERVIEW: Appellant patient, an incomplete quadriplegic, suffered severe burns as the result of physical therapy treatments in which hot packs were applied to the back of appellant patient's legs. Twenty-three months later, appellant patient filed a negligence action against the hospital and physical therapist. Appellee hospital and physical therapist filed a motion for summary judgment, arguing that because the hospital was a political subdivision and the physical therapist was an employee of a political subdivision, the one-year statute of limitations for the Tort Claims Act, Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-11, applied rather than the two-year statute of limitations for the general malpractice statutes. On appeal, the court affirmed the grant of summary judgment. The court held that the one-year statute of limitations for the Tort Claims Act applied because the hospital was a political subdivision and the physical therapist was an employee. Moreover, the court held that the discovery rule did not apply because appellant patient's injuries were not latent. Thus, because the statute of limitations began running on the day of the injury, the filing of the suit was untimely.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee hospital and doctor because appellant patient failed to comply with the applicable statute of limitations.

Turner v. State


NO. 97-DP-00583-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


732 So. 2d 937; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 61



February 4, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied November 1, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 7156.
Writ of certiorari denied Turner v. Mississippi, 528 U.S. 969, 120 S. Ct. 409, 145 L. Ed. 2d 319, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 7156 (1999)
Subsequent civil proceeding at Curry v. Turner, 2002 Miss. LEXIS 426 (Miss., Dec. 12, 2002)
Post-conviction relief denied at Turner v. State, 953 So. 2d 1063, 2007 Miss. LEXIS 2 (Miss., 2007)
Motion denied by Turner v. State, 2007 Miss. LEXIS 47 (Miss., Jan. 4, 2007)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Certificate of appealability denied Turner v. Epps, 412 Fed. Appx. 696, 2011 U.S. App. LEXIS 3231 (5th Cir. Miss., 2011)
Related proceeding at Turner v. Epps, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 13810 (S.D. Miss., Feb. 6, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: CARROLL COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 2/15/97. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. C. E. MORGAN, III.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the Carroll County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which found appellant guilty on two counts of capital murder and which sentenced appellant to two death sentences. Appellant raised 13 assignments of error on appeal including an allegation that he had been illegally arrested without a warrant and an allegation that the trial court had erred in denying his proposed lesser included offense instruction.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was given two death sentences after being found guilty on two counts of capital murder. Appellant's convictions and death sentences were affirmed on appeal, despite 13 assignments of error raised by appellant. The court found that appellant had not been illegally arrested without a warrant pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 99-3-7 (1998) because all of the evidence was found to have amounted to reasonable grounds for the arresting officers to have suspected and believed that appellant had committed the murders. The court noted that even if the arrest had been found improper, that the error would have been harmless since no evidence flowed from that arrest which was crucial to the conviction. The trial court was not found to have erred in denying appellant's proposed lesser included offense instruction because, after applying the one continuous transaction rule, the actions of appellant were all related to the felony murder count as charged. Furthermore, the court found that appellant's failure to object to allegedly improper prosecutorial cross-examination had waived the issue for appeal. Appellant's remaining errors were also found to be without merit.


OUTCOME: Appellant's convictions on two counts of capital murder and his two death sentences were affirmed on appeal because all 13 assignments of error raised by appellant were found to be without merit. Included among the court's findings was a finding by the court that appellant had not been subject to an illegal warrantless arrest and a finding that the trial court had not erred in denying appellants proposed lesser included offense instruction.

 

686 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Watts v. State


NO. 96-DP-01030-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


733 So. 2d 214; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 45



January 28, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 8/09/96. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. R. I. PRITCHARD, III. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: MARION COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Marion County (Mississippi) that convicted him of murder and sentenced him to death. Defendant claimed among other things that the trial court's instructions to the jury concerning the sentences available for his crime were constitutionally deficient.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted and sentenced to death for murder. He appealed his conviction and sentence, claiming among other things that the trial court's instructions to the jury concerning the sentences available for his crime were constitutionally deficient. The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction but reversed and remanded his sentence. The court rejected most of defendant's claims as procedurally barred or waived because they were not preserved for appellate review. However, although defendant waived his right to challenge the constitutionality of the jury instructions by not objecting to them at trial, the appellate court held that the trial court improperly instructed the jury as to the available sentencing options. The trial court instructed the jury that the two sentencing options for capital murder were life in prison and the death penalty. Under Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-21(1994), however, there were three sentencing options - death, life imprisonment without parole, or life imprisonment with parole. Because the trial court should have presented all three options to the jury and failed to do so, defendant was entitled to resentencing proceedings.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction for capital murder, but reversed and remanded his sentence. The appellate court held that although defendant waived his right to challenge the constitutionality of jury instructions by not objecting to them at trial, defendant was entitled to resentencing where there were three sentencing options for capital murder and the trial court instructed the jury regarding only two of them.

 

687 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Fleming v. State


NO. 97-KA-01123-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


732 So. 2d 172; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 52



January 28, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/17/1997. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. C. E. MORGAN, III. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: ATTALA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Attala County Circuit Court (Mississippi) convicting him of the offense of fraud by a public officer pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 97-11-31.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 97-11-31, defendant was convicted of the offense of fraud by a public officer. Defendant allegedly defrauded the county by using county funds to repair the starter on his personal tractor. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred by denying his objections to the prosecutor's peremptory challenge of African-American veniremen. The court held that the state's reasons for the challenge were race-neutral and therefore reasonable given that the trial court was granted great deference. The trial court sufficiently met the requirement of a factual determination of the merits of the state's reasons. Further, the court determined that while the trial court should have removed a certain venirewoman for cause because she was related to a witness, the court concluded that the witness was a mere document introduction witness rather than a fact witness and that, therefore, the error was harmless. Finally, the court held that the facts were such that the jury could have found defendant guilty. The court ruled that putting a part rebuilt with county funds on one's own property reasonably could be deemed by a jury as warranting a verdict of guilty.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of the offense of fraud by a public officer. The appellate court concluded that the state's reasons for peremptory challenge of African-American veniremen were race-neutral and reasonable, that the trial court's failure to remove a certain venirewoman was harmless error, and that the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction.

 

688 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Hudson v. Moon


NO. 97-CA-01059-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


732 So. 2d 927; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 53



January 28, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected February 22, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 07/23/1997. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. DENNIS M. BAKER. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: DESOTO COUNTY CHANCERY COURT.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant heirs sought review of the judgment rendered by the Desoto County Chancery Court (Mississippi) that failed to grant them a right in the land conveyed to appellee foundation by decedent.


OVERVIEW: Appellee foundation was devised, in trust, thirty acres of land. Decedent had given appellee twenty acres of land on a prior occasion. The will contained a clause directing that "no part of the fifty acres be sold." The final decree of the Chancery Court adjudged that land could be sold and that conveyances by appellee within ten years would render the statute of mortmain inapplicable to said land. Appellants filed an action seeking to quiet title. The trial court found that when the mortmain statute was abolished, appellants' interest in the property was contingent and extinguished by the repeal of Miss. Const. art. 14, § 270. Appellants sought review. Appellants asserted that § 270 and Miss. Code Ann. § 91-5-31 granted them a vested interest in thirty acres of land which was subject to divestiture by sale by appellee within ten years of decedent's death. The court reversed the judgment of the Chancery Court. The court concluded that the ten years in the mortmain statute began to run at decedent's death and that at the time the mortmain statute was repealed appellants had a vested right in the land, which could not be stripped from them by the repeal of mortmain.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the Chancery Court that failed to grant appellant heirs a right in the land conveyed to appellee foundation by decedent because the heirs had a vested right in the land since appellee did not dispose of within ten years under the mortmain statute.

 

689 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Ivy v. State


NO. 98-CP-00200-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


731 So. 2d 601; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 29



January 21, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LOWNDES COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/20/98. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. HARVEY S. BUCK.



DISPOSITION: LOWER COURT'S DENIAL OF POST CONVICTION RELIEF AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Lowndes County Circuit Court (Mississippi) denying his initial motion for post conviction relief. The trial court found that defendant's motion was time barred by the three year statute of limitations contained in Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-5(2) (1994). Defendant claimed that his motion was not time barred and that the trial court could not impose a life sentence absent a recommendation from the jury.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to capital murder, and the trial court sentenced defendant to life imprisonment. Defendant filed his initial motion for post conviction relief alleging that his life sentence was improperly imposed by the trial court. The trial court denied defendant's motion and ruled that it was time barred by the three year statute of limitations contained in the Mississippi Post Conviction Relief Act, Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-5(2) (1994). Defendant alleged that the trial court erred when it determined that defendant's motion for post conviction relief was time barred. Defendant's motion alleged that he was serving time under an illegal sentence and was, therefore, not subject to the time bar. The court agreed with defendant and held that the trial court erred when it dismissed defendant's motion for post conviction relief. The trial court improperly declined to hear defendant's petition for post conviction relief. After considering defendant's motion for post conviction relief on the merits, the court denied it because the only viable sentence was life in prison. The trial court did not have authority to impose the death penalty or a sentence of less than life in prison.


OUTCOME: The court held that the trial court improperly declined to hear defendant's motion for post conviction relief. The three year statute of limitations did not apply because defendant alleged that he received an illegal sentence. The court determined that the only viable sentence was life in prison because the sentencing judge did not have the discretion to issue the death penalty or a sentence less than life imprisonment.

 

690 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Barnes v. Singing River Hosp. Sys.


NO. 97-CA-01552-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


733 So. 2d 199; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 31



January 21, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JACKSON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/13/1997. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. BILL JONES.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed the order from the Jackson County Circuit Court (Mississippi), dismissing their negligence action against defendant hospital.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs sued defendant hospital, alleging that defendant was responsible for their damages resulting from plaintiff wife's injuries. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss, asserting that plaintiffs' claims were barred by the one-year statute of limitations set out in the Mississippi Tort Claims Act, Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-11(3). The court held that there was no support for plaintiffs' assertion that the Mississippi Tort Claims Act violated the Mississippi Constitution. The one-year statute of limitations in the Mississippi Tort Claims Act was rationally related to a proper legislative purpose -- protecting the state's interest in conserving government funds and protecting the public health and welfare. However, the court held that, despite the absence of specific discovery language in the statute, the discovery rule applied to § 11-46-11(3). Plaintiffs filed their complaint within one year of their discovery of defendant's alleged negligence. Because the court found that the statute of limitations did not begin to run until such reasonable discovery, the trial court erred in awarding defendant summary judgment based upon expiration of the statute of limitations.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court which granted defendant hospital's motion to dismiss plaintiffs' suit and awarded summary judgment to defendant. Because the applicable statute of limitations did not begin to run until plaintiffs' discovery of defendant's alleged negligence, the trial court erred in awarding defendant summary judgment based upon expiration of the statute.

 

691 of 825 DOCUMENTS


James v. State


NO. 97-CA-01497-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


731 So. 2d 1135; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 33



January 21, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: COAHOMA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/10/97. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ELZY J. SMITH, JR.



DISPOSITION: DENIAL OF MOTION TO DISMISS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence from the Coahoma County Circuit Court (Mississippi) for possession of a firearm as a convicted felon in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-37-5. Defendant claimed that Miss. Code Ann. § 97-37-5 was unconstitutional because it violated his right to keep and bear arms as guaranteed by Miss. Const. art. III, § 12.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a convicted felon, was indicted for the crimes of burglary and for a violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-37-5, which prohibited possession of a firearm after conviction of a felony. The burglary charge was dismissed by entry of nolle prosequi. The trial court rejected defendant's constitutional challenge to the weapons charge and defendant was found guilty on the charge of possession of a firearm after conviction of a felony. Defendant was sentenced to serve a term of three years imprisonment without possibility of probation or parole. Defendant appealed claiming that Miss. Code Ann. § 97-37-5 was unconstitutional because he had the right to keep and bear arms as provided under Miss. Const. art. III, § 12. The court concluded that Miss. Code Ann. § 97-37-5 was constitutional and affirmed defendant's conviction because the right to keep and bear arms was not absolute and was subject to a reasonable exercise of the state's police power. By limiting the possession of firearms by those persons who have been shown to present a threat to public safety, peace, and order, the court held that the state reasonably exercised its power to protect the interest of the public.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for possession of a firearm as a previously convicted felon. The court held that the statute prohibiting convicted felons from possessing firearms was constitutional because it was a valid exercise of the state's police power to promote the public peace, safety, and order.

Rogers v. The Mississippi Bar


NO. 97-BA-01388-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


731 So. 2d 1158; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 40



January 21, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: COMPLAINT TRIBUNAL. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/06/97.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND RENDERED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant attorney appealed a judgment from the Complaint Tribunal (Mississippi) holding that defendant violated Miss. Rules of Professional Conduct Rules 8.4(a), (c), and (d) by converting funds from his law firm by performing legal services after hours and suspending defendant indefinitely from the practice of law. Defendant urged that the rules were unconstitutionally vague and that the evidence was insufficient.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed in part and reversed and rendered in part a civil judgment suspending defendant attorney indefinitely from the practice of law on the grounds that he violated Miss. Rules of Professional Conduct Rules 8.4(a), (c), and (d) by converting funds from his law firm by performing legal services after hours. The court held that Rules 8.4(a), (c), and (d), which prohibited violations of the rules or to engage in dishonesty, fraud, deceit, misrepresentation, or conduct prejudicial to the administration of justice, were not unconstitutionally vague because they were sufficiently clear as to their meaning and application so as to instruct those of ordinary intelligence, within the profession, on how to pattern their actions in accordance with the rules. The evidence below did not support the complaint tribunal's findings that defendant violated Rule 8.4(d), relating to the administration of justice, because the transactions at issue, loan closings, were not related to a judicial proceeding. In light of the mitigating and aggravating circumstances involved, the court suspended defendant from the practice of law for 180 days.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that the evidence was sufficient to find defendant attorney violated the professional conduct rules, except that defendant's conduct was not prejudicial to the administration of justice because it was unrelated to a court proceeding. The rules were sufficiently clear to avoid a charge of vagueness. Defendant was suspended from the practice of law for 180 days in light of the mitigating and aggravating circumstances.

Moody v. Mississippi Dep't of Pub. Safety/Highway Patrol


NO. 98-CC-00233-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


729 So. 2d 1249; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 13



January 14, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 01/07/1998. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. W. SWAN YERGER.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee challenged the statutory limitation on retirement benefits for state highway patrol employees. He sought review of an order from the Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which overruled the Mississippi Employee Appeals Board (board) and held that the matter was a non-grievable issue, that the board was without authority to declare a statute unconstitutional, and that the statute in question was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant employee brought an action against appellee, state department of public safety and highway patrol, and challenged the statutory limitation on retirement benefits for state highway patrol employees. A hearing officer found the statute violated appellant's right to substantive due process. The state employee appeals board (board) affirmed. The circuit court overruled the board and held the matter was a non-grievable issue, that the board was without authority to declare a statute unconstitutional, and that the statute in question was constitutional. On appeal, the court held the applicable board administrative rules clearly provided that the establishment and revision of the compensation plan were non-grievable issues. Further, administrative agencies were able to exercise only those powers granted by statute. There was nothing within the statute creating the board that allowed it to declare a statute unconstitutional. Finally, because the statutory limitation on retirement benefits was rationally related to the legitimate legislative purpose of fiscal planning, the statute did not violate appellant's substantive due process rights. The circuit court judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court, which overruled the judgment of the state employee appeals board (board), and held the statutory limitation on retirement benefits was a non-grievable issue, that the board was without authority to declare a statute unconstitutional, and that the statute in question was constitutional. The trial judge did not err in his holding.

Porter v. State


NO. 96-DP-01324-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


732 So. 2d 899; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 1



January 14, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT 08/15/96. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LAMAR COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. MICHAEL RAY EUBANKS.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeal from judgment of the Circuit Court of Lamar County (Mississippi), favoring plaintiff, and sentencing defendant to death for the capital murder of the victim; a third party had hired defendant and his roommate to kill victim.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his roommate were hired to kill the victim. Immediately after the victim's murder, defendant's roommate returned to the scene alone and killed the other victim, because she had recognized him. Defendant was convicted of capital murder and sentenced to death. Defendant's appeal involved only count II of the indictment, the capital murder of the first victim. The supreme court held that defendant's Sixth Amendment right to counsel was violated by a police-initiated interrogation that resulted in defendant's confession, and which occurred two days after defendant asserted his right to counsel at an initial appearance. The court concluded that the confession, made without the benefit of counsel, would have been suppressed. Therefore, the case was reversed and remanded to the trial court for proceedings consistent with the opinion of the court.


OUTCOME: Defendant's capital murder conviction and death sentence were reversed because his Sixth Amendment right to counsel was violated by a policy-initiated interrogation that led to his confession, and which occurred two days after he had asserted his right to counsel at an initial appearance.

Branaman v. Long Beach Water Mgmt. Dist.


NO. 97-CA-00522-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


730 So. 2d 1146; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 10



January 14, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 04/05/97. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WILLIAM L. STEWART.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant land owners appealed the judgment from the Harrison County Chancery Court (Mississippi), denying defendants' motion to dismiss plaintiff water district's petitions to determine just compensation for permanent easements on defendants' property, and the award of the easements to plaintiff.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, water district, sought permanent easements for drainage purposes on property owned by defendants. The statute under which plaintiff pursued the property, Miss. Code Ann. § 51-29-39, required only two days' notice in which defendants could prepare for a hearing before plaintiff could take private property from private citizens and determine what just compensation should be. This was not adequate notice, and the statute was unconstitutional as violative of due process rights. Defendants were granted a continuance to allow them to prepare for trial, and there due process rights were not, therefore, violated. Judgment for plaintiff denying defendant's motion to dismiss and determining fair appraisal for the taking of defendant's property was, thus, affirmed.


OUTCOME: Judgment denying defendant's motion to dismiss and determining fair appraisal for the taking of defendant's property was affirmed, where defendants' due process rights were preserved via a continuance to allow them to seek a fair appraisal on their property. The statute allowing plaintiff district to determine an appraisal amount and have a hearing with only two days' notice to landowners was unconstitutional as violative of due process rights.

 

696 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Reddix v. State


NO. 96-KA-00991-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


731 So. 2d 591; 1999 Miss. LEXIS 21



January 14, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 07/26/96. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JACKSON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JAMES W. BACKSTROM.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Jackson County (Mississippi), which convicted him of aggravated assault and sentenced him to four years imprisonment. Defendant complained that the jury was not properly instructed as to the elements of aggravated assault, as to the lesser included offense of simple assault, or that it was duty bound to acquit him if it believed he acted in self defense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated assault and sentenced to four years imprisonment. On appeal, defendant complained that the jury was not properly instructed as to the elements of aggravated assault, as to the lesser included offense of simple assault, or that it was duty bound to acquit defendant if it believed defendant acted in self defense. The appeals court reversed and remanded the matter for a new trial because the jury was not properly instructed on the elements of aggravated assault or on the law of self-defense. The court ruled that the instruction given by the trial court failed to set out the essential elements of aggravated assault because it did not instruct the jury that it had to find that defendant attempted to cause or purposely or knowingly caused bodily injury to the victim. The court ruled that the self-defense instruction given by the trial court failed to notify the jury it was bound to acquit defendant if it found that he acted in self-defense. Because the self-defense instruction did not properly treat the subject, the trial court committed reversible error by refusing defendant's offered instruction on the basis that it was inartfully drawn.


OUTCOME: The appeals court reversed and remanded the matter for a new trial because the jury was not properly instructed on the elements of aggravated assault or on the law of self defense. The court held that defendant was not entitled to an instruction on the lesser-included offense of simple assault because there was no evidence that defendant acted negligently when he shot the victim.

Cohen v. State


NO. 95-CT-00233-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


732 So. 2d 867; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 623



December 31, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/08/95. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ELZY JONATHAN SMITH, JR. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: COAHOMA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: DECISION OF COURT OF APPEALS REVERSED - JUDGMENT AND SENTENCE OF TRIAL COURT REINSTATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review, through a writ of certiorari, of the decision of the Court of Appeals (Mississippi) which reversed the conviction of defendant for shooting a victim and held that the trial court improperly refused a requested defense instruction on accidental injury.


OVERVIEW: The state filed for a writ of certiorari to review the Court of Appeals determination that the trial court improperly refused a requested jury instruction on accidental injury in defendant's trial for shooting an innocent bystander. The state claimed that the jury was adequately instructed by the jury instructions that were given when taken as a whole. The court reversed the decision of the Court of Appeals. The court held that the requested jury instruction was properly denied, as it did not correctly state the law and the instruction in the case as a whole adequately instructed the jury. The instructions given properly stated the theory of self-defense. The court held that the jury could have acquitted defendant on the theory he was fairly defending himself, but the facts did not support such a conclusion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the Court of Appeals and reinstated the conviction and sentence entered by the trial court, as defendant's requested instruction improperly stated the law and the jury was adequately instructed by the instruction given as a whole on the theory of self-defense.

Stevenson v. State


NO. 97-KA-00693-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


733 So. 2d 177; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 627



December 31, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief dismissed at Stevenson v. Miss. Parole Bd., 2013 Miss. App. LEXIS 527 (Miss. Ct. App., Aug. 27, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 04/04/1997. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. FRANK G. VOLLOR. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: WARREN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.
Stevenson v. State, 674 So. 2d 501, 1996 Miss. LEXIS 212 (Miss., 1996)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment from the Warren County Circuit Court (Mississippi) that convicted and sentenced him of capital murder, on the grounds that the trial court erred in admitting two large photographs of the victim, and in ruling that a witness, who was previously convicted of perjury, was unavailable under Miss. R. Evid. 804, and allowing the witness' testimony to be read to the jury.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction for capital murder for slaying a prison authority. Defendant claimed that the trial court erred in denying his motions judgment notwithstanding the verdict (NOV) or in the alternative a new trial, in admitting two large photographs of the victim, and in concluding that a witness, who had previously been convicted of perjury, was an unavailable witness under Miss. R. Evid. 804. The court affirmed defendant's conviction, holding that the large photographs of the victim were admissible because they were probative, and not prejudicial or overly inflammatory. The court found that the trial court properly admitted the convicted perjurer's prior testimony because as a convicted perjurer, the witness was incompetent to testify under former Miss. R. Evid. 601(b), which was an "infirmity" for purposes of determining the availability of a witness under Rule 804. The court held that the trial court correctly determined that the evidence was sufficient to support a guilty verdict, and properly denied defendant's motion for a directed verdict, request for a peremptory instruction, and motion for a judgment NOV, or in the alternative, a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of capital murder, finding that two large crime scene photographs were properly admitted, that the prior testimony of a declarant who was unavailable because of a perjury conviction was admissible, and that the trial court properly denied defendant's motions for a directed verdict, judgment notwithstanding the verdict, and for a new trial.

 

699 of 825 DOCUMENTS


City of Jackson v. Brown


NO. 97-CA-00359-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


729 So. 2d 1231; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 629



December 31, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 01/10/97. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JAMES E. GRAVES, JR. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant City of Jackson challenged the order of the Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi) that denied its motion for summary judgment, motion to reconsider, and motion for a diverted verdict in an action brought by appellee individual and representative for negligence in the death of his father.


OVERVIEW: The decedent fell into a creek located next to a street and drowned. Appellee individual and representative brought a negligence action against appellant City of Jackson for failure to properly maintain the streets including the placement of guardrails. The trial court denied appellant's motions for summary judgment, motion to reconsider, and motion for a diverted verdict, and the jury returned a verdict with judgment in favor of appellee. The court reversed the trial court's decision, granted appellant's motion for summary judgment, and dismissed the case. The court held that appellant was immune from liability pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-3(1) because the function that appellee complained about was a governmental function. According to the court, the placement of a guardrail between a street and the creek was not a proprietary function of street construction and maintenance from which there was no immunity pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-3(3). Rather, the placement of a guardrail was a discretionary governmental decisionmaking function that immunized appellant from liability.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order denying appellant City of Jackson's motion for summary judgment and other motions, granted appellant's motion for summary judgment, and dismissed appellee individual and representative's action for negligence in his father's death. The court held that the placement of guardrails between a street and a creek was a discretionary governmental decisionmaking function that immunized appellant from liability.

 

700 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Coast Materials Co. v. Harrison County Dev. Comm'n


NO. 97-CA-01133-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


730 So. 2d 1128; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 632



December 31, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/26/97. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. KOSTA N. VLAHOS. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant manufacturer sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Harrison County, Mississippi, which dismissed appellant's bill of exceptions and supporting affidavits that alleged a violation by appellee, Harrison County Board of Supervisors, of its stated policy to restrict sales within the industrial district to non-manufacturers.


OVERVIEW: Appellant manufacturer challenged the trial court's dismissal of its bill of exceptions and supporting affidavits and the affirmation of the decision by appellee, Harrison County Board of Supervisors, to sell land in the industrial district to a manufacturer. Appellant claimed that the sale violated a stated policy against such a sale and the trial court improperly dismissed its complaint. The court affirmed the judgment. The court held that neither the minutes attached to the bill or the affidavits in support supported the idea that appellees had a stated policy of excluding manufacturers. Appellee had the authority under Miss. Code Ann. § 59-9-19(b) to sell the land to be used for industrial operations, and therefore, the sale was not a violation of applicable law. The statutes cited by appellant were constitutional and clearly bore a reasonable relationship to the expansion and development of the state's harbors and ports by authorizing the counties to act in furtherance of that state objective. The court held that appellee was not required to provide an explanation of its deviation from its prior policy as no prior policy was ever established in its minutes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the bill of exceptions and the supporting affidavits, as appellant manufacturer failed to demonstrate an existing policy of excluding manufacturers from property owned in Harrison County. Appellant was unable to prove damages since it could not prove a change in the alleged policy and appellant failed to raise any constitutional challenge regarding the applicable statutes.

 

701 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Cockrell v. City of Southaven


NO. 97-CA-01073-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


730 So. 2d 1119; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 634



December 31, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected August 10, 1999. Certiorari Denied October 4, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 5010.


PRIOR HISTORY: DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/04/97. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. GEORGE C. CARLSON, JR. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: DESOTO COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review of a judgment from the Desoto County Circuit Court (Mississippi) that affirmed the issuance of an order of removal pursuant to eminent domain proceedings instituted by appellee city.


OVERVIEW: Appellants' home was located on property subject to a buy out program instituted by a local airport. Appellants failed to participate in the program, and appellee city began eminent domain proceedings. Appellants were awarded compensation and damages for their home. Appellants then filed a series of actions in federal court challenging the eminent domain proceedings. Appellants' claims were dismissed, and appellee filed an Affidavit of Eviction pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 89-7-27. The county court issued an order of removal, which was affirmed by the district court on appeal. Appellant sought review, claiming that the lower courts did not have subject matter jurisdiction and that state condemnation and eviction law must yield to federal law. The court affirmed, holding that had the proceedings been brought by a federal agency, jurisdiction would have been proper in federal court, but that appellee city initiated the eminent domain proceedings to acquire the property. Also the property was not part of the parcel being used for the airport, but for an adjacent city park, thus was not being acquired pursuant to federal law. The court rejected appellant's other claims of error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court judgment that affirmed the issuance of an order of removal pursuant to eminent domain proceedings instituted against appellant property owners by appellee city. The court held that the lower state courts had subject matter jurisdiction over the matter because the property was not acquired by appellees subject to any federal law, and the eminent domain proceeding was not instituted by a federal agency.

 

702 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. State


NO. 93-DP-01470-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


729 So. 2d 1191; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 590



December 10, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied June 24, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 4551.
Writ of certiorari denied Smith v. Mississippi, 527 U.S. 1043, 144 L. Ed. 2d 808, 119 S. Ct. 2410, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 4551 (1999)
Post-conviction proceeding at Smith v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 547 (Miss., May 20, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: DATE OF JUDGMENT: 07/01/93. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. GRAY EVANS. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LEFLORE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Leflore County Circuit Court (Mississippi) that convicted him of capital murder and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of capital murder and sentenced to death after he and his brother robbed and killed a liquor store owner. Defendant appealed, and the court affirmed. Defendant alleged several errors on his appeal, many of which the court refused to consider because they were not properly preserved for appeal. A party seeking reversal of a judgment of a trial court had to present a record adequate to show that reversible error had been committed and that the point was procedurally preserved. As for the remaining errors, the court found that they lacked merit. One error alleged was the trial court's dismissal of a juror after she expressed uncertainty as to whether she understood the law. The trial court was permitted to remove a juror when it was of the opinion the juror could not decide the case competently or impartially. Defendant also alleged the trial court erred when it failed to sever his trial from that of his brother. The court acknowledged that as a general rule a defendant in a capital case had an absolute right to a separate trial from that of a co-defendant. However, defendant waived this right when he specifically requested a joint trial.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for capital murder and his sentence to death were affirmed. Many of the alleged errors were not preserved for review because defendant failed to present the court with a record adequate to show that reversible error had been committed and that the errors had been objected to or otherwise procedurally preserved. The trial court did not err when it excused a juror who did indicated she did not understand the law.

 

703 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. State


NO. 97-CP-01202-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


730 So. 2d 567; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 587



December 10, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/13/97. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. GRAY EVANS. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: SUNFLOWER COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the Sunflower County Circuit Court (Mississippi) denying appellant's petition for a writ of habeas corpus to challenge the trial court's judgment of a life sentence for the crime of murder.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pleaded guilty to murder, and was sentenced to life imprisonment. Appellant sought post-conviction relief from his life sentence, claiming that he should have received a sentence reasonably less than life. The trial court denied the petition, ruling that life was the only available sentence for murder. The court affirmed the trial court's order. In so ruling, the court rejected appellant's argument that he should have been sentenced under Miss. Code Ann. § 2562, which provides for a sentence for all statutory crimes not containing a set penalty, because Miss. Code Ann. § 2217, providing for a life sentence for murder, had been declared unconstitutional. The court noted that appellant had previously raised this issue before the court, and it had been rejected as barred, under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-5(2) (1994). Moreover, the court emphasized that the sentence given to appellant was within the trial court's authority.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order denying appellant's petition for a writ of habeas corpus because the trial court had the authority to impose a life sentence for appellant's murder conviction.

 

704 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Clark v. Luvel Dairy Prods., Inc.


NO. 96-IA-01284-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


731 So. 2d 1098; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 578



November 25, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/09/96. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WILLIAM F. COLEMAN. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant injured person sought review of the order of the Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which granted the appellees, company and its president, the right to change of venue from the trial court to another court in the state. The injured person had brought an action against the company and its president for actionable words, false imprisonment, and defamation.


OVERVIEW: Appellant injured person brought an action against appellees, company and its president, (company) for actionable worlds, false imprisonment, and defamation. The trial court granted the company's motion for a change of venue and ordered that venue be transferred to another county court within the state. The court granted interlocutory appeal, reversed the order of the trial court, and remanded the case to the trial court. The court found that the history of the common law doctrine of forum non conveniens revealed no support for intrastate forum non conveniens, and that principals of venue were a function of statute. The court held that common law should only be applied when the venue statutes were silent and thus, by enacting a general venue statute which limited venue to the residence of the defendant or the place where the defendant could be found, the legislature effectively repealed the common law with regard to changing venue for the sake of convenience. Therefore, the court ruled, when change of venue was sought a matter of convenience, the venue statute applied.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court and remanded the case back to it for further proceedings. The court held that the doctrine of intrastate forum non conveniens did not apply in Mississippi. Thus, the trial court's decision to order transfer to another county court with the state was reversible error.

 

705 of 825 DOCUMENTS


R.S. v. State (In the Interest of B.D.)


NO. 93-CA-01186-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


720 So. 2d 476; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 574



November 20, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 2, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 07/12/93. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ALFRED THAD LEGGETT, III. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: PIKE COUNTY YOUTH COURT.

This Opinion Substituted by the Court for Withdrawn Opinion of June 25, 1998, Previously Reported at: 1998 Miss. LEXIS 308.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After adjudicating a juvenile as a delinquent child for his acts of burglary and grand larceny, the Youth Court of Pike County, Mississippi, held and a separate restitution hearing and entered a restitution judgment against the juvenile and appellants, his mother and stepfather, pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 43-21-619 (1993). An insurance company was one of the named restitution recipients. The mother and stepfather appealed.


OVERVIEW: Appellants argued on appeal, inter alia, that § 43-21-619 was unconstitutional because it allowed restitution against parents without a showing of fault on their part and without due process, that the State failed to offer proof of who exercised parental custody and control of the juvenile in question and whether the juvenile willfully or maliciously damaged or destroyed the property in question, and that the insurance company was not a proper party to receive restitution. The appellate court held that the restitution statute was constitutional is it was rationally related to a legitimate purpose and was a valid expression of the state's police power. Because all parties had proper notice that restitution was being sought and the opportunity to argue and object at the hearing, the restitution procedure comported with due process. However, the youth court's failure to consider evidence, and make a specific finding, as to who exercised parental custody and control over the juvenile was plain error. Although it was possible for the insurance company to qualify as a victim for restitution purposes, it was erroneously not made a party to the restitution proceeding.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the constitutionality of the act; reversed the restitution judgement of the youth court; and remanded the matter to the youth court for further restitution proceedings, with any judgment of restitution to be supported by findings, on the record, concerning parental custody and control.

 

706 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Tisdale v. Clay


NO. 97-CA-01076-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


728 So. 2d 1084; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 551



November 12, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/14/97. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WILLIAM JOSEPH LUTZ. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: MONROE COUNTY CHANCERY COURT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the mayor, the city attorney, and a member of the Board of Aldermen, sought review of a declaratory judgment from the Monroe County Chancery Court (Mississippi), which held that the city council, which consisted of the mayor and appellee Board of Aldermen (board), had the authority to appoint city officers pursuant to 1854 Miss. Laws 100, §§ 8, 21.


OVERVIEW: The mayor instituted a declaratory action for a determination of who had the authority to appoint city officers. The trial court declared that the city council, consisting of both the mayor and the board, had the authority to appoint the city officials, and that the mayor could appoint replacement officials. The mayor appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that § 21 gave the mayor the responsibility of enforcing the laws of the city and appointing replacement officials. The court further held that § 8 specifically granted the city council the authority to appoint all officers. The court found that the trial court correctly concluded that both the mayor and the board composed the city council, therefore the authority to appoint was divided between the mayor and the board.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that declared that the mayor and the board had joint authority to appoint the city officials.

 

707 of 825 DOCUMENTS


State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co. v. Grimes


NO. 95-CA-00918-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


722 So. 2d 637; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 525



October 22, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/17/95. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WILLIAM F. COLEMAN. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT

This Opinion Substituted on Grant of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of December 4, 1997. Previously Reported at: 1997 Miss. LEXIS 676.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee insured filed an action against appellant insurer, seeking compensatory and punitive damages arising out of the insurer's failure to pay the insured's car theft claim. The jury returned a verdict for actual and punitive damages in the Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi) in favor of the insured. The insurer appealed the damage awards.


OVERVIEW: On appeal of damage awards, the court held that the evidence was not so overwhelmingly in favor of an insurer that impartial and fair jurors could not have validly concluded the insurer wrongfully denied coverage. The punitive damages verdict was neither excessive nor against the weight of the evidence. The court affirmed the jury's finding that the claim was denied without an arguable basis, as it could have could have validly concluded that, absent some direct evidence the insured had committed the fraud in question, a denial of the claim was not sufficiently supported by credible evidence as to lead a reasonable insurer to deny the claim. The court did not find the punitive damages scheme unconstitutional. The court found no abuse of discretion in the trial court's disallowance of evidence that the insured was suspended from the police force, or in its allowance of a repair cost estimate as an adoptive admission. The fact that an arguable reason for denial of the claim was presented to the jury did not preclude consideration of punitive damages. The jury was free to decide whether there was an arguable reason for denying the claim and whether punitive damages were warranted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the jury award of actual and punitive damages to the insured.

Gulf Coast Research Lab. v. Amaraneni


NO. 91-CA-00172-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


722 So. 2d 530; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 504



October 8, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Remanded by Gulf Coast Research Lab. v. Amaraneni, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 496 (Miss., May 13, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 01/16/91. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. KENNETH BARKLEY ROBERTSON. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JACKSON COUNTY CHANCERY COURT.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employees filed a complaint that charged defendant state employer and defendant individual supervisors with violating 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 based on the employees' race and national origin. The Chancery Court of Jackson County (Mississippi) entered judgment in favor of the employees and awarded them damages and attorneys' fees. The employer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employees were hired to create a physiology section of the employer's research laboratory. The Board of Trustees of State Institutions of Higher Learning had authority over the employer pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 37-101-21 (1996). The court reversed and remanded the lower court's judgment in favor of the employees. The court held that neither a state nor a state agency was a "person" under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and the employer should have been dismissed from the suit as to that claim. The court also held that the employees' procedural due process rights were not violated. The court held that although the employees presented a viable claim against the individual supervisors under § 1983, the lower court applied an erroneous standard under federal law in finding discriminatory intent on the part of the individual supervisors and misapplied the law concerning damages. The court held that according to the record, the lower court apparently based its conclusions on the disparate impact that the terminations had on the employees. The court remanded for more definite findings on the issue of the employer's discriminatory intent.


OUTCOME: The judgment in favor of the employees was reversed and remanded.

 

709 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Page v. Siemens Energy & Automation, Inc.


NO. 97-CA-00063-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


728 So. 2d 1075; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 507



October 8, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 12/10/96. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. KATHY KING JACKSON. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JACKSON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, husband and wife, sued defendant company after the husband was almost electrocuted allegedly due to the negligent design of a disconnect switch. The case was removed to the United States District Court, but was later remanded to the circuit court. The Jackson County Circuit Court, Mississippi, entered final judgment for the company. The husband and wife's motions for new trial and for relief from judgment were denied.


OVERVIEW: The husband and wife appealed from the denial of their motion for relief from judgment. The circuit court had denied the motion on the basis that the claim of a skewed jury was waived. On appeal, the Supreme Court held that the Jackson County Circuit Clerk failed to follow the statutory procedures for calling jurors, resulting in the unilateral exclusion from the venire of persons qualified for jury service. The husband and wife were not in a position to discover the circuit clerk's practices of excluding all potential jurors who had been summoned to serve on the jury within the past two years and of granting excuses to jurors without them coming to court. Thus, the circuit court reversibly erred by denying the motion. The circuit court did not reversibly err by not taking judicial notice of certain testimony from another proceeding, since it would not have aided the judicial process further. Further, because the husband and wife could have exercised due diligence to discover that an aberration on the jury existed, they waived the claim on appeal.


OUTCOME: The case was reversed and remanded for a new trial.

 

710 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Malouf


NO. 92-CA-01177-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


722 So. 2d 490; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 460



September 24, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/21/92. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. EUGENE M. BOGEN. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LEFLORE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, father and paternal grandparents, brought an action against appellees, mother and maternal grandparents, for civil conspiracy and intentional infliction of emotional distress. The Leflore County Circuit Court (Mississippi) granted a motion to dismiss pursuant to Miss. R. Civ. P. 12(b)(6) filed by the mother and the maternal grandparents. The father and the paternal grandparents appealed.


OVERVIEW: A father of a child born out of wedlock attempted to prevent the mother from giving the child up for adoption. He obtained a permanent injunction enjoining the mother from proceeding with the adoption. The mother nevertheless allowed the child to be adopted in a sister state. The lower court found that, pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 93-17-5, the unwed father had no parental rights to object to the adoption of his child. It ruled that the paternal grandparents lacked standing to assert their claims against the mother or the maternal grandparents. The court reversed the judgment as to the claims of the father and affirmed it regarding the paternal grandparents' claims. The father had a federal constitutional right to be notified of or to withhold his consent to the adoption of his child in light of his substantial and prompt attempts to establish a relationship with the child. He was unable to establish that relationship because of the efforts of the mother and the maternal grandparents. The father presented a viable claim for intentional infliction of emotional distress and civil conspiracy. The court found that the paternal grandparents had no legal interests at stake.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court was reversed, except as to the claims of the maternal grandparents, and the case was remanded to the lower court for further proceedings.

In re Moore


NO. 95-M-00277-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


722 So. 2d 465; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 458



September 24, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] TRIAL JUDGE: HON. FRANK ALLISON RUSSELL. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: MONROE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: PETITION FOR WRIT OF MANDAMUS AND/OR OTHER APPROPRIATE EXTRAORDINARY WRIT GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state filed a petition for extraordinary relief that the court vacate certain orders by which the Circuit Court of Monroe County (Mississippi) had freed defendant, who was then incarcerated for manslaughter. The state contended that the circuit court judges were outside their authority in releasing defendant from the custody of the Mississippi Department of Corrections (department).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for murder and plead guilty to the crime of manslaughter. Defendant was sentenced to a term of 20 years in the department, with 10 years suspended dependent upon good behavior. Two circuit court judges later ordered that the balance of defendant's sentence be suspended, placed defendant on supervised probation, and released defendant. The state filed a petition for extraordinary relief that the court vacate the orders that freed defendant. Upon review, the court granted the writ and ordered that defendant was to be returned to the custody of the department. The court held that the orders were entered by the judges without the authority of law and, as such, were void and were vacated. The court found that the state's action in re-incarcerating defendant had a rational, non-arbitrary connection to a legitimate purpose, including the appropriate punishment for criminals, protection of the general population from such persons, and having the law applied in a legal manner by the judiciary. Defendant was not improperly singled out as subject to re-incarceration because there was no evidence of a discriminatory purpose.


OUTCOME: The court granted the state's petition for writ of mandamus and ordered that defendant be immediately returned to the custody of the department.

Molden v. Mississippi State Dep't of Health


NO. 97-CC-00454-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


730 So. 2d 29; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 443



September 17, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 03/06/97. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. PAT H. WATTS, JR. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JACKSON COUNTY CHANCERY COURT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant nurse aides sought review of a judgment from the Jackson County Chancery Court (Mississippi), affirming a decision of appellee Mississippi State Department of Health (department), which found that the aides were negligent in their care of a nursing home patient and which, pursuant to department regulations, revoked their nurse aide certification and permanently removed them from the certified nurse aide roster.


OVERVIEW: The patient was burned during a whirlpool bath supervised by one of the aides. The second aide transported the patient back to her room following the bath, and neither aide reported the burns. The court affirmed. The court rejected the aides' claim that the department's regulations violated the United States and the Mississippi Constitutions, holding that the regulations were adopted voluntarily to comply with federal law, and so did not violate principles of federalism; that the regulations provided the aides with due process; that the penalty imposed on the aides was not overly harsh; and that the regulations were not impermissibly vague. The court also rejected the aides' claim that the department's hearing officer erred in denying the aides' motion to compel the department to disclose certain documents and in denying the aides' motion to permit access to department witnesses, holding that the state rules of civil procedure did not apply in administrative hearings and that the department had followed its own regulations. Finally, the court held that the chancery court's findings were not arbitrary or capricious, and were supported by substantial evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the chancery court's order, which affirmed the department's decision to revoke the certification of the aides and to remove them permanently from the certified nurse aide roster.
