One (1) 1979 Ford 15v v. State ex rel. Miss. Bureau of Narcotics


NO. 94-CA-00521-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


721 So. 2d 631; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 401



August 27, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/02/94. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. GRAY EVANS. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LEFLORE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND RENDERED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owner sought review of a decision of the Leflore County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which entered a judgment in favor of appellee Mississippi Bureau of Narcotics (bureau) in the bureau's action to have the owner's van and two bank accounts forfeited pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-177 (amended 1972).


OVERVIEW: After the owner was convicted of conspiracy to sell narcotics the bureau filed a petition for forfeiture of the owner's van and two bank accounts. The trial court granted the bureau's petition and denied the owner's motion to dismiss. On appeal the court affirmed, in part, and reversed and rendered, in part, the trial court's decision. The court held that for forfeiture to be permissible there had to be a sufficient nexus between the crime and the property and the extent of the property's role in the crime. The court noted that the forfeiture could not divest the owner of property whose value was grossly disproportionate to the crime or the owner's culpability. The court found that the owner was driving the van when the drug deal was set up and that it was used to facilitate the drug deal, which gave the van a role in the conspiracy. The court stated that based on the severity of the crime, the forfeiture was not grossly disproportionate to the crime or the culpability of the owner. The court held that because no witness testimony tied the accounts to any of the owner's criminal conduct a sufficient nexus was not established and the forfeiture of the accounts was improper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, in part, the judgment of the trial court ordering the forfeiture of the owner's van. The court reversed and rendered, in part, the judgment of the trial court ordering the forfeiture of the owner's bank accounts.

One 1992 Toyota 4-Runner v. State ex rel. Miss. Dep't of Wildlife Fisheries & Parks


NO. 94-CA-00390-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


721 So. 2d 609; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 398



August 27, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 04/01/94. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. R. I. PRICHARD, III. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LAWRENCE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND VACATED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant properties, a vehicle, a boat, an ice chest, an electrical device, and a dip net, sought review of the summary judgment on a forfeiture petition entered by the Lawrence County Circuit Court (Mississippi) in favor of appellee Mississippi Department of Wildlife, Fisheries and Parks. The forfeiture was the result of the convictions of a husband and wife for illegally fishing and possession of the illegally acquired fish.


OVERVIEW: The properties were seized incident to the arrest of the husband and wife for taking fish with an electrical device and possession of illegally obtained fish. On appeal, the court reversed in part the summary judgment and order of forfeiture. The court held that the forfeiture of the vehicle violated the amended form of Miss. Code Ann. § 49-7-103 that excluded motor vehicles from forfeiture. The amended form of § 49-7-103 applied because the action was pending when the amendment was made. The court also held that seizures pursuant to § 49-7-103 were made only upon probable cause to believe that the prohibited conduct had occurred. The fact that that the officer waited until the husband and wife had returned to shore did not diminish his authority under Miss. Code Ann. § 49-1-43(4)(d)(Supp. 1997) to make the arrest or his authority under § 49-1-43(4)(b) to conduct the search on the basis of what he observed. The delay between the officer's observations of the wrongdoing and the subsequent warrantless arrest did not violate any state or federal constitutional restriction on warrantless arrests.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part the grant of summary judgment and order of forfeiture against the properties. The court reversed and vacated that part of the trial court's judgment inasmuch as the forfeiture of the vehicle violated the amended form of the civil forfeiture statute, which was amended prior to the conclusion of the action.

Pro-Choice Miss. v. Fordice


NO. 95-CA-00960-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


716 So. 2d 645; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 374



August 13, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/30/95. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. PAT WISE.

This Opinion Substituted by the Court for Withdrawn Opinion of June 25, 1998, Previously Reported at: 1998 Miss. LEXIS 310.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, doctors, women's organizations, and pro-choice organization, sought review of an order from the Hinds County Chancery Court (Mississippi), which granted defendant state's motion for summary judgment finding that the Mississippi Constitution contained a specific right to abortion and that the several statutes, rules, and regulations restricting it were constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs argued that statutes and rules requiring a 24 hour waiting period before a woman could have an abortion, Miss. Code Ann. § 41-41-21 et seq. (1993), requiring minors to obtain consent of both parents prior to having an abortion, Miss. Code Ann. § 41-41-51 through 41-41-63 (1993), Miss. R. App. P. 48 and U.C.C.R. 10.01, and requiring a physician to complete a residency in obstetrics and gynecology before performing abortions, Rules and Regulations for the Operation of Ambulatory Surgical Facilities and Abortion Facilities § 102.19, violated the Mississippi Constitution. The court held that because the mandatory consultation and 24 hour delay ensured that a woman had given thoughtful consideration in deciding whether to obtain an abortion § 41-41-31 et seq. did not create an undue burden. The court found that because it was not too restrictive, the state had a legitimate interest in protecting the health of its minors, and there was a judicial bypass, the parental consent law passed the undue burden test. The court held that the issue pertaining to the licensing of doctors was not properly before the court because administrative remedies were not exhausted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the lower court granting summary judgment in favor of the state because the statutes and rules placing restrictions on the ability of women to obtain abortions and on the ability of doctors to perform them were not unconstitutional.

 

716 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Coast Materials Co. v. Harrison County Dev. Comm'n & Delta Indus.


NO. 97-CA-00726-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


1998 Miss. LEXIS 384



August 13, 1998, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION.


PRIOR HISTORY: COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/26/97. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. THOMAS WRIGHT TEEL.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant company appealed a judgment of the Chancery Court for the First Judicial District of Harrison County (Mississippi), which dismissed its action against appellees, county development commission and competitor, arguing in part that the trial court had jurisdiction over an appeal from the commission's decision and that the action was not a collateral attack on the decision of the board of supervisors.


OVERVIEW: Claiming that it relied on the commission's representations that property in an industrial district was only for manufacturing companies, the company purchased property outside the district. It then brought an action to enjoin the commission from conveying the property to non-manufacturers. It also sought a declaratory judgment and damages. The trial court dismissed the action, and the court affirmed the judgment below, holding that Miss. Code Ann. § 11-51-75 provided a plain, adequate, speedy, and complete remedy for a challenge to the action of a municipal authority. Because the company failed to appeal the decision under § 11-51-75, it was prohibited from attacking it collaterally by way of a request for an injunction. The court also ruled that because the trial court did not have jurisdiction to hear the claim for an injunction, it did not have jurisdiction to hear the request for a declaratory judgment. Miss. R. Civ. P. 57 did not expand the trial court's jurisdiction. In addition, § 11-51-75 was constitutional and did not violate the remedy clause of the Mississippi Constitution or the due process clauses of either the Mississippi or the United States Constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment dismissing the company's complaint for an injunction, declaratory relief, and damages against the commission and the competitor.

 

717 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Turner v. State


NO. 96-KA-00957-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


726 So. 2d 117; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 372



August 6, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LEE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/03/96. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. BARRY W. FORD.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Lee County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him of the crime of driving under the influence resulting in death, a violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 63-11-30(4) (1996). Defendant alleged multiple errors, including in part the weight and legal sufficiency of the evidence, admission of blood alcohol results as well as other evidentiary rulings, and the unconstitutionality of the statute.


OVERVIEW: Convicted of driving under the influence of alcohol resulting in the death of another in violation of § 63-11-30(4), defendant alleged many assignments of error. The court denied all of them; some were dismissed without merit, some were errors but not prejudicial, and others were dismissed because defendant failed to argue or present authority concerning them before the court; hence, they were deemed waived. As to the more important issues, the court declared § 63-11-30(4) to be constitutional. It was not too vague because the level of culpability was only simple negligence and other claims of unconstitutionality were not argued and therefore not considered. The blood alcohol test results were properly admitted; there was probable cause to measure it, and defendant's verbal consent to the test was sufficient to make the "search," that is the blood test, constitutional. The trial court's exclusion of defendant's expert witness was not an abuse of discretion because, in part, the trial court was not satisfied as to the witness' qualifications to testify. Finally, the evidence was sufficient to convict. Therefore, it was not an abuse of discretion to deny a motion for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the verdict of the trial court that convicted defendant of driving under the influence of alcohol resulting in the death of another. Defendant's allegations of error were either without merit, waived by defendant's failure to present authority for his positions before the court, or were not reversible error. The court affirmed the sentence and imposed costs and restitution.

H. J. Wilson Co. v. State Tax Comm'n


NO. 97-CA-00121-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


737 So. 2d 981; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 362



July 30, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Modified September 10, 1998.
Certiorari Denied October 4, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 5774; 1999 U.S. LEXIS 5775.


PRIOR HISTORY: COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 12/23/96. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. DENISE OWENS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART FOR PROCEEDINGS NOT INCONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant business sought review of the decision of the Hinds County Chancery Court (Mississippi), which denied appellant relief in its challenge of use tax assessments by appellee tax commission.


OVERVIEW: Appellant business challenged the applicability of appellee tax commission's (commission's) two use tax assessments against it for the cost of the publications printed and mailed to the residents of Mississippi, one of which included use tax on postage costs, but appellee denied all relief requested. On review by the trial court, appellant argued that the tax rule providing for an exemption to newspapers resulted in unlawful, discriminatory taxation against appellant in violation of U.S. Const. amend. I. Appellant sought review of the trial court's judgment in favor of the commission. The court concluded that one criteria of Miss. Code Ann. § 27-65-3(l) was an invalid content-based criteria for determining whether a publication should be afforded the newspaper exemption from the imposition of sales and use tax, but the remainder of the statute was to remain in effect as constitutional content-neutral criteria. The court held that while the commission's tax scheme violated U.S. Const. amend. I, appellant was not entitled to a full refund of the use tax assessments, but only to that portion related to postage costs. The judgment was affirmed in part and reversed in part.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the trial court's judgment denying appellant business relief in its challenge of use tax assessments by appellee tax commission because while one subsection of the challenged statute was rendered unconstitutional, the remainder of the discriminatorily based tax exemption was content neutral.

Smith v. Roberts


NO. 96-CP-00817-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


1998 Miss. LEXIS 363



July 30, 1998, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied May 17, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U. S. LEXIS 3331.


PRIOR HISTORY: COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED:SUNFLOWER COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/22/96. TRIAL JUDGE:HON. GRAY EVANS.



DISPOSITION: LOWER COURT'S DENIAL OF POST-CONVICTION RELIEF AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of the decision of the Sunflower County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which denied his application for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: In 1973, petitioner pled guilty to murder, armed robbery, and kidnapping, for which he was sentenced to life, 45, and 30 years imprisonment, respectively, to be served consecutively. Petitioner also received consecutive sentences in 1976 and 1979 for aggravated assault. After petitioner was informed that he would not be eligible for parole until he served 36 years of his sentence, he applied for a writ of habeas corpus seeking his immediate release. The circuit court entered a judgment for respondent correction officials and denied petitioner's application. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that petitioner must serve 10 years for each 1973 sentence, 1 year for the 1976 sentence, and 5 years for the 1979 sentence, for a total of 36 years. Thus, petitioner's claim that he became parole eligible after 21 years was without merit. Further, petitioner was allowed to earn good time. However, he lost most of it after he escaped. Finally, a jury could have fixed no lighter punishment than that which was imposed by the trial court after petitioner pled guilty. Accordingly, it was completely within the trial judge's authority to impose a life sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's denial of the writ of habeas corpus relief.

 

720 of 825 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jones


NO. 96-CA-00937-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


726 So. 2d 572; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 322



July 2, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/20/96. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. PAT WISE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the State of Mississippi and various school districts, appealed a judgment from the First Judicial District of the Hinds County Chancery Court (Mississippi), which ordered that plaintiff teachers were entitled to lump sum payments at their regular rate of pay for accrued leave regardless of the school district in which the leave accumulated and held that Miss. Code Ann. § 37-7-307 violated the teachers substantive due process rights.


OVERVIEW: The teachers sought a declaration that the 1995 and 1996 amendments to Miss. Code Ann. § 37-7-307 were unconstitutional, and that the teachers were entitled to payment at the regular rate for all accumulated leave, regardless of the school district in which the leave accumulated. The chancery court ruled in favor of the teachers. On appeal, the court found that the teachers failed to meet their heavy burden of proving that the statute was not rationally related to a legitimate government interest. The Legislature was the appropriate entity to determine the question of lump-sum payment for leave accumulated by retiring teachers. Because the teachers were not a suspect class and did not have a fundamental right to lump sum payments for accrued leave upon retirement, only a rationally related legislative purpose was required. The court found that financial "chaos" in local school districts was avoided by limiting the lump-sum payment to 30 days accumulated in the last school district in which the teacher was employed. The State had a legitimate interest in ensuring the solvency of its school districts.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that ordered that the retiring teachers were entitled to lump sum payments at their regular rate of pay for accrued leave regardless of the school district in which the leave accumulated and rendered judgment for the State.

 

721 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Quinn v. Mississippi State Univ.


NO. 94-CA-01160-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


720 So. 2d 843; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 328



July 2, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/14/94. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: OKTIBBEHA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. LEE J. HOWARD.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parents appealed the order of the Oktibbeha County Circuit Court (Mississippi) that granted summary judgment in favor of defendants university, administrators and coaches based on sovereign immunity, qualified immunity, and contractual release, in response to plaintiffs' personal injury action brought under negligence and breach of an implied contract for the failure to provide baseball instruction to their son in a safe manner.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs' son attended a baseball camp sponsored by defendants university, administrators and coaches. Plaintiffs signed a general release in favor of defendants. A bat swung by the coach hit the boy in the mouth, knocking out one permanent tooth and permanently damaging four other teeth. The trial court granted defendants' motion for summary judgment. Plaintiffs failed to submit affidavits in response to the motion in a timely manner. However, any consideration of those affidavits was harmless error, since they only affirmed what the complaint alleged. Plaintiffs entered into an implied contract with defendant university upon paying the admission fee to have their son attend the baseball camp. The contract carried with it the implied promise that the university would provide a safe instructional environment for the campers attending the baseball camp, which was breached when the boy was hit with the bat. Therefore, the implied contract suit against the university was not barred and was not ripe for summary judgment, as a jury should have been allowed to determine the reasonable interpretations and contemplations of the parties concerning the release.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, and reversed and remanded for a trial on the merits dealing only with the issues of the implied contract and the release with only the defendant university.

West v. State


NO. 94-DP-01200-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


725 So. 2d 872; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 309



June 25, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT ENTRY: 08/11/94. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JAMES E. THOMAS.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE OF DEATH VACATED; REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Harrison County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him of capital murder and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: The jury in the trial court found defendant guilty of capital murder and sentenced him to death for the killing of a convenient store clerk. Defendant argued that the trial court committed reversible error in refusing his repeated requests to apply the amendments to Miss. Code Ann. §§ 97-3-21, 99-19-101, and to instruct the sentencing jury that it could sentence him to life imprisonment without parole. Prior to the amendments, defendants who were convicted of capital murder could only be sentenced to either death or life with the possibility of parole. The court agreed with defendant and vacated his death sentence. The court held that the plain meaning of § 97-3-21 indicated that the legislature intended any defendant whose pretrial, trial, or sentencing proceedings commenced after July 1, 1994 to have his sentencing juries instructed on the sentencing options of life, life without parole, or death. Defendant's trial commenced on August 8, 1994. The court held that defendant was entitled to the application of § 97-3-21, and the trial court's failure to do so constituted reversible error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for capital murder and vacated his death sentence.

In re Higginbotham


NO. 93-CA-01172-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


716 So. 2d 631; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 307



June 25, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT ENTRY: 10/05/93. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT LEWIS GIBBS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff supervisor sought review of the judgment of the Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which granted defendant state officials' motion to dismiss the supervisor's complaint alleging that his constitutional rights had been violated by an order convening a removal council for the purpose of considering whether there was a substantial basis for removing the supervisor from his public position.


OVERVIEW: Petitions were filed by concerned citizens requesting that the supervisor be removed from his office for failure to perform his duties. After certification of the petitions was made to the Governor, the Governor convened a removal council for the purpose of determining whether there was a substantial basis for removing the supervisor from office, pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 25-5-3. The supervisor filed the instant action alleging that his constitutional rights had been violated. The trial court granted the state officials' motion to dismiss the complaint based upon lack of jurisdiction. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court found that the trial court was without jurisdiction to review the supervisor's claims. The Governor's actions in accepting the signatures on the petitions was beyond review by statute. In addition, the removal council had the power to consider whether any part of the statutory scheme governing the removal of public officials had been violated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which granted the state officials' motion to dismiss the supervisor's complaint alleging that his constitutional rights had been violated by an order convening a removal council for the purpose of considering whether there was a substantial basis for removing the supervisor from his public position.

Post-conviction relief denied at, Application denied by Bell v. State, 879 So. 2d 423, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 543 (Miss., 2004)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Bell v. Epps, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 58264 (N.D. Miss., June 18, 2008)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Motion granted by, in part, Motion denied by, in part, Remanded by Bell v. State, 66 So. 3d 90, 2011 Miss. LEXIS 85 (Miss., 2011)

OVERVIEW: The jury found that defendant entered the store where the victim worked fully intending to use lethal force in robbing it. Tinnon v. Martin


NO. 96-CA-00271-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


716 So. 2d 604; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 299



June 18, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/19/96. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JERRY OWEN TERRY SR. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, patient and his wife, sought review from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Harrison County (Mississippi), which dismissed appellants' medical malpractice claim against appellees, doctors and a hospital, for treatment received while appellant was a patient at the hospital.


OVERVIEW: The patient and his wife alleged that he aspirated vomit into his lungs during the induction of anesthesia and/or during surgery due to the failure of the physicians and hospital employees to meet the required standard of care. On appeal, the court found that the lower court should not have imposed the ultimate sanction of dismissal because a letter was not a violation of the order of the lower court. The letter from the patient's attorney was simply attempting to clarify what the order required of the doctor while protecting his client's interests. A copy of the order and the complaint was enclosed in the letter. The attorney suggested that the doctor consult with his own attorney to determine an appropriate course of action in light of the order granting ex parte contacts. Thus, the letter as written was not a violation of the lower court order allowing ex parte contact. The letter was not an attempt to limit the disclosure as to time, place, or method. Further, Miss. R. Evid. 503(f) did not deny the doctors' equal protection, due process, or free speech rights. There were other avenues of discovery besides ex parte contacts.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded for a new trial.

Chamberlin v. City of Hernando


NO. 96-CA-00600-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


716 So. 2d 596; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 295



June 18, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/10/96. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ANDREW CLEVELAND BAKER. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: DESOTO COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, survivors of decedent, challenged the decision of the Desoto County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which granted a motion to dismiss the survivors' wrongful death action, which motion was filed by appellees, city, ambulance service, and ambulance service director (city).


OVERVIEW: The director responded to an ambulance call at the decedent's home. The director told the decedent's wife that the decedent would be a vegetable if he were revived. The wife gave her consent to stop CPR. The director told those performing CPR that the wife did not want the CPR to continue. The decedent died as a result of a cardiac arrest. Two years later, the survivors filed a wrongful death action against the city. The trial court granted the city's motion to dismiss. The survivors appealed. The court affirmed, finding that the Sovereign Immunity Act (Act), Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-1 et seq., applied to the case. The court determined that the city enjoyed the protection of sovereign immunity at the time the survivors' action arose. The court concluded that the survivors' action was timed-barred due to their failure to comply with both the notice of claim and the one-year statute of limitations provisions found in Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-11 (Supp. 1997). Further, the discovery rule did not apply because the survivors knew or should have known about the basis of their action, given that the decedent's injury was not latent. The court also upheld the Act's constitutionality.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that granted the city's motion to dismiss the survivors' wrongful death action.

Smith v. State


NO. 95-KA-01225-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


716 So. 2d 1076; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 285



June 11, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/12/95. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT LOUIS GOZA, JR. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: RANKIN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Franklin Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted her of conspiracy to possess more than one kilogram of marijuana with intent to distribute.


OVERVIEW: A woman found with marijuana at an airport stated that she had flown from El Paso, Texas to meet with defendant. The police approached defendant and she admitted that she had come to pick up the woman and take her to a place to exchange the drugs. The trial court permitted the woman's testimony about previous drug deals. Defendant testified that she did not know that her boyfriend and the woman were drug dealers and that they had set her up. The court affirmed defendant's conviction, holding that there was ample evidence to support defendant's conspiracy conviction and thus the exception to the rule allowing a party to allege factual insufficiency for the first time on appeal was inapplicable. The woman's testimony concerning previous drug deals was properly admissible to show that she and defendant had previously trafficked drugs and intended to do so on the day of their arrests. Defendant's criminal prosecution after the prior forfeiture of her vehicle did not violate the Double Jeopardy Clauses of the Mississippi and United States Constitutions because the forfeiture was not criminal in nature, was not overly punitive, and did not place defendant in jeopardy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for conspiracy to possess more than one kilogram of marijuana with intent to distribute.

Moody v. State


NO. 93-KA-00998-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


716 So. 2d 562; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 279



June 11, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 8/25/93. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JONES COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. BILLY JOE LANDRUM.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Jones County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted her of the crime of false pretenses brought by plaintiff State and denied her motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict or in the alternative a new trial.


OVERVIEW: The Assistant District Attorney testified that the automatic fine was a standard practice upon indictment of false pretenses, which presented defendants with the option of paying the fine plus restitution and having the case nolle prossed or otherwise facing criminal prosecution. Defendant was unable to pay restitution as an indigent defendant, was convicted by sufficient evidence of the crime, and received a jail sentence. On appeal, defendant raised the issue of whether the State's standard practice of imposing the automatic fine was in violation of the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment. The court held that the automatic fine plus restitution option was violative of an indigent's equal protection rights because it offered the class of potential defendants who were able to pay the fine the ability to avoid prosecution while the class of indigent potential defendants would always have confronted jail time. The court determined that the remedy was to remand for new sentencing where the trial court could place defendant on probation that required reasonable efforts to pay a reasonable fine pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 99-15-26 (Supp. 1997).


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the conviction of defendant for the crime of false pretenses brought by the State pursuant to the Mississippi Bad Check Law.

Mosby v. Moore


NO. 95-CA-00672-SCT CONSOLIDATED WITH 95-CA-01363-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


716 So. 2d 551; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 276



June 4, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/14/96. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. R. KENNETH COLEMAN. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LAFAYETTE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 06/16/95. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. R. KENNETH COLEMAN. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LAFAYETTE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the first case, plaintiff, mother individually and on behalf of minor child (mother), appealed an order of the Lafayette County Circuit Court (Mississippi) granting summary judgment to defendants, officers in their official capacities and city in an action to recover injuries from a car accident during a police chase. The trial court granted summary judgment in the second case filed against defendant officers in their individual capacities.


OVERVIEW: In the first action, the trial court held that the suit only applied to the officers in their official capacities and the city. In both suits, the court reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment only as to the officers in their individual capacities. It found that in both complaints the mother sued the officers in their individual capacities. In the first action, the mother filed for punitive damages and the affirmative defense of qualified immunity was raised, indicating that the action was filed against the officers in their individual capacities. The officers in their official capacities and the city were entitled to sovereign immunity under the new law, Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-3 (Supp. 1992). The law did not violate equal protection because it was rationally related to the legitimate purpose of protecting the public treasury. Officers were not entitled to qualified public official immunity when they breached a legal duty that was ministerial, the duty involved the use of discretion, or they committed an intentional tort. The court found that the act of continuing the police chase was up to the officers' discretion and they operated under a discretionary duty.


OUTCOME: As to both actions, the court reversed the grant of summary judgment as to defendant officers in their individual capacities. The court remanded the case for further proceedings.

Parker v. City of Philadelphia

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, parents and injured child, challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Neshoba County (Mississippi) that granted summary judgment in favor of appellee city in appellants' personal injury action, finding that the claims were barred by sovereign immunity.


OVERVIEW: The child was paralyzed after she was hit by a car while crossing the street. Appellants alleged that overhanging limbs obstructed the view of the road and that the injuries occurred due to the city's unsafe and unreasonable maintenance of the street. The court affirmed summary judgment for the city, holding that the city was immune from liability for the personal injury claims. Based on the timing of the action, the court applied Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-6, which required application of the common law doctrine of sovereign immunity. Under common law, the city was immune for conduct occurring in the exercise of a governmental function, and the placing of warning signs was within the purview of the city's governmental functions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to the city in appellants' personal injury action.

Mississippi Transp. Comm'n ex rel. Moore v. Allday


NO. 94-CA-00971-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


726 So. 2d 563; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 243



May 14, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 03/22/94. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JONES COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. BILLY JOE LANDRUM.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Mississippi Transportation Commission (commission) sought review of the judgment of the Jones County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which entered a judgment in favor of plaintiff victim in the victim's personal injury action. The victim also appealed the amount of the jury's award.


OVERVIEW: The victim was seriously injured when the car her husband was driving struck a pothole and careened into a concrete bridge abutment. The victim filed the instant action against the commission alleging that the commission was negligent in its construction and maintenance of the highway and bridge. The jury returned a verdict in favor of the victim in the amount of $ 160,000. The commission sought review of the judgment in favor of the victim, and the victim challenged the adequacy of the jury's award. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that the victim's claim was barred by sovereign immunity. The court found that its prospective ruling in another matter, declaring the unconstitutionality of the sovereign immunity doctrine, cloaked the commission with immunity protection from the victim's action. The decision finding the sovereign immunity statute, Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-6, unconstitutional did not become effective until the petition for a rehearing in that cause was denied, after the victim's cause of action arose. Therefore, when the victim's injuries occurred, the commission still enjoyed the protection of sovereign immunity.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which entered a judgment in favor of the victim in the victim's personal injury action against the transportation commission.

 

732 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Mack v. State


NO. 97-DP-00375-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


1998 Miss. LEXIS 249



May 14, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 06/29/91. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ELZY J. SMITH, JR. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: BOLIVAR COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: APPLICATION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant death row inmate filed a petition for post conviction collateral relief.


OVERVIEW: The inmate's conviction and sentence for capital murder were affirmed on direct appeal. His petition for write of certiorari to the U.S. Supreme Court was denied but a federal district court stayed his execution and appointed counsel to pursue federal habeas relief. The inmate filed a petition for post conviction collateral relief. An attorney requested that the inmate's case be stayed pending disposition of a federal class action. However, the inmate did not request a stay and the attorney did not represent him for purposes of his post-conviction petition. The court denied the petition finding that most of the claims were procedurally barred as they were decided on direct appeal or could have been raised at that time. The remaining claims of ineffective assistance of counsel were without merit because the inmate failed to overcome the presumption that his defense counsel was competent. The petition was a laundry list of issues with no supporting affidavits, argument, or citations of authority. The court denied the inmate's request for appointment of counsel because he had no state or federal constitutional right to appointed counsel in post-conviction proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court denied the inmate's petition for collateral post-conviction relief.

City of Grenada v. Harrelson


NO. 96-CA-00326-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


725 So. 2d 770; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 187



April 30, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: GRENADA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 03/29/96. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. C. E. MORGAN, III.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a decision of the Grenada County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which refused to enjoin certain elections. The city had filed an action for a declaratory judgment and injunctive relief against appellees, the members of a city election commission and a city clerk. The city alleged that the election process and the election districts did not comply with the requirements of Miss. Code Ann. § 21-17-9 (1990).


OVERVIEW: After the city determined that the election procedures and election districts adopted by its city council were not properly adopted, the city commenced an action for a declaratory judgment and injunctive relief against appellees. The city asserted that the election process and the election districts did not comply with the requirements of Miss. Code Ann. § 21-17-9 (1990). The circuit court determined that it had no authority to enjoin the elections and therefore refused to enjoin the elections. The court reversed the circuit court's order and remanded the matter to the circuit court. The court held that the circuit court had the power and jurisdiction to have enjoined the elections until the city could have amended its charter in compliance with § 21-17-9, as the city election commission had an official duty to see to it that the elections in the city were carried out in compliance with state law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's refusal to enjoin the city's elections and remanded the case to the circuit court.

Leblanc v. State


NO. 96-KA-01225-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


1998 Miss. LEXIS 287



April 30, 1998, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION


PRIOR HISTORY: DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/20/96. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JOHN H. WHITFIELD. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment from the Circuit Court of Harrison County, Mississippi, which found him guilty of violating Miss. Code Ann. § 75-76-301(c) (1997) of the Gaming Control Act.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested at a casino after he was video taped opening the top of a video poker machine, taking tokens from the machine, placing them in a cup, putting some of the tokens back into the machine, and going to the change window with the cup in his hand. Defendant challenged his conviction, but the court affirmed. The court held that defendant was procedurally barred from challenging the constitutionality of § 75-76-301(c) on appeal because he had not made the argument to the trial court. Defendant could not challenge jury instructions that he did not object to at trial. Defendant was not denied his statutory right to a speedy trial as guaranteed by Miss. Code Ann. § 99-17-1 (1972) because when the court deducted the numbers of days of the delay was attributable to defendant, the trial was held within the statutory period. Defendant was not denied his constitutional right to a speedy trial under the Sixth Amendment. Defendant and the State were both responsible for the delay, defendant never made a demand for a speedy trial, the delay was not intentional, and there was no actual prejudice. The State presented sufficient evidence to cause the case to go to the jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Fortune v. Lee County Bd. of Supervisors


NO. 94-CA-00102-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


725 So. 2d 747; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 321



April 23, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Filed: 5/6/98.


PRIOR HISTORY: DATE OF JUDGMENT: 01/04/94. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LEE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. THOMAS J. GARDNER, III.

This Opinion Substituted on Denial of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of April 23, 1998, Previously Reported at: 1998 Miss. LEXIS 161.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff widow appealed a decision by the Lee County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which granted summary judgment for defendant, a county board of supervisors, based on its finding that the widow's claim for negligent construction and maintenance of a bridge was barred by an amended sovereign immunity statute, Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-3 (Supp. 1997).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff widow's husband and their children were killed when a vehicle in which they were riding fell from a bridge without guardrails. The widow filed suit against the county board and defendant construction company, alleging that the county board was negligent in failing to properly construct and maintain guardrails on the bridge. In affirming the trial court's grant of summary judgment for the county board, the court held that the court's prior decision in an interlocutory appeal that affirmed the denial of the county board's motion to dismiss was not a final judgment. In its prior decision, the court merely remanded for proceedings consistent with an opinion released while the appeal was pending in which the sovereign immunity statute, Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-6, was declared unconstitutional. The court explained, however, that the decision was prospective in its application only. Thus, § 11-46-6 applied and the county board enjoyed the protection of sovereign immunity. The county board had no need to avail itself of the provisions of the amended statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment for the county board of supervisors.

Foster v. State


NO. 96-CA-00004-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


716 So. 2d 538; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 139



April 16, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/28/95. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. LARRY EUGENE ROBERTS. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LAUDERDALE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision of the Lauderdale County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which denied his petition for post-conviction relief after he pled guilty to grand larceny as a habitual offender and robbery without the use of a deadly weapon as a habitual offender and was sentenced. Defendant's petition sought to vacate the habitual offender portion of his sentence based on alleged irregularities in the indictments.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced after pleading guilty to grand larceny and robbery as a habitual offender. He sought post-conviction relief, claiming the habitual offender portion of his sentence should be vacated because the indictment did not include the previous convictions and due to the placement of the enhancement language in the indictment. The trial court denied the petition. Defendant raised the same issues and others on appeal. The court affirmed the denial of defendant's petition. It found that defendant waived his argument on the validity of that portion of the indictment in which he was charged as a habitual offender when he entered his valid plea of guilty. Further, the issue of whether the trial court became improperly involved in the plea discussions was procedurally barred because it was not raised in the petition for post-conviction relief. The court also rejected defendant's claim that he had ineffective counsel because defendant demonstrated no prejudice as the indictment was curable by amendment and, by pleading guilty, defendant received a sentence of 20 years while he could have been sentenced to life in prison without parole had he been convicted by a jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendant's petition for post-conviction relief to vacate the habitual offender portion of his sentence.

Humphrey v. Pannell


NO. 95-CA-00229-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


710 So. 2d 392; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 145



April 16, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified April 30. 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: PRENTISS COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/03/95. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JOHN C. ROSS JR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff biological father sought review from a judgment of the Prentiss County Chancery Court (Mississippi), which determined that he had no legal rights as the natural unwed father of a child born to a woman in an existing marriage after the child was adopted by defendants, the maternal grandparents.


OVERVIEW: The court had to determine what legal rights to notice the biological father had concerning an adoption of the child by the child's grandparents. On appeal, the court held that the biological father was entitled to no notice under the statutory or common law of the state and that his constitutional rights were similarly not violated. The court held the adoption of the minor child to be valid in spite of the lack of notice. Given the validity of the adoption, the trial court was correct in refusing to divest the adoptive parents of custody of the minor child. Miss. Code Ann. § 93-17-5 expressly provided that the father of an illegitimate child was not a parent at all for the purposes of the adoption statutes. Moreover, the state of Mississippi had no way of knowing that the biological father was the natural father, given that the child was presented to the court as the natural child of the custodial parents. The court held that the adoption by the grandparents be upheld and that they retain custody of the minor as her adoptive parents. The court further held that the provisions of the voluntary agreement were still in effect in which the biological father was granted visitation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the adoption of the minor child.

Jones v. State


NO. 95-KA-01313-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


710 So. 2d 870; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 144



April 16, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: BOLIVAR COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/21/95. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JOHN LESLIE HATCHER.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Bolivar County Circuit Court (Mississippi) convicted defendant mother of manslaughter and defendant son of murder with respect to the shooting death of the victim. Both defendants sought review.


OVERVIEW: Defendants raised several claims of error. The court rejected each claim and affirmed the convictions. The court agreed with the mother that the lower court erred in not requiring the state to turn over a previously taped statement of a witness that was used for impeachment. However, the court found that there was nothing new from the use of this statement because the impeachment repeated the witness' previous testimony. Thus, the court held that the error was harmless. Although the evidence was conflicting, the court held that it was sufficient for the jury to conclude that the mother aided and abetted her son in the murder. In addition, the court upheld the denial of the motion for a directed verdict. The court also rejected the son's claim that the lower court erred in denying his motion for severance because there was no evidence from either defendant that tended to exculpate one defendant at the expense of the other. The court also upheld the constitutionality of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-19(a) because the statutory language of "deliberate design" to take another's life clearly connoted intent to kill and there was substantial evidence that the son intended to kill the victim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant mother of manslaughter and defendant son of murder.

Corry v. State


NO. 96-KA-01251-SCT

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of a judgment from the Amite County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted the first defendant of hunting deer without orange and hunting deer without a license. The second defendant was convicted of hunting deer without orange, hunting over bait, and hunting deer without a license. Defendants alleged the baiting statute was unconstitutional and that the officers did not have probable cause to arrest defendants.


OVERVIEW: Based on a tip from a confidential informant, officers went to the location where the hunting violations were alleged to be occurring. The officers crossed the property of land owned by two individuals before they came to the lease where defendants were hunting. One officer testified that the officers observed the first defendant hunting from a tree stand before they entered the lease where defendants were hunting. The other officer testified that the officers had crossed over into the lease before the officers observed one defendant hunting from a tree stand without orange. The officers then discovered the second defendant that was hunting over an area baited with corn. Defendant's filed a motion to suppress the evidence on the basis that the officers were trespassers. The second defendant also alleged that the baiting statute, Miss. Code Ann. § 49-7-33, was unconstitutionally vague. Defendants were convicted. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that: (1) defendants did not have standing to assert that the officers were trespassers; (2) the officers observed the hunting violations and had probable cause to arrest defendants; and (3) section 49-7-33 was constitutional.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Newton County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him of capital murder and sentenced him to life in prison without parole.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and another man escaped from jail, broke into a home, and killed a man. They were captured shortly thereafter. Defendant was indicted for capital murder during the commission of a robbery. Due to defendant's extensive criminal record, the indictment charged him as a habitual offender in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-81 (1972). Defendant was convicted of capital murder and given the death penalty, but the court reversed and remanded for a new trial. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction of defendant for capital murder and his sentence of life in prison without the benefit of probation or parole.

Crawford v. State


NO. 94-DP-01016-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


716 So. 2d 1028; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 100



March 12, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: TIPPAH COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 04/23/94. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. R. KENNETH COLEMAN.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision by the Tippah County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted and sentenced him for capital murder, rape, burglary, and sexual battery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised many contentions of error. The court held that 1) the trial court did not err in refusing to suppress defendant's confession because the confession was not coerced and did not violate defendant's constitutional rights or the attorney-client privilege, 2) the trial court did not err in not requiring the prosecution to give notice of the aggravating circumstances because upon indictment, defendant knew that he was being charged with capital murder predicated on the felony of kidnapping and therefore, he had adequate notice of the aggravating circumstances, 3) the trial court did not err in disallowing the defense to voir dire the jury regarding whether they would automatically vote for the death penalty because the trial judge conducted voir dire directly on the issue, 4) the alleged errors in the prosecution's arguments were procedurally barred because the defense failed to make contemporaneous objections to the prosecutor's statements, and 5) the introduction of victim impact testimony during sentencing did not violate defendant's constitutional rights and was properly admitted as relevant to the jury's determination of whether to impose the death penalty.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Boler v. State

Farmer v. State


NO. 96-CA-00329-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


1998 Miss. LEXIS 46



February 19, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION


PRIOR HISTORY: DATE OF JUDGMENT: 04/12/96. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. GRAY EVANS. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LEFLORE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner challenged a judgment from the Leflore County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which had convicted petitioner of aggravated assault with a deadly weapon pursuant to a guilty plea under Miss Code Ann. § 97-3-7 and had dismiss his motion for post-conviction relief, which sought to vacate the conviction and sentence on the ground that his guilty plea was not knowingly, intelligently and voluntarily entered.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner pled guilty to and was convicted of aggravated assault with a deadly weapon under § 97-3-7. He then filed a motion to vacate the conviction and the sentence by order on the ground that the guilty plea was not knowingly, intelligently, and voluntarily entered because his trial counsel had advised that if petitioner went to trial, then petitioner would be sentenced under the 85 percent law, S.B. 2175. On appeal from the trial court's dismissal of the motion, the court held that: (1) although petitioner had prematurely filed the appeal, which was filed before the order of dismissal was entered, the court had jurisdiction to hear the appeal under Miss. R. App. P. 2(c), which required a suspension of the post-conviction appellate rules to prevent manifest injustice; (2) application of S.B. 2175 to those who committed offenses before enactment of the statute was unconstitutional as an ex post facto law; (3) applying the Strickland test, trial counsel's assistance was legally ineffective because the advice was erroneous and fell below an objective standard of reasonableness; and (4) hence the guilty plea was not knowingly, intelligently, and voluntarily entered.


OUTCOME: The court reversed petitioner's conviction and sentencing for aggravated assault with a deadly weapon and the denial of petitioner's motion for post-conviction relief. The court remanded to the trial court with instructions to allow petitioner to withdraw his guilty plea.

Keyes v. State


NO. 95-KA-01170-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


708 So. 2d 540; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 33



February 5, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion For Rehearing Filed: 10/2/97.


PRIOR HISTORY: COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/30/95. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT H. WALKER.

This Opinion Substituted on Grant of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of September 4, 1997, Previously Reported at: 1997 Miss. LEXIS 428.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought a rehearing after the court held that the administrative suspension of defendant's driver's license under Miss. Code Ann. § 64-11-23(2) (1992) was punishment for purpose of double jeopardy and reversed the ruling of the Circuit Court of Harrison County, Mississippi, which denied defendant's motion to dismiss his prosecution for driving under the influence (DUI), Miss. Code Ann. § 64-11-30 (1996), on double jeopardy grounds.


OVERVIEW: When defendant was arrested for DUI, he registered a blood-alcohol content of at least .33 percent. Before defendant was prosecuted for felony DUI, the Mississippi Department of Public Safety suspended his driver's license, pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 63-11-23(2) (1992). The court granted the motion for rehearing and affirmed the trial court's order denying defendant's motion to dismiss. Assuming that administrative license suspension (ALS) under § 63-11-23(2) was sufficiently punitive to invite a double jeopardy analysis under U.S. Const. amend. V and Miss. Const. art. 3, § 22, the court applied the Blockburger "same-elements" test and held that ALS required different elements than conviction under Miss. Code Ann. § 63-11-30 (1996). The court also found that ALS did not constitute punishment for double jeopardy purposes because the legislature impliedly indicated that ALS was a civil penalty by conferring the authority to impose ALS upon an administrative agency and because, based upon the Kennedy guideposts, the statutory scheme was not so punitive in purpose or effect as to negate that intention.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion for rehearing, withdrew its original opinion, and affirmed the trial court's ruling denying defendant's motion to dismiss his prosecution for DUI on double jeopardy grounds.

Ward v. State


NO. 96-CA-00067-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


708 So. 2d 11; 1998 Miss. LEXIS 4



January 29, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 01/29/96. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. HENRY LAFAYETTE LACKEY. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: CHICKASAW COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Chickasaw County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which denied defendant's motion for postconviction relief following defendant's conviction for sale of cocaine and escape from jail.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a plea of guilty to charges alleging sale of cocaine and escape from jail. Defendant was sentenced to 15 years' imprisonment on the sale charge, and five years' imprisonment on the escape charge, to be served concurrently. Defendant filed a petition for post-conviction relief, which the trial court denied. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment of the trial court. The court found that defendant received an illegal sentence on the escape conviction. Miss. Code Ann. § 97-9-49(2) provided that defendant's maximum sentence on the escape charge could not exceed six months. In addition, the court concluded that defendant's attorney did not provide effective representation because the attorney did not even perceive that defendant was being sentenced under the wrong statute on the escape charge, and that defendant received a sentence 10 times longer than authorized. The court held that defendant's guilty pleas were involuntary because defendant was not informed of the actual range of punishment to which he was exposed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which denied defendant's motion for postconviction relief following defendant's conviction for sale of cocaine and escape from jail. The court vacated the convictions of both crimes.

Beckwith v. State


NO. 94-KA-00402-SCT CONSOLIDATED WITH 91-IA-01207-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


707 So. 2d 547; 1997 Miss. LEXIS 749



December 22, 1997, Decided


NOTICE:

[EDITOR'S NOTE: PART 2 OF 3. THIS DOCUMENT HAS BEEN SPLIT INTO MULTIPLE PARTS ON LEXIS TO ACCOMMODATE ITS LARGE SIZE. EACH PART CONTAINS THE SAME LEXIS CITE.]


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected December 30, 1997. As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/05/94. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. L. BRELAND HILBURN, JR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of the murder of a civil rights leader and sentenced to life imprisonment. He appealed from the judgment of the Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi), arguing that his constitutional speedy trial, due process, and compulsory process rights were violated. He also alleged numerous evidentiary errors, prosecutorial misconduct, and errors relating to jury selection, jury instructions, and jury-related misconduct.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was released in 1969 upon the entry of a nolle prosequi after two mistrials had been declared. The State did not reinitiate criminal proceedings until 1990, after having learned that a State agency had improperly assisted defendant in the prior prosecutions. The court held that, as there was no statute of limitations for murder, defendant could have been repeatedly retried following mistrials until a jury reached a unanimous verdict. Because a lengthy pre-indictment delay was wholly irrelevant to a speedy trial claim, there was no violation of defendant's right to a speedy trial. There was no due process violation, as the State did not intentionally delay re-indictment. The State did not pursue prosecution because it did not believe it would have been able to obtain a conviction. Not until the State learned of the State agency's improper activities did it pursue the third prosecution. Thus, the State did not intentionally delay in order to gain a tactical advantage. The court held that the refusal to allow an undisclosed defense witness to testify was not a violation of compulsory process, as defendant was motivated by a desire to obtain a tactical advantage.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant of murder and sentenced him to life imprisonment.

 

748 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Beckwith v. State


NO. 94-KA-00402-SCT CONSOLIDATED WITH 91-IA-01207-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


707 So. 2d 547; 1997 Miss. LEXIS 749



December 22, 1997, Decided


NOTICE:

 [**1] [EDITOR'S NOTE: PART 1 OF 3. THIS DOCUMENT HAS BEEN SPLIT INTO MULTIPLE PARTS ON LEXIS TO ACCOMMODATE ITS LARGE SIZE. EACH PART CONTAINS THE SAME LEXIS CITE.]


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected December 30, 1997. As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/05/94. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. L. BRELAND HILBURN, JR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted and sentenced him for the 1969 murder of a well-known civil rights leader. He argued that the trial in 1990 violated his right to speedy trial, due process, and his right to compulsory process.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction and life sentence for the murder of a well-known civil rights leader. Defendant was released in 1969 on a nolle prosequi of the indictment after two mistrials. The state did not re-initiate criminal proceedings until 1990, when defendant was tried and convicted. Defendant challenged his conviction, alleging violations of his right to speedy trial, due process rights, and his right to compulsory process. He also argued that the trial court erred in admitting into evidence various items for the sole purpose of inflaming and prejudicing the jury against defendant. The appellate court affirmed the conviction because no statute of limitations existed for murder and a defendant could be repeatedly retried following mistrials until a jury reached a unanimous verdict. The appellate court held that defendant was not prejudiced by the lapse in time and that there was no due process violation because the state did not intentionally delay re-indictment. The court also held that the refusal to allow an undisclosed defense witness to testify was not a violation of compulsory process where the defense was motivated by a desire to obtain a tactical advantage.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction and the life sentence imposed on defendant was affirmed because the defendant failed to show that he was prejudiced by the lapse in time. The court held that a nolle prosequi entered in a particular case at an end on the docket did not bar another prosecution for the same offense if commenced in the court where the case originated.

Woodward v. State


NO. 95-DP-00144-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


726 So. 2d 524; 1997 Miss. LEXIS 742



December 18, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Woodward v. Mississippi, 526 U.S. 1041, 119 S. Ct. 1338, 143 L. Ed. 2d 502, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 2253 (1999)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Application denied by Woodward v. State, 843 So. 2d 1, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 92 (Miss., 2003)
Motion granted by Woodward v. State, 2010 Miss. LEXIS 229 (Miss., May 6, 2010)
Stay denied by Woodward v. State, 2010 Miss. LEXIS 255 (Miss., May 20, 2010)

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: PERRY COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/20/95. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. RICHARD WAYNE McKENZIE.
Woodward v. State, 1993 Miss. LEXIS 605 (Miss., Dec. 23, 1993)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Perry County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which sentenced him to death for the brutal rape and capital murder of a woman.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought review of the lower court's imposition of the death sentence. Defendant had been convicted of the rape and murder of a volunteer, court-appointed, special advocate for children. The court affirmed the death sentence because an indigent defendant was not entitled to select his own psychiatrist, peremptory challenges of black veniremen were for race-neutral reasons, the use of photographs and a projector were proper, a disjunctive jury instruction was permissible as to aggravating circumstances, and the penalty was proportionate to the crime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the death sentence imposed upon defendant.

 

750 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Brown v. Houston Sch. Dist.


NO. 95-CA-00268-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


704 So. 2d 1325; 1997 Miss. LEXIS 745



December 18, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: CHICKASAW COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/17/95. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. R. KENNETH COLEMAN.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of the order of the Chickasaw County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, school district and officials, in the mother's action for wrongful death and for claims made pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and the Individuals with Disabilities Education Act (IDEA), 20 U.S.C.S. § 1400 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The mother's child, a special education student, was left unattended in the principal's office after being disciplined. He left the office and ran away from the school. The next day his body was found in a creek not far from the school. The mother filed a wrongful death action against the school district and officials. She also alleged claims brought under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and the IDEA. The trial court granted summary judgment to the school district and officials, finding that the claims were barred as a matter of law by sovereign immunity. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-1 et seq., provided legislative sovereign immunity to the school district. Moreover, the incident giving rise to the wrongful death action occurred prior to a precedent that only had prospective application. The court found that the mother failed to establish any violation of a clearly established constitutional right under color of state law. Thus, her claim 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 was properly dismissed. Similarly, the mother failed to provide a factual basis for her IDEA claim. There was no evidence that her child was denied a free, appropriate public education.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which granted summary judgment in favor of the school district and its officials. The mother's wrongful death claim was barred by sovereign immunity, and she provided no factual basis for the § 1983 or IDEA claims.

 

751 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Jenkins v. State


NO. 97-CA-00489-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


1997 Miss. LEXIS 692



December 8, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION.


PRIOR HISTORY: DATE OF JUDGMENT: 04/07/97. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. HENRY LAFAYETTE LACKEY. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LAFAYETTE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate was granted leave to appeal in forma pauperis from a judgment of the Lafayette County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which granted defendant State's motion for summary dismissal of the inmate's motion for post-conviction relief pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-11(2) (1972). The inmate claimed that his guilty pleas were involuntary for failure to inform him that a plea of guilty would waive his right against self-incrimination.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted in a jury trial of capital murder and was sentenced to life in prison on February 22, 1986. He later entered guilty pleas to aggravated assault, burglary, and grand larceny. Almost ten years later, the inmate filed a motion to vacate his guilty pleas. He claimed his pleas were involuntary because the trial judge failed to advise him that by pleading guilty, he was waiving his right against self-incrimination. He also asserted that he was unaware that his guilty pleas would waive this right, and had he known the effect he would not have pleaded guilty. The court held that the inmate had three years from the date of his pleas to petition for post-conviction relief, making his deadline April 14, 1989. He missed the deadline by almost eight years by filing his motion on April 3, 1997. None of the recognized exceptions to the time-bar applied and none was asserted in his brief. Therefore, his motion was time-barred on its face pursuant to § 99-39-5(2). The court rejected the inmate's argument that his claim should not be time-barred because the trial court's alleged failure to inform him of the consequences of his guilty plea raised a constitutional concern.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment dismissing the inmate's petition for post-conviction relief.

 

752 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Adams v. State


NO. 95-CA-01257-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


1997 Miss. LEXIS 699



December 8, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION.


PRIOR HISTORY: DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/27/95. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. KEITH STARRETT. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: PIKE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After appellant inmate was convicted and sentenced for conspiracy to commit the crime of unlawful possession of cocaine with intent to distribute and being a habitual offender, he filed a motion for post-conviction relief, claiming that his sentence was disproportionate, that his guilty plea was involuntary, and that counsel was ineffective. After hearing, the Pike County Circuit Court (Mississippi), entered a judgment denying relief.


OVERVIEW: The inmate and others were indicted for conspiracy and unlawful possession of cocaine with intent to distribute. After signing a form, which provided that he was aware of his rights and voluntarily and knowingly offered a guilty plea, he pled guilty to conspiracy. He was found to be a habitual criminal and was sentenced to 20 years in prison, without the benefit of probation, parole, or early release. Co-defendants were not prosecuted with enhancement. On appeal, the court held that the circuit court properly rejected the inmate's claim that he was subjected to selective prosecution. The inmate failed to show either that he was singled out for prosecution though others who committed the same acts were not prosecuted or that the selective prosecution of him was driven by constitutionally-impermissible motives. Moreover, the disparity in the inmate's sentence and that of co-defendant's was attributable to the fact that he, unlike co-defendant, was sentenced as a habitual offender. There was no merit to the inmate's claim that he pled guilty due to counsel's threatening him with an 80-year sentence if he did not. The record showed the inmate knew his rights before pleading guilty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

 

753 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Irving v. Lee


NO. 96-CA-00708-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


1997 Miss. LEXIS 632



November 20, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION.


PRIOR HISTORY: DATE OF JUDGMENT: 06/05/96. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. GRAY EVANS. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: SUNFLOWER COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate brought a petition for a writ of habeas corpus against appellees, the Director of Classification, the then Superintendent of the Mississippi State Penitentiary, and his successor in office. Treating the petition as one for post-conviction relief, the Circuit Court of Sunflower County (Mississippi) denied the petition. The inmate then filed a notice of appeal and the circuit court granted him leave to proceed in forma pauperis.


OVERVIEW: The inmate's habeas corpus petition challenged his custody classification status. The circuit court summarily dismissed the petition. On appeal, the court held that the circuit court properly denied the inmate's petition for a writ of habeas corpus but also could and should have ruled that it had no jurisdiction over this purely administrative decision regarding the inmate's classification status. Moreover, the court held that the circuit court erred in allowing the inmate to proceed to the instant court in forma pauperis on a custody classification matter. Specifically, an inmate had no right to appeal in forma pauperis in any other than a criminal case or an action for post-conviction relief pursuant to the Mississippi Uniform Post-Conviction Collateral Relief Act (Act), Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-1, et seq. The court reasoned that the inmate's complaint regarding custody classification was not a criminal matter and did not fall under one of the enumerated grounds for relief set forth in § 99-39-5(1) of the Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Berry v. State

Motion dismissed by Berry v. State, 2008 Miss. LEXIS 216 (Miss., May 8, 2008)
Motion granted by, Motion denied by, Stay denied by Berry v. State, 2008 Miss. LEXIS 249 (Miss., May 22, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 06/25/92. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. R. KENNETH COLEMAN. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: CHICKASAW COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.
Berry v. State, 575 So. 2d 1, 1990 Miss. LEXIS 849 (Miss., 1990)



DISPOSITION: REMANDED TO THE CIRCUIT COURT TO CONDUCT A BATSON HEARING; AFFIRMED ALL REMAINING ISSUES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In accordance with the jury's verdict, the Circuit Court of Chickasaw County (Mississippi) convicted defendant of capital murder and sentenced him to death. The conviction was affirmed, but the death sentence was vacated and remanded for a new sentencing trial. On retrial, the jury again returned a sentence of death. The trial court denied defendant's motion for a new trial and judgment notwithstanding the verdict. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant confessed to a kidnapping and murder. Defendant appealed his death sentence, raising 18 separate errors for review. Finding that defendant waived many of the errors by failing to make a contemporaneous objections, the state supreme court rejected every assignment of error except for one. Specifically, the court remanded for a Batson hearing because the trial court failed to recognize that a white defendant had standing to challenge discriminatory peremptory strikes. The prosecution struck every available black person from the venire except for the one left after it had exhausted all of its peremptory challenges. This resulted in a jury of eleven whites and one black. Such a jury composition certainly created an inference of purposeful discrimination. Where a case had no reversible error other than a Batson violation without a Batson hearing, the proper remedy was to remand the case for a Batson hearing. If the lower court found discrimination, then a new trial would be ordered. If the trial court found no evidence of discrimination, then the cause would be certified to the state supreme court along with the record of the hearing and the finding of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court remanded to the trial court to conduct a Batson hearing, but affirmed all remaining issues.
