Am. Federated Life Ins. Co. v. Dale


NO. 95-CA-01036-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


701 So. 2d 809; 1997 Miss. LEXIS 625



November 13, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/18/95. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. DENISE OWENS.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant life insurance company challenged a judgment from the Chancery Court of Hinds County (Mississippi), which granted appellee Commissioner of Insurance's (commissioner) motion for summary judgment in the life insurance company's petition for review and objection to a newly adopted regulation by the commissioner.


OVERVIEW: The life insurance company objected to a proposed regulation by the commissioner that related to rates charged for certain "age bands" with respect to credit life insurance pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. §§ 85-53-23(2)(b) and 83-53-23(5) (1991), which provided that an insurance company was allowed to charge certain maximum rates for credit life insurance without the commissioner's approval if they made coverage available to all customers less than 65 years old. Following the adoption of the regulation, the life insurance company filed a complaint and appeal for review in the lower court, but they granted the commissioner's motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court reversed. The court ruled that the commissioner's regulation exceeded his authority because it materially altered § 85-53-23(5) where the regulation required at least a 50 percent overall loss ratio in order to charge the maximum rates, and an administrative officer was not able to have lawfully adopted regulations that were inconsistent with any statutes.


OUTCOME: The court reversed in favor of the life insurance company and granted their motion for summary judgment in their petition for review and appeal of a regulation adopted by the commissioner.

Hord v. City of Yazoo City


NO. 95-CA-00524-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


702 So. 2d 121; 1997 Miss. LEXIS 626



November 13, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 04/04/95. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JAMES E. GRAVES, JR.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Hinds County (Mississippi), which dismissed the inmate's negligence action against defendant city as barred by the city's sovereign immunity under the Mississippi Tort Claims Act.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was sent to a work center and assigned the duty of mounting used tires. While he was mounting the used tires, a tire exploded resulting in serious injuries to his hand. The inmate filed an action alleging that the commissioner of corrections acted in negligent disregard of the inmate's personal safety in violation of the Eighth Amendment. The complaint also alleged that the city acted negligently in failing to provide proper training, supervision, and safety equipment. The case was removed to a federal district court, which dismissed the inmate's 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claims under the Eighth Amendment. On remand to state court, the circuit court granted the city's motion to dismiss pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-9 (1)(m) (Supp. 1996), which barred claims against governmental entities by inmates and § 11-46-9 (1)(n), which barred claims arising out of work performed by convicts when the work was authorized by law. The court reversed and held the pre-Pruett common law standard was applicable and that the assignment of the inmate to mount used tires on a passenger van owned by the city was a proprietary function for which the city enjoyed no sovereign immunity.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of the city's motion to dismiss.

 

757 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Peterson v. State


No. 96-CA-00985-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


1997 Miss. LEXIS 616



November 6, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION.


PRIOR HISTORY: DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/20/96. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. GRAY EVANS. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: SUNFLOWER COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.

Reported in Table Case Format at: 1997 Miss. LEXIS 663.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Sunflower County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which denied appellant's petition for post-conviction relief after he was convicted of a sale of cocaine and sentenced as a habitual offender to a term of 10 years without the possibility of parole.


OVERVIEW: After appellant pled guilty to a sale of cocaine, the circuit court convicted him and sentenced him as a habitual offender. The court affirmed the denial of a petition for post-conviction relief. Appellant subsequently filed a second petition for post-conviction relief based on the alleged illegality of his sentence and brought an ore tenus motion to amend and include a claim of ineffective assistance of counsel. The circuit court granted the motion to amend but denied the petition. On appeal, the court concluded that the second petition was both time barred and barred as a successive writ and that the claim of ineffective assistance of counsel failed on the merits. The court determined that the second petition, which was filed more than five years after the guilty plea, conviction, and sentence, was time-barred under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-5(2) (1994) and was a successive writ and that no intervening decision lifted the procedural bars. The court concluded that, although appellant's counsel was deficient in failing to object to the fatally defective habitual offender portion of an indictment, there was no prejudice to the defense because an amendment could have cured the defect.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

Fuselier v. State


No. 96-DP-00045-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


702 So. 2d 388; 1997 Miss. LEXIS 529



October 23, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Fuselier v. Hamilton, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 82381 (S.D. Miss., June 18, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JONES COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 12/14/95. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. BILLY JOE LANDRUM.
Fuselier v. State, 654 So. 2d 519, 1995 Miss. LEXIS 222 (Miss., 1995)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Jones County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which on remand had convicted defendant of capital murder and had sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was accused of the stabbing the victim to death. On his two previous trials, he had been found guilty. On his third trial, defendant was convicted of capital murder sentenced to death. Defendant appealed. The court held that the trial court's decision to allow the State to present evidence of defendant's flight warranted reversal of his conviction and sentence. When defendant had been apprehended, he had attempted to flee. There was an independent reason for the flight in that defendant was an escapee. In a prior appeal, the court had instructed the trial court on remand to exclude such evidence. The State admitted that it could not and did not give the jury an instruction on flight because the evidence of the flight was probative of things other than his guilt or guilty knowledge. The flight evidence was improperly admitted. The error was not harmless. The court also held that the trial court erred in excluding the testimony of a witness who had been convicted of perjury. The perjury conviction could have been used for impeachment purposes, but the witness was competent to testify and the veracity of his testimony was an issue for the jury to consider.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's capital murder conviction and remanded the matter for a new trial.

Warren v. Mississippi Workers' Compensation Comm'n


No. 95-CC-00595-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


700 So. 2d 608; 1997 Miss. LEXIS 496



October 9, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/09/95. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. DENISE SWEET OWENS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff claimants under the Mississippi Workers' Compensation scheme, Miss. Code Ann. § 71-3-1 et seq., sought review of an order from the Hinds County Chancery Court (Mississippi) which denied the request of claimants, who were injured workers, to strike down the workers' compensation scheme as unconstitutional due to the characteristically long delays in the resolution of claims.


OVERVIEW: In this case the court considered the constitutionality of the Mississippi Workers' Compensation scheme. Because the claimants failed to demonstrate in the record that characteristic delays caused any constitutional injury, the court affirmed the trial court's decision to uphold the Workers' Compensation scheme. In addressing the claimants' argument that the delays in the system under Miss. Code Ann. § 71-3-1 et seq. violated their rights to due process, the court stated that an act of the legislature had to appear beyond all reasonable doubt to violate the United States Constitution before being struck down. This standard was not met by the claimants as any delay in the adjudication of claims after they were taken into the circuit court could not have been attributed to the workers' compensation system, many of the delays complained of were the result of the claimants' own actions or inactions, and even if there was some inherent delay in the workers' compensation system, none of the claimants proved that such inherent delays followed a state-imposed deprivation of an established right to benefits that was executed against them without notice or opportunity to be heard.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order which denied the relief sought by the claimants and declined to strike down the Mississippi workers' compensation scheme.

Whitfield v. State


No. 96-CA-00123-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


1997 Miss. LEXIS 499



October 9, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION


PRIOR HISTORY: DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/21/95. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. R. KENNETH COLEMAN. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: CHICKASAW COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Chickasaw County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which denied her petition for post-conviction relief upon her conviction on three counts of the sale of a controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to three charges of the sale of a controlled substance, cocaine. She subsequently filed a petition to vacate and set aside the convictions. The circuit court denied defendant post-conviction relief, and she appealed. Upon review, the court reversed the judgment and remanded the cause for further proceedings. The court held that the circuit court erred in allowing defendant to plead guilty and be sentenced without an indictment and without a valid waiver of indictment. A criminal defendant should not be proceeded against criminally for a felony unless defendant was properly indicted by the grand jury or waived such indictment by a sworn statement. There was neither in the present action. Defendant was not indicted and did not execute a valid waiver of indictment until after she had entered her plea and had been sentenced by the circuit court. Miss. Const. art. III, § 27(1890), required an indictment before the prosecution for felonies unless one of the noted exceptions existed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

 

761 of 825 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mississippi Ass'n of Supervisors


No. 95-CA-01083-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


699 So. 2d 1221; 1997 Miss. LEXIS 448



September 25, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/16/95. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT LEWIS GIBBS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state challenged a decision from the Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which granted appellee county board of supervisors' (boards) motion for summary judgment and declared that an amendment to Miss. Code Ann. §§ 27-19-81, 63-5-33, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The state legislature passed a bill that amended Miss. Code Ann. §§ 27-19-81, 63-5-33, and allowed vehicles that hauled sand, gravel, and agricultural products to apply for a harvest permit to operate on non-federal highways at a maximum weight. The boards brought an action to have the bill declared unconstitutional. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the boards. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court stated that under prior case law the legislature could regulate the boards in their exercise of discretion so long as it did not remove that discretion in any way. The court stated that under the legislation the boards had no discretion to veto any operator's right to travel on the ground that the load carried was to heavy. The court stated that the bill was unconstitutional because it removed the boards' discretion in violation of Miss. Const. art. 6, § 170 (1890).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of the boards' motion for summary judgment that declared a state bill unconstitutional.

 

762 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Evans v. State


No. 93-DP-01173-SCT CONSOLIDATED WITH No. 94-CA-00176-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


725 So. 2d 613; 1997 Miss. LEXIS 389



September 11, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 9/18/93. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. KOSTA N. VLAHOS.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION OF CAPITAL MURDER AND SENTENCE OF DEATH AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted for capital murder with the underlying felonies of kidnapping and sexual battery. The venue was changed for the limited purposes of jury selection, and defendant was subsequently convicted in the Harrison County Circuit Court (Mississippi). Defendant appealed from his conviction and death sentence citing numerous errors.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction arose out of the kidnapping, rape, and murder of a 10 year old girl. Among the numerous issues that defendant raised, he contended that his statements should not have been admitted, that his federal kidnapping conviction precluded another conviction in state court, and that the judge should have been disqualified for being a defendant in a separate federal action. The court held that defendant waived his right to remain silent against the advice of his attorney and a magistrate and that the statements made to officers were not excludable plea negotiations. The court also held that Miss. Code Ann. § 99-11-27, and the doctrine of double jeopardy, did not prevent defendant from being convicted of kidnapping after being convicted of the same offense in federal court. Moreover, the court held that kidnapping could be accomplished by deceiving the child and her mother. Finally, the court held that the judge was not disqualified merely by naming him as a defendant in an in forma pauperis federal civil rights action. Approving the in forma pauperis application was not proof that judge had a conflict without some evidence to show that judge was biased or unqualified.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and death sentence.

 

763 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Cities of Oxford, Carthage, Louisville, Starkville & Tupelo v. Northeast Miss. Elec. Power Ass'n


No. 95-CA-01261-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


704 So. 2d 59; 1997 Miss. LEXIS 386



September 11, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected September 30, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LAFAYETTE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. R. KENNETH COLEMAN. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/24/95.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff municipalities appealed the decision of the Lafayette County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which granted defendant utilities' motion for summary judgment in the municipalities' declaratory judgment action. In the declaratory judgment action, the municipalities had sought, inter alia, to have the 1987 amendments to Miss. Code Ann. §§ 77-3-13, 77-3-17, 77-3-21 (1972) (1987 amendments) declared unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The municipalities filed a declaratory judgment action against the utilities, arguing that the 1987 amendments were unconstitutional because they had revised the Mississippi Public Utilities Act of 1956, Miss. Code Ann. § 77-3-1 et seq. (1972), so as to allow the utilities to abridge the eminent domain rights of the municipalities in violation of Miss. Const. art. 7, § 190. The trial court granted summary judgment to the utilities. On appeal, the municipalities reiterated their constitutional argument and sought reconsideration of a series of decisions which held that certificates of public convenience and necessity granted to power companies were exclusive. The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to the utilities for several reasons. First, the proper forum for the issue raised by the municipalities was the legislature. Second, the 1987 amendments did not abridge the municipalities' powers of eminent domain because they had no such powers unless granted by the legislature. Finally, the grant of a certificate of public convenience and necessity to a power company was exclusive so long as it was providing adequate service in the area covered by the certificate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision granting the utilities' motion for summary judgment in the municipalities' action challenging the constitutionality of certain amendments to the Mississippi Public Utilities Act of 1956.

Holland v. State


NO. 93-DP-00494-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


705 So. 2d 307; 1997 Miss. LEXIS 388



September 11, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected January 21, 1998. As Corrected January 22, 1998.
Rehearing denied by Holland v. State, 706 So. 2d 252, 1998 Miss. LEXIS 30 (Miss., 1998)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Holland v. Mississippi, 525 U.S. 829, 119 S. Ct. 80, 142 L. Ed. 2d 63, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 5017 (1998)
Post-conviction relief denied at Holland v. State, 878 So. 2d 1, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 413 (Miss., 2004)
Motion granted by, Motion denied by Holland v. State, 2010 Miss. LEXIS 241 (Miss., May 13, 2010)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Motion denied by Knox v. State, 2010 Miss. LEXIS 263 (Miss., May 20, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 4/2/93. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. KOSTA N. VLAHOS.

Reported in Table Case Format at: 1998 Miss. LEXIS 30.
Holland v. State, 587 So. 2d 848, 1991 Miss. LEXIS 648 (Miss., 1991)



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION OF CAPITAL MURDER AND SENTENCE OF DEATH AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of Harrison County (Mississippi) of capital murder committed during the underlying crime of rape, and was sentenced to death. On appeal, the conviction of capital murder was affirmed but the death penalty was vacated and the case remanded for resentencing. A resentencing jury imposed the death penalty. The defendant's appeal was consolidated with the mandatory review of the death sentence.


OVERVIEW: The court rejected defendant's claims that the statute permitted the death penalty for certain felony murders without a finding of intent to kill but not for premeditated murder and that the statutory classifications violated the Eighth and Fourteenth Amendments. Evidence defendant offered as mitigation, which was nothing more than an attempt to relitigate the prior finding of guilt, was properly excluded, including testimony of a serologist that the rape did not occur. Defendant could not argue residual or whimsical doubt to the resentencing jury, which had not convicted him. There was no error in admitting evidence of the result of the guilt phase because it was not a separate trial. The victim's criminal history was not material to defendant's conduct and was inadmissible. Defendant did not prove a substantial need for a mental examination. A change of venue for resentencing was not required due to the lapse of time since the original trial. Potential jurors could not be asked what weight they would give to certain mitigating factors. It was proper for a forensic pathologist to testify about the victim's injuries and the trauma such injuries produced.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of capital murder and the sentence of death.

Carpenter v. City of Petal


No. 95-CA-00359-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


699 So. 2d 928; 1997 Miss. LEXIS 382



September 11, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: FORREST COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 03/03/95. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. RICHARD WAYNE MCKENZIE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner challenged the judgment of the Forrest County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which dismissed his bill of exceptions after appellee city, pursuant to Petal, Miss., Ordinance 1979(42), § 6.113, denied his request for a zoning variance to permit him to install a mobile home on his farm.


OVERVIEW: After the property owner requested a variance from the zoning provisions of § 6.113 so that he could place a mobile home on his farm, the city denied his request, and the property owner filed a bill of exceptions in circuit court. When the circuit court dismissed his bill of exceptions, the property owner appealed. The court reversed, holding that he was denied due process because he did not receive a full and fair opportunity to respond to the concerns raised by the opponents to his variance and, consequently, was denied the opportunity to be heard at all critical stages of the process. Further, the court found that the city's decision to restrict the location of mobile homes to approved mobile home parks was a legitimate effort to achieve the governmental goal of protecting property values. However, that objective could not justify the ordinance's restriction of manufactured homes from all residential areas, especially in light of the improvement of modern manufactured homes, the steps that could minimize the negative impact, and the overall oppressive impact of the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that dismissed the property owner's bill of exceptions to the city's denial of his request for a zoning variance to permit him to install a mobile home on his farm.

Booker v. State


No. 92-KA-00877-SCT CONSOLIDATED WITH 93-DP-00671-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


699 So. 2d 132; 1997 Miss. LEXIS 375



September 4, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: TATE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/16/90. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ANDREW CLEVELAND BAKER.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to capital murder and was sentenced to death. The United States Supreme Court granted certiorari, vacated the judgment, and remanded the matter for reconsideration, after which the court affirmed the conviction and sentence a second time. Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Tate County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which denied his motion for post-conviction relief as to his guilty plea and appeal of his sentence.


OVERVIEW: In considering defendant's motion to vacate judgment and sentence, the circuit court considered guilty plea issues but found them time-barred by the statute of limitations for filing a motion within three years following the entry of a guilty plea under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-5(2). The court reversed the decision denying post-conviction relief on the guilt phase issues and remanded for consideration on the merits of those issues. The court reversed the death sentence and remanded for resentencing. The court found that § 99-39-5(2) provided three years in which to file a petition for post-conviction relief where a direct appeal was taken, as was taken by defendant, and that the guilty plea did not alter such result. The court found that the failure of the circuit court to supply the jury with a properly limiting definition of "especially heinous, atrocious or cruel" to accompany the aggravating factor was error requiring remand for a new sentencing hearing. Further, the court held that while it was not error to have instructed the jury that the capital murder was committed on two aggravating factors, robbery and pecuniary gain, at sentencing, it should not be done at resentencing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's decision that denied post-conviction relief on the guilt phase issues and remanded those issues, and the court reversed the death sentence and remanded for resentencing with a properly limiting definition of an unconstitutionally vague aggravating factor and without an instruction that the murder was committed on two aggravating factors.

Smith v. City of Picayune


No. 95-KA-00444-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


701 So. 2d 1101; 1997 Miss. LEXIS 379



September 4, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: PEARL RIVER COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 04/07/95. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. MICHAEL RAY EUBANKS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Pearl River County Circuit Court (Mississippi) after he was convicted of disorderly conduct in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-35-7(1) (1972). Defendant contested the constitutionality of § 97-35-7(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant, an owner of an arcade, learned of a disturbance in his adjoining parking lot, so he went to the parking lot, carrying a baseball bat. Two police officers arrived at approximately the same time and ordered defendant to leave the parking lot. When defendant refused, he was placed under arrest. On appeal from his disorderly conduct conviction, defendant contended that § 97-35-7(1) was unconstitutional because, among other things, it was overbroad and vague. In affirming defendant's conviction, the court held that § 97-35-7(1) was not unconstitutional as applied to defendant's case. The court noted that disorderly conduct ordinances often made resort to broadly stated definitions and prohibitions and that such resort was difficult to avoid. However, § 97-35-7(1) provided defendant with adequate notice that the failure to obey a police order under such circumstances could have resulted in arrest. The case concerned the right of a police officer to control conduct, the carrying of a baseball bat, that greatly increased the potential for sudden violence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Sunflower County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him of taking contraband onto penitentiary grounds and imposed a sentence. Defendant alleged that the trial judge erred when it refused to rule on motions in limine seeking to bar the introduction of the fruits of a poisonous trees.

On appeal, the court reversed and held that the trial court should have considered defendant's motions under the circumstances and because there was no cut-off date for motions set.

770 of 825 DOCUMENTS


State v. Roderick


No. 95-KA-00701-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


704 So. 2d 49; 1997 Miss. LEXIS 313



August 7, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 06/16/95. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT H. WALKER.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Mississippi challenged a judgment from the Harrison County, Circuit Court (Mississippi), which granted defendants' motion to quash and dismiss the indictment against them for violation of the Mississippi's RICO Act, specifically Miss. Code Ann. § 97-43-5(3).


OVERVIEW: Defendants were indicted for violation of § 97-43-5(3). The indictment charged that they were engaged in a pattern of collecting unlawful debt through a check cashing business. Defendants filed a motion to quash and dismiss the indictment arguing that the application of the RICO Act to usury was unconstitutionally vague. The trial court granted their motion and the state appealed. The court granted review. A statute was unconstitutionally vague if it forbid or required the doing of an act in terms so vague that men of common intelligence had to necessarily guess at its meaning and differed as to its application. Defendants made an effort to determine whether they were in compliance with Mississippi law, and yet were unable to find that their business violated Mississippi's RICO Act. Any other person of common intelligence reading RICO and the laws governing usury in Mississippi would have been unable to ascertain that usury was criminally barred by RICO. As a result, the court affirmed the circuit court's order finding that Mississippi's RICO Act was unconstitutionally vague as applied to usury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court that granted defendants' motion to dismiss the indictment because the application of the state's RICO Act to usury was unconstitutionally vague.

Autry v. State


No. 95-CA-00357-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


698 So. 2d 84; 1997 Miss. LEXIS 305



July 31, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: February 27, 1995. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. R. KENNETH COLEMAN. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: MARSHALL COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a bail bondsman, sought review of an order of the Marshall County Circuit Court (Mississippi) which overruled his motion for relief from judgment. That judgment was rendered in appellee county's action seeking to forfeit an appearance bond after the principal failed to appear for a hearing.


OVERVIEW: The bondsman entered into an appearance bond on behalf of the principal. The bond was headed in the name of a bond service and three names appeared below the signature line, one of which was the bondsman's name. The bond was signed by the bondsman. The principal failed to appear in court on a specified date and the trial court entered judgment nisi against the principal, the bond service, and the bondsman. Subsequently, final judgment on the bond was entered against the bond service. The principal was later captured. The bondsman filed a motion for relief from judgment 23 months after the final judgment on the bond was entered. The trial court overruled the motion based on the fact that it was not filed with the 12-month limitation period in Miss. Code Ann. § 83-39-7. On appeal, the order was affirmed. The court rejected the bondsman argument that the trial court did not have personal jurisdiction over him because the judgment nisi and scire facias were served on an unauthorized agent. He ratified the agent through his inaction and payment of the bond. Section 83-39-7 was not unconstitutional on its face or as applied to the bondsman. It was a valid statute of limitations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order.

Seward v. State

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Harrison County Circuit Court (Mississippi) of felony driving under the influence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was observed by a police officer driving in an erratic manner. The officer ascertained that defendant's driver's license was suspended and when defendant pulled into a convenience store, questioned him and placed him under arrest. Defendant had been convicted of two prior offenses of driving under the influence and after the jury found that he had been driving under the influence, he was convicted of felony driving under the influence since it was his third offense. On appeal, the court held that defendant was barred from raising any issues that he had not objected to at trial. The court found that the failure to notify defendant that a refusal to take a breathalyzer test would result in a suspension of his license was not to be remedied through a reversal of his conviction, but would have warranted a reversal of his suspension. The court ruled that the trial court had not erred in refusing to give jury instructions requested by defendant because the requests were either incorrect statements of law or were addressed in other instructions.


OUTCOME: The court, finding that defendant's claims lacked merit, affirmed his conviction of felony driving under the influence.

Allstate Ins. Co. v. McGory


No. 94-CA-00494-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


697 So. 2d 1171; 1997 Miss. LEXIS 303



July 24, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: December 28, 1993. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. FRANK ALLISON RUSSELL. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LEE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In response to appellant insurer's declaratory action, appellee insured counterclaimed for bad faith refusal to pay a claim. The Lee County Circuit Court (Mississippi) ruled that the jury verdict in favor of the insurer was against the great weight of evidence and granted the insured a new trial. At the new trial, the circuit court granted the insured's motion for a directed verdict but refused to consider punitive damages. Both parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: The insurer argued that the trial court erred in granting a new trial when the jury found for the insurer and subsequent directed verdict for the insured. The insured contended that the issue of punitive damages should have been considered given the insurer's alleged bad faith and misconduct. The court held that wilful incendiarism by an insured was a defense to the insurer's liability. However, the insurer had to prove the elements of its claim by clear and convincing evidence. The elements were 1) incendiary fire, 2) motive of the insured, and 3) the insured's opportunity to set the fire. The court found that there was absolutely no evidence that the insured had the opportunity to set the fire or arrange for its being set. Therefore, the trial judge correctly granted the insured's motion for a directed verdict because the insurer failed to present any evidence for the jury to consider on the element of opportunity. The court noted that the insured failed to raise the ruling denying punitive damages on the first appeal of the case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Gressett by & Through Gressett v. Newton Separate Mun. Sch. Dist.


No. 94-CA-00940-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


697 So. 2d 444; 1997 Miss. LEXIS 326



July 17, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected August 6, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: NEWTON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/02/94. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. MARCUS D. GORDON.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant high school student challenged the judgment of the Newton County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which dismissed his negligence lawsuit against appellee school district on sovereign immunity grounds.


OVERVIEW: A high school student was attacked by another student. After the attack, he sued his school district, claiming that the latter had negligently failed to protect him from the attack. The school district moved to dismiss the complaint, contending it was immune from liability since it was a political subdivision of the state. The judge assigned the case agreed, and granted the motion. The high school student appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed. It held that its earlier law declaring unconstitutional a state statute's attempted retrospective application did not apply, inasmuch as in this case another state law was later enacted that covered this precise situation. Under that statute, in effect at the time of the attack, the school district was immune from liability.


OUTCOME: The judgment, dismissing the high school student's negligence lawsuit, was affirmed.

Christmas v. State


No. 93-KA-01164-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


700 So. 2d 262; 1997 Miss. LEXIS 246



June 12, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 7594 from Judgment dated MARCH 15, 1993, James E. Thomas RULING JUDGE, Hancock County Circuit Court.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION OF TOUCHING A CHILD FOR LUSTFUL PURPOSES AND SENTENCE OF SIX (6) YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Hancock County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him of fondling a 12-year old girl. Defendant claimed that he was convicted under an ex post facto law, and that the trial court permitted the jury to find guilt on a preponderance of the evidence rather than guilt beyond a reasonable doubt.


OVERVIEW: In June, 1989, defendant fondled a young girl. In April, 1989, the statute of limitations of Miss. Code Ann. § 99-1-5 was two years. In April, 1989, the limitation period was amended to seven years, effective July, 1989. The child was silent until 1992, when she told her parents. Defendant was convicted in a jury trial of fondling, in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-5-23, and sought review on the grounds that he was convicted under an ex post facto law, and that the trial court permitted the jury to convict on a preponderance of the evidence, rather than guilt beyond a reasonable doubt. The court held that: (1) the statute of limitations, contained in a separate act, was procedural and not substantive; (2) at the time the statute was amended, the prior limitation period had not expired; (3) the amendment did not change the definition or punishment of the crime, and was not ex post facto under Miss. Const. § 16 (1890), U.S. Const. art. I, §§ 9, 10; (4) the jury was properly instructed, and distinctions between reasonable doubt, all possible doubt, beyond a shadow of a doubt, while not proper in jury instructions, were permissible in closing argument.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of touching a child for lustful purposes because his conviction was not ex post facto and the jury was properly instructed.

Wright v. White


No. 94-CA-00269-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


693 So. 2d 898; 1997 Miss. LEXIS 160



May 8, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 9375462CV from Judgment dated FEBRUARY 09, 1994, Robert Lewis Gibbs RULING JUDGE, Hinds County Cicuit Court, First Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employees appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of the First Judicial District of Hinds County (Mississippi), which vacated an order in which the Employee Appeals Board (EAB) transferred a pending state civil service employment matter to circuit court for disposition, as beyond the statutory authority of the EAB, and dismissed the employees' complaint predicated on that transfer.


OVERVIEW: The employees brought an action before the EAB, but before completing that proceeding, they filed an original suit in a circuit court. The EAB then transferred the matter to the circuit court and relinquished jurisdiction. The circuit court vacated the EAB's order of transfer and dismissed the complaint. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the EAB was wholly competent to consider every claim asserted and no aspect of the statutes creating the EAB gave it authority to transfer a pending state employment matter to circuit court. Nothing in the record indicated that the employees ever argued that the state civil service statute was pre-empted by 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and was in violation of the federal Constitution. The record on appeal indicated that a post-judgment motion for reconsideration was itself untimely and the circuit court was without any jurisdiction to consider the new arguments advanced if it had wanted to. The employees were procedurally barred from arguing on appeal that the state civil service statute was pre-empted by 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OUTCOME: The judgment vacating the EAB's order of transfer and dismissing the employees' complaint was affirmed.

Benedict v. City of Hattiesburg


NO. 93-CA-00259-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


693 So. 2d 377; 1997 Miss. LEXIS 161



May 8, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 53611D from Judgment dated FEBRUARY 03, 1993, Sebe Dale Jr. RULING JUDGE, Forrest County Chancery Court.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED FOR PROCEEDINGS NOT INCONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant voter challenged a decision of the Forrest County Chancery Court (Mississippi), which dismissed his action against appellees, city and election commissioners, seeking a declaratory judgment and injunctive relief and alleging that the election on the question of permitting or prohibiting the use, possession, and sale of alcoholic beverages in the area was without legal authority.


OVERVIEW: Prior to completion of the election on the question of permitting the use, possession, and sale of alcoholic beverages in the area, the voter brought a complaint against the city and election commissioners, seeking declaratory and injunctive relief and alleging that the election was without legal authority. The city and election commissioners brought a motion to dismiss the action. The chancery court dismissed for lack of subject matter jurisdiction, and the voter appealed. The court held that the chancery court lacked subject matter jurisdiction over the voter's action because the statute directing that appeals from judgments or decisions of municipal authorities were to be taken to the circuit court, Miss. Code Ann. § 11-51-75 (1972), provided the exclusive remedy for the voter. The court found that the chancery court's action in dismissing the case over which it lacked subject matter jurisdiction was manifest error, and that the proper remedy would have been to transfer the case to the circuit court which had jurisdiction. The judgment was reversed and remanded.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the chancery court's dismissal of the voter's action challenging the legality of the election held by the city and election commissioners for lack of subject matter jurisdiction because the chancery court should have transferred the action to circuit court.

Martin v. Coop


No. 95-CA-01174-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


693 So. 2d 912; 1997 Miss. LEXIS 169; 69 A.L.R.5th 685



May 8, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 95177 from Judgment dated AUGUST 22, 1995, Percy Lee Lynchard Jr. RULING JUDGE, DeSoto County Chancery Court.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED FOR PROCEEDINGS NOT INCONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of a decree from the DeSoto County Chancery Court (Mississippi), which awarded appellee grandparents visitation of their minor grandson pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 93-16-1 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The grandparents filed a petition for visitation of their minor grandson pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 93-16-1 et seq. The grandparents were the parents of the child's deceased father. The trial court entered a decree awarding visitation of the child to the grandparents. On appeal, the mother contended that the amount of visitation granted to the grandparents was excessive and thus not in the best interests of the child. The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case. The court held that: (1) all the proof necessary under Miss. Code Ann. § 93-16-3(1) was present and therefore the grandparents should be awarded visitation; (2) the trial court abused its discretion in awarding the grandparents the same visitation that it would award to a non-custodial parent; (3) natural grandparents did not have a right to visit their grandchildren that was as comprehensive as the rights of a parent; and (4) visitation granted to grandparents should not be equivalent to that which would be granted to a non-custodial parent unless the circumstances overwhelmingly dictated that it should be.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decree of the trial court, which had awarded visitation of the grandchild to the grandparents, and remanded the case.

Bullock v. Mississippi Empl. Sec. Comm'n


NO. 93-CC-01036-SCT CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 94-CC-00840-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


697 So. 2d 1147; 1997 Miss. LEXIS 167



May 8, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 93574 from Judgment dated SEPTEMBER 02, 1993, Billy Joe Landrum RULING JUDGE, Jones County Circuit Court, Second Judicial District.

Appeal No. 9311154 from Judgment dated AUGUST 11, 1994, Billy Joe Landrum RULING JUDGE, Jones County Circuit Court, Second Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT IS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a civil service employee, was terminated by appellee city under Miss. Code Ann. § 21-31-27 and § 21-31-75 (1972) after he qualified to run for a mayor, and his termination was upheld by the civil service commission and the Jones County Circuit Court, Second Judicial District (Mississippi). His claim for unemployment compensation was denied by appellee employment security commission and the circuit court, and he appealed both judgments.


OVERVIEW: The employee was an administrative employee of the city when he qualified to run for the office of mayor of the city. The incumbent mayor then terminated his employment on the basis that running for a local office was grounds for removal, and the termination was upheld on appeal. The court first noted that Miss. Code Ann. § 21-31-27 (1972), one of the statutory authorities that the mayor relied upon, did not apply to the employee because § 21-31-27 only applied to employees of fire and police departments. The employee argued that the mayor's other statutory authority, Miss. Code Ann. § 21-31-75 (1972), prohibited the employee from campaigning for another candidate, but did not prohibit him for running for office himself. The court ruled that a reasonable interpretation of the legislative intent of § 21-31-75 prohibited the employee from running for office while he served in a civil service position, and thus his termination precluded him from receiving unemployment compensation benefits. The court rejected the employee's argument that § 21-31-75 was overly broad because it might be unconstitutional as to other persons because he did not have standing to make that argument.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of the circuit court.

 

780 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Esco v. Blackmon


No. 96-CC-00097-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


692 So. 2d 74; 1997 Miss. LEXIS 156



April 17, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. CI950146 from Judgment dated JANUARY 25, 1996, RULING JUDGE, Mississippi Legislature House of Representatives.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT IS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a candidate for election to the Mississippi House of Representatives, sought review of a decision of the Mississippi Legislature House of Representatives, which unconditionally seated appellee, another candidate, as a duly elected member of the House.


OVERVIEW: Appellant claimed that the House had no jurisdiction to conduct a hearing regarding his election contest because he had never been a member and that the legislature denied him due process to meaningfully pursue his election contest. Appellant lost the election but claimed that photocopies of ballots had been used, which was inappropriate because voting machines would not register them. He also alleged that poll workers gave false instructions and that appellee's aides unduly influenced voters. The court held that: (1) the legislature's conduct of the election contest under Mississippi Election Code § 23-15-955 was not an illegal election of its own members because it merely examined the elective process to decide whether illegal or corrupt practices took place; (2) Mississippi Election Code § 23-15-957 gave the legislature the power to compel testimony and the production of documents in an election contest, so the legislature had jurisdiction to interview a county election commission and hear from the parties; (3) the legislature was a proper forum; and (4) the proceedings did not violate appellant's due process rights because he voluntarily submitted himself and had a hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the House.

 

781 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Lester v. State


No. 93-DP-00619-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


692 So. 2d 755; 1997 Miss. LEXIS 143



April 10, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Modified May 15, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal No. 921012 from Judgment dated MARCH 01, 1993, William F. Coleman RULING JUDGE, Hinds County Circuit Court, First Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED TO THE CIRCUIT COURT OF HINDS COUNTY FOR A NEW TRIAL.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found the defendant guilty of the capital murder of his one-year-old daughter in the course of felonious child abuse, Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-19(2)(f). Upon the jury's vote that the death penalty be imposed, the Hinds County Circuit Court, First Judicial District (Mississippi) sentenced the defendant to death by lethal injection. The defendant filed 35 separate errors for appellate review.


OVERVIEW: The defendant was indicted for the capital murder of his baby daughter in the course of felonious child abuse in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-19(2)(f). Two days into the trial, the circuit court granted the prosecution's motion to amend the indictment to include abuse during the time period occurring in the four months before the baby died. The defendant was found guilty and ordered put to death by lethal injection. On appeal, the court noted that most of the issues raised were either procedurally barred or without merit, however, the conviction and sentence was reversed, and a new trial was ordered because the trial court committed reversible error in allowing the indictment to be substantially amended by adding the additional time period and additional instances of battery, it abused its discretion in refusing the defendant's request for a continuance in order to adequately prepare a defense of the surprise introduction of sexual abuse evidence, and the combined effect of the prosecutor's improper, irrelevant, and prejudicial cross-examination and closing argument unfairly prejudiced the defendant in the eyes of the jury.


OUTCOME: The conviction of capital murder and sentence of death by lethal injection was reversed based upon the trial court's err in ordering an amendment to the indictment on the second day of trial, the prosecutor's improper, irrelevant, and prejudicial cross-examination and closing argument, and the denial of a continuance after improper evidence of child sexual abuse was admitted. The case was remanded for a new trial.

Mississippi Gaming Comm'n v. Board of Educ.


No. 95-CA-00133-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


691 So. 2d 452; 1997 Miss. LEXIS 89



March 20, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. A24019400211 from Judgment dated DECEMBER 30, 1994, James E. Thomas RULING JUDGE, Harrison County Circuit Court, First Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: REVERSE THE ORDER OF THE CIRCUIT COURT AND REINSTATE THE COMMISSION'S DECISION.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Mississippi Gaming Commission sought review of a judgment that was entered by the Harrison County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which reversed the commission's decision to deny a preliminary site approval plan that was filed by petitioners, a casino corporation and a board of education.


OVERVIEW: The commission denied petitioners' preliminary site plan after it determined that the tract of land was located on a bayou and was not a legal gambling site under Mississippi Gaming Commission Regulation No. 2 (1990). Petitioners contended that neither state statutes nor Regulation No. 2 prohibited gaming operations on the proposed site. They also argued that if Regulation No. 2 was found to bar development of the site, it should be declared void and in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-33-1 (1993). The commission argued that the circuit court lacked jurisdiction over the matter because preliminary site approval was not statutorily subject to appeals. In reversing the judgment, the court held that (1) the circuit court had jurisdiction to entertain the casino corporation's appeal of the commission's denial of its preliminary site request, (2) the board of education had standing in the action, (3) the circuit court erred in ruling that the commission exceeded its authority in determining that the bayou was not a proper gaming site, and (4) the circuit court erred in concluding that the commission's decision was arbitrary, capricious and unsupported by the evidence.


OUTCOME: The order of the circuit court, which reversed the commission's decision to deny petitioners' application for a preliminary site approval to build a casino, was reversed, in petitioners' action to review that decision.

THIS SENTENCE SHALL BE CONSECUTIVE TO THE SENTENCE IMPOSED BY THE CIRCUIT COURT OF RANKIN COUNTY IN CAUSE NUMBER 94-DP-00760-SCT. OUTCOME: The court dismissed the arguments raised by defendant for lack of merit, and affirmed the conviction and death sentence. The court held that, considering the crime, the death sentence imposed upon this defendant was not excessive or disproportionate.

Stokes v. Kemper County Bd. of Supervisors


No. 94-CA-00949-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


691 So. 2d 391; 1997 Miss. LEXIS 102



March 6, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 3742 from Judgment dated AUGUST 24, 1994, ROBERT W. BAILEY RULING JUDGE, Kemper County Circuit Court.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT TO AS KEMPER COUNTY BOARD OF SUPERVISORS IS AFFIRMED. JUDGMENT AS TO JAMES WILSON IS REVERSED AND REMANDED FOR TRIAL.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff driver appealed an order of the Kemper County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which granted defendants, county employee and board of supervisors (board), immunity and summary judgment dismissing the negligence action.


OVERVIEW: A driver was injured when a county employee, acting in the scope of his employment, drove his truck into the path of the driver's vehicle. The driver alleged that the county employee's negligent failure to yield the right of way was imputed to his county employer. The trial court granted the motion of the county employee and board for summary judgment dismissing the driver's negligence action. The driver appealed. The court affirmed summary judgment for the board. The court held that the board was protected by legislative sovereign immunity from the action, which arose in 1991, did not involve any actions by the board, and was an attempt to sue the county while avoiding the harsher sovereign immunity law. The board qualified as a state subdivision and escaped the governmental-proprietary distinction applied to municipalities. The court reversed and remanded for trial against the county employee because sovereign or public official immunity provided no protection for an individual performing the ministerial act of driving a car.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the driver's negligence action against the board and reversed the dismissal of the action against the employee and remanded for trial.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction from the trial court in DeSoto County (Mississippi), which convicted him of three counts of capital murder in the course of robbery, burglary, and kidnapping respectively.


OVERVIEW: A family was found murdered in their burning home. Defendant was arrested and charged with capital murder. Defendant confessed to the murders but later tried to suppress the confession, saying he was scared. Before trial, venue was transferred to one county, after which the trial court denied defendant's request for another change of venue. Defendant was tried and convicted of capital murder and sentenced to death. The court affirmed the convictions. The court found neither error nor a constitutional violation in admitting defendant's confession nor in refusing defendant's proposed instruction on the weight to be given his confession. There was no error in refusing to allow defendant's family members to testify on the effect that his execution would have on their lives.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's capital murder convictions and death sentences.

Board of Trustees v. Knox


No. 94-CA-00394-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI

February 13, 1997, Decided

DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Board of Trustees challenged an order from the Hinds County Chancery Court, First Judicial District (Mississippi) that reversed the suspension of appellee school principal for "other good cause" pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 37-9-59.


OVERVIEW: The board suspended the principal from his duties after he permitted the reading of prayers over the high school intercom despite counsel's advice that this action was unconstitutional. The trial court reversed this suspension, but on appeal, the court reversed the trial court's decision. The court held that the actions of the principal in disregarding the legal advice of the staff attorney and in proceeding with the reading of school prayers despite a lack of urgency constituted "other good cause" in support of suspension. The dismissal was supported by substantial evidence and was not arbitrary and capricious. The trial judge incorrectly based his ruling in part upon his own strongly held personal views on school prayer.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order that reversed the suspension of the school principal after he permitted the reading of prayers over the high school intercom.

Herring v. State


No. 93-KA-01183-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


691 So. 2d 948; 1997 Miss. LEXIS 37



February 13, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Herring v. State, 693 So. 2d 384, 1997 Miss. LEXIS 208 (Miss., 1997)

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. CR9011CP2 from Judgment date OCTOBER 08, 1993, George C. Carlson Jr. RULING JUDGE, Panola County Circuit Court, Second Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: COUNT I: CONVICTION OF CONSPIRACY TO SELL COCAINE AND SENTENCE TO TWENTY (20) YEARS IN THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS AFFIRMED. COUNT II: CONVICTION OF SALE OF COCAINE AND SENTENCE TO THIRTY (30) YEARS IN THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS AFFIRMED; THIS SENTENCE SHALL RUN CONSECUTIVE TO THE SENTENCE IMPOSED IN COUNT I. COUNT III: CONVICTION OF SALE OF COCAINE AND SENTENCE TO SERVE THIRTY (30) YEARS IN THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS AFFIRMED; THIS SENTENCE SHALL RUN CONSECUTIVE TO THE SENTENCE IMPOSED IN COUNT II. CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Panola County Circuit Court, Second Judicial District (Mississippi), which convicted him of one count of conspiracy to sell a controlled substance in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-1-1(a) and two counts of sale of a controlled substance in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-139(a)(1). His case had been transferred from the county youth court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of conspiracy to sell a controlled substance and sale of a controlled substance. The supreme court affirmed the judgment. The court held that defendant was not denied his right to a speedy trial under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-17-1 because he caused the delay by fleeing the jurisdiction and fighting extradition. Also, defendant's constitutional right to a speedy trial was not violated. The court found that defendant's statements were properly admitted. Because defendant had been arrested numerous times before, he was familiar with the procedures and could not say that he did not understand his Miranda rights. The court held that the facts, viewed in a light most favorable to the state, proved that defendant committed the offenses as charged. The verdict was not against the overwhelming weight of the evidence, and the trial court correctly denied defendant's motion for a new trial or judgment n.o.v. The court found that the sentence was not disproportionate to the crime. Thirty years was not cruel and unusual punishment for drug charges, and in light of defendant's juvenile record, the judge did not err in imposing the sentences consecutively.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed defendant's conviction for conspiracy to sell a controlled substance and sale of a controlled substance.

Mississippi Comm'n on Judicial Performance v. Russell


NO. 96-CC-00507-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


691 So. 2d 929; 1997 Miss. LEXIS 35



February 6, 1997, DECIDED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended April 8, 1997. Rehearing Denied April 10, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal No. 94146 from Judgment dated MAY 10, 1996, John C. Love Jr. RULING JUDGE, Commission On Judicial Performance.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent circuit court judge sought review of the decision of petitioner Mississippi Commission on Judicial Performance (commission) that adopted the findings of a hearing panel and recommended a public reprimand and monetary fine. The commission had charged that the judge violated Miss. Const. § 177A (1890 as amended), Miss. Code Ann. §§ 47-5-110, 99-37-19, and Miss. Code Jud. Conduct Canons 1, 2A, 2B, 3A (1)(4), 3(B).


OVERVIEW: The charges of judicial misconduct, that the commission filed against the judge, stemmed from the post-sentencing release of four inmates after the term of court during which they were sentenced. On review, the court conducted a de novo review and affirmed the commission's decision, which adopted the hearing panel's findings and recommended a public reprimand and monetary fine. The court held that the commission had jurisdiction pursuant to Miss. Jud. Performance Comm'n R. 10 because at the time the judge entered the orders releasing the prisoners he knew or should have know that he was exceeding his authority. His actions violated Miss. Const. § 177A because they constituted willful misconduct in office prejudicial to the administration of justice. The court also held that the composition of the commission was not unconstitutional because the combination of investigative and adjudicative functions did not constitute a due process violation, and there was not sufficient evidence of financial bias or motivation which would have violated due process. The doctrine of judicial immunity did not exempt the judge from professional misconduct proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the commission's decision, which adopted the hearing panel's findings. Thus, pursuant to the commission's recommendations, the court ordered public reprimand and monetary fine against the judge for judicial misconduct. The court found that the judge's actions in releasing the prisoners was excess of the authority and jurisdiction conferred upon him as a circuit court judge.

Collins v. State


No. 94-KA-00565-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


691 So. 2d 918; 1997 Miss. LEXIS 6



January 30, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected February 4, 1997. Certiorari Denied October 6, 1997, Reported at: 118 S. Ct. 198, 1997 U.S. LEXIS 5567, 139 L. Ed. 2d 135.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal No. 93103BT from Judgment dated JUNE 06, 1994, Andrew Cleveland Baker RULING JUDGE, Tate County Circuit Court.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION OF CAPITAL RAPE AND SENTENCE OF LIFE IN THE CUSTODY OF MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction by the Tate County Circuit Court (Mississippi), for capital rape, Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-65(1). Defendant claimed that the trial court erred in not instructing the jury to consider "mistake of age" as a defense to capital rape and did not instruct the jury on the offense of statutory rape. Defendant also raised a Batson claim and argued the trial court erred in accepting the reasons articulated by the state.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of capital rape after the 13 year-old victim identified him. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court held that "mistake of age" was not applicable to capital rape in Mississippi because the clear intent underlying the crime was the same as was applicable to statutory rape, the protection of children of the specified age. The core concern was that children should not be exploited for sexual purposes regardless of their consent; they simply could not appreciate the significance or the consequences of their actions. The court found that recognizing the defense of "mistake of age" would at best frustrate the purpose of the legislative enactment. The court also found that the evidentiary basis for a "mistake of age" instruction was tenuous at best because there was evidence that defendant had known the victim since she was between eight and nine years old. The court held that statutory rape was not a lesser-included offense of capital rape because statutory rape included the element that the age of the child was between 14 and 18, which was not included in capital rape, where the child had to be under 14 years old.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for capital rape.

Emil v. Miss. Bar


NO. 94-BA-00749-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


690 So. 2d 301; 1997 Miss. LEXIS 3



January 9, 1997, DECIDED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected June 12, 1997.



DISPOSITION: SANCTION OF DISBARMENT REVERSED. COMPLAINT TRIBUNAL'S FINDINGS OF MISCONDUCT FOR THE SOLICITATION OF BUSINESS AFFIRMED. GERALD R. EMIL SHALL BE PUBLICLY REPRIMANDED. COMPLAINT TRIBUNAL'S FINDINGS OF MISCONDUCT FOR SOLICITING BUSINESS AND SHARING LEGAL FEES AFFIRMED. GERALD R. EMIL IS HEREBY SUSPENDED FROM THE PRACTICE OF LAW INDEFINITELY. REINSTATEMENT OF GERALD R. EMIL IS SOLELY CONTINGENT ON PROOF FROM THE BOARD OF BAR EXAMINERS THAT HE HAS SUCCESSFULLY PASSED ALL SECTIONS OF THE MISSISSIPPI BAR EXAMINATION. WHEN THIS PROOF IS PRESENTED TO THIS COURT AN IMMEDIATE ORDER OF REINSTATEMENT FOR GERALD R. EMIL WILL ISSUE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney challenged the judgment of the Complaint Tribunal of the Supreme Court (Mississippi), which found the attorney guilty of violating certain provisions of the Mississippi Rules of Professional Conduct, and which recommended disbarment as the appropriate sanction to be imposed.


OVERVIEW: Appellee Mississippi Bar (Bar) filed a formal complaint against an attorney, alleging that the attorney violated certain provisions that prohibited solicitation of employment and of sharing legal fees with a non-attorney. The trial court denied the attorney's motions to dismiss the claim for multiplicity of counts and for prejudicial delay, as well as the attorney's motion for separate trials on each of the seven counts. The trial court denied each of the attorney's motions, found the attorney guilty, and recommended disbarment as the sanction to be imposed. The court affirmed the findings that the attorney was guilty of solicitation of employment and of sharing legal fees, but the court reversed the sanction of disbarment. The court found that the appropriate sanction for the solicitation of business was a public reprimand, and the attorney was suspended indefinitely from the practice of law, with reinstatement contingent upon the attorney's passing of the bar examination. The disciplinary proceedings were quasi-criminal, not criminal, in nature, and the attorney was not entitled to all substantive due process rights as a criminal defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the findings that the attorney was guilty of soliciting business and sharing legal fees. The court reversed the sanction of disbarment and imposed a public reprimand, as well as the indefinite suspension of the attorney from the practice of law, with reinstatement contingent upon the attorney's passing of the state bar examination.

Fordice v. Bryan


No. 94-CA-00031


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


651 So. 2d 998; 1995 Miss. LEXIS 17



January 12, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 153685 from Judgment dated DECEMBER 22, 1993, W. O. Dillard RULING JUDGE, Hinds County Chancery Court, First Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant governor sought review of a judgment from the Chancery Court of the First Judicial District of Hinds County (Mississippi), which granted appellee legislators' motion for summary judgment in a case concerning the veto power of the governor as to appropriation bills.


OVERVIEW: The governor vetoed, allowed, and amended parts of legislative bond and appropriation bills. The legislators filed a complaint and the lower court granted their motion for summary judgment and held that the veto actions of the governor were not constitutionally authorized. On appeal, the governor argued that he properly exercised his partial veto power under Miss. Const. art. IV, §73. The court affirmed the lower court judgment because the governor's action in striking the amounts and inserting his own reduced amount of bonded indebtedness was inconsistent with Miss. Const. art. IV, §§ 72, 73. In order for the bills to be susceptible to the governor's partial veto power, they had to fix a definite maximum amount and not continue to be in force longer than two months after the expiration of the fiscal year ending after the meeting of the legislature. The court held that the governor sought to veto a condition prescribed by the legislators rather than a distinct appropriation and that such action was not constitutionally authorized. The court held that the actions by the governor were a nullity and that the lower court properly granted the legislators' motion for summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court judgment that granted the legislators' motion for summary judgment.

 

793 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Mayfield v. State


No. 90-KA-448


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


612 So. 2d 1120; 1992 Miss. LEXIS 847



December 31, 1992


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Union County (Mississippi), which convicted him of two counts of vehicular homicide under Miss. Code Ann. § 63-11-30(4) (1988). Defendant contended that his convictions violated the state and federal prohibitions against double jeopardy.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was driving to a concert at the time of a wreck in which two of his friends died because he was the most sober member of the group despite being intoxicated himself. Defendant was convicted of two counts of vehicular homicide. The jury found defendant not guilty of manslaughter by culpable negligence but guilty of two counts of aggravated D.U.I. under Miss. Code Ann. § 63-11-30(4) (1988). The court reversed one of defendant's convictions and affirmed the other. Section 63-11-30(4) was truly a statute that merely proscribed the act of driving while intoxicated and was not a homicide statute and defendant's second conviction for the offense constituted double jeopardy. The court overruled Avery v. State, 555 So.2d (Miss. 1990) and held that because defendant had already been indicted when the trial court granted his motion to conduct a preliminary hearing, he could not complain on appeal concerning inadequacies in the hearing because, as an indictee, the mere grant of a hearing gave him more than the law required. The manslaughter statute under which defendant was charged, Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-47 (1972), was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court reversed one of defendant's convictions of vehicular homicide and affirmed the other.

Bolton v. State


NO. 1998-KA-01151-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


752 So. 2d 480; 1999 Miss. App. LEXIS 701



December 7, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 07/10/1998. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. RICHARD W. MCKENZIE. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: FORREST COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED ON TWO COUNTS OF ATTEMPTED ROBBERY: SENTENCED TO TWO CONSECUTIVE TERMS OF 15 YEARS IN THE MDOC.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged both his attempted robbery convictions and the 30-year sentence of confinement imposed by the Forrest County (Mississippi) Circuit Court.


OVERVIEW: Appellant appealed conviction for two counts of attempted burglary and resultant 30-year sentence of confinement. State appellate court affirmed in all respects, holding that (a) trial court did not abuse discretion in denying motion for new trial, and sufficient evidence existed given partial identification testimony of appellant as perpetrator and corroborative evidence of attempted burglary; (b) trial court's factual finding that prosecutor had not exercised peremptory challenges based on race were not clearly erroneous, thus precluding relief on that ground; (c) partial identification testimony properly admitted, inasmuch as there was no undue suggestively in its acquisition and testimony had probative value; (d) lesser offense instruction improper since factual basis for it was lacking; and (e) trial judge did not abuse his discretion at sentencing, as he considered relevant circumstances in addition to the crime and did not consider any impermissible factors.


OUTCOME: Convictions and sentences appealed; evidence was sufficient and no abuse of discretion in denying retrial, no racial discrimination by prosecution in jury selection, identification testimony was probative and not unduly suggestive, proposed lesser offense instruction lacked factual support, and sentence based only on proper factors.

 

795 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. State


NO. 1998-CP-01391-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


752 So. 2d 477; 1999 Miss. App. LEXIS 703



December 7, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 06/18/1998. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. GRAY EVANS. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: SUNFLOWER COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: MOTION GRANTED AS TO THE CALCULATION OF HIS SENTENCE AND PAROLE ELIGIBILITY; ALL OTHER CLAIMS DENIED.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order by the Sunflower County Circuit Court (Mississippi), denying his post-conviction motion after defendant was convicted of aggravated assault and sexual battery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated assault and sexual battery. The trial court denied his motion for post-conviction relief. On appeal, the court affirmed. Defendant failed to meet his burden of proof on his ineffective assistance of counsel claim because the only proof he submitted consisted of his own affidavits. Defendant's claim of insufficient evidence against him failed because defendant pleaded guilty and hence the State was not required to prove any of the essential elements of the crime. Defendant's claim that Mississippi's sexual battery statute, Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-95, was void for vagueness was contrary to clear precedent. Moreover, defendant's claims were procedurally barred, under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-21(1), because defendant did not raise them at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed because defendant was not denied effective assistance of counsel during the plea and sentencing hearings, the State was not required to prove the essential elements of the crime charged inasmuch as defendant pleaded guilty, and the sexual battery statute was not void for vagueness.
