Walton v. State


NO. 1999-CP-00171-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


752 So. 2d 452; 1999 Miss. App. LEXIS 692



November 23, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 01/05/1999. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT G. EVANS. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JASPER COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT FOR APPELLANT: PRO SE. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: 01/05/1999: .



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the Jasper County Circuit Court (MS), which denied appellant's post-conviction motions stemming from a guilty plea.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was indicted for capital murder. Appellant subsequently pled guilty to murder and was sentenced to life imprisonment with the possibility of parole after serving ten years. After sentencing by the trial court, appellant filed a motion for post-conviction collateral relief based on ineffective assistance of counsel; a petition for a free transcript of his plea; and a motion for reduction of sentence because he was not the principal actor in the crime. On appeal, the court denied all requested relief because there was no ineffective assistance of counsel, there was no right to a free transcript in a case where defendant pled guilty and there was no prejudice by not having access to such a transcript, and pursuant to 3 Miss. Code Ann. § 47-7- 3, there was no distinction between aider and abettor and a principal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of appellant's post-conviction motions because it determined that there was no merit in any of appellant's claims.

 

797 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Campbell v. State


NO. 98-KA-00083-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


749 So. 2d 1208; 1999 Miss. App. LEXIS 562



September 7, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/12/1997. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JOSEPH H. LOPER JR. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: CARROLL COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: 12/12/1997: MURDER: SENTENCED TO SERVE THE REMAINDER OF HIS NATURAL LIFE IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MDOC; SENTENCE IMPOSED IN THIS CAUSE SHALL RUN CONSECUTIVELY TO ANY SENTENCE PREVIOUSLY IMPOSED;.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction of deliberate design murder in the Carroll County Circuit Court (Mississippi).


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his jury conviction of deliberate design murder, arguing that the indictment was fatally flawed. In affirming, the court rejected defendant's argument, which was premised upon the document's failure to state the judicial district in which it was brought, taking issue with the use of the phrase "in the county, judicial district, and state aforesaid." The court concluded that this language was sufficient; the primary purpose of the indictment was to provide the accused with a description of the charges that would sufficiently enable him to prepare his defense. The court likewise rejected defendant's claim that the trial court erred in refusing to quash the indictment when it failed to contain the code subsection for deliberate design murder. "Capital murder" was limited to offenses punishable by death, not by life imprisonment; thus, deliberate design murder, punishable only by imprisonment, was not a capital murder crime.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed, as the indictment was not flawed, and the trial court did not err in refusing to quash.

 

798 of 825 DOCUMENTS


McVeay v. State


NO. 98-CA-00644-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


754 So. 2d 486; 1999 Miss. App. LEXIS 533



August 17, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JACKSON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 03/18/1998. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. EDWIN C. HARDIN. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: PCR DENIED.



DISPOSITION: THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT OF JACKSON COUNTY IS AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART FOR AN EVIDENTIARY HEARING ON THE ISSUE OF WHETHER APPELLANT'S DEFENSE COUNSEL'S PERFORMANCE IN ALLEGEDLY FAILING TO ADVISE APPELLANT CONCERNING POSSIBLE VIOLATION OF HIS CONSTITUTIONAL RIGHT TO A SPEEDY TRIAL WAS SO DEFICIENT AS TO ENTITLE APPELLANT TO WITHDRAW HIS PLEA OF GUILTY AND PROCEED APPROPRIATELY WITH A DEFENSE TO THE MERITS OF THE INDICTMENT. ALL COSTS OF THIS APPEAL ARE ASSESSED TO JACKSON COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant moved for post conviction relief from the conviction entered upon a guilty plea before the Jackson County Circuit Court (Mississippi), denied without a hearing, alleging that he was improperly sentenced under the habitual offender laws, and that it was ineffective assistance of counsel when his counsel did not pursue his speedy trial rights.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought post conviction relief, alleging numerous errors. The court affirmed the judgment in part. While defendant did not plead guilty to habitual offender charges, these charges were not counts to which he would plead separately to. Defendant waived his rights to pursue the speedy trial, double jeopardy, and defective indictment claims because he pleaded guilty. The court reversed the denial of relief from the claim of ineffective assistance of counsel. Defendant should have been counseled regarding the waiver of his speedy trial rights by pleading guilty. The guilty plea was caused by ineffective counsel, because an extremely long period passed between arrest and bringing defendant to trial. The court found the period that passed was presumptively in violation of U.S. Const. amend. VI. The court remanded for a hearing to determine what portion of the delay was chargeable to defendant, for the record contained no such information.


OUTCOME: The order denying post conviction relief was reversed to the extent that the case was remanded for a hearing to determine the extent delay was chargeable to defendant in the ineffective assistance of counsel claim related to failure to pursue speedy trial. Costs were assessed to the county.

 

799 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Briggs v. State


NO. 97-KA-01484-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


741 So. 2d 986; 1999 Miss. App. LEXIS 357



June 22, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 04/11/1997. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT G. EVANS. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: SIMPSON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: 04/11/1998: FELONY DUI (THIRD OFFENSE): SENTENCED TO SERVE A TERM OF (3) YEARS IN THE MDOC, WITH (15) MONTHS TO SERVE AND (21) MONTHS SUSPENDED AND DEFENDANT PLACED ON PROBATION, CONDITIONED UPON THE DEFENDANT UNDERGOING ALCOHOL AND DRUG TREATMENT WHILE INCARCERATED IN THE MDOC.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the Simpson County Circuit Court (Mississippi), convicting appellant for third offense of driving under the influence of alcohol. Appellant alleged that he was denied a fair and impartial jury, and that the roadblock where he was stopped, and which checked drivers' licenses and vehicle registration, was an unconstitutional means of obtaining evidence of criminal conduct.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted for third offense driving under the influence of alcohol. Police officer was conducting a routine roadblock to check for proper drivers' licenses and vehicle registration when he smelled the odor of alcohol emanating from appellant's vehicle. Upon further investigation, the officer determined that there was reasonable ground to believe that appellant was intoxicated. The officer transported appellant to the local jail and administered a chemical breath analysis. Appellant challenged his conviction, alleging that he was denied a fair and impartial jury because a number of jurors during voir dire expressed the view that a person should not operate a motor vehicle if that person had ingested alcohol. No error occurred for refusing to excuse for cause those jurors who honestly expressed their personal views on the subject but then affirmatively indicated their ability to decide appellant's guilt on the law. Appellant challenged the constitutionality of the roadblock. Appellee state had a legitimate interest in ensuring that drivers were properly licensed with proper registration on their vehicles. As such, appellant's conviction was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction, holding that the trial court did not err by refusing to excuse for cause those jurors who honestly expressed their personal views on the subject of consuming alcohol and driving and that appellee state had a legitimate interest in ensuring drivers of vehicles were properly licensed and that vehicles were properly registered and inspected.

 

800 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Overstreet v. George County Sch. Dist.


NO. 97-CA-01456-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


741 So. 2d 965; 1999 Miss. App. LEXIS 358



June 22, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/31/1997. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. KATHY KING JACKSON. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: GEORGE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: MOTION TO DISMISS GRANTED TO APPELLEE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed the decision of the George County Circuit Court (Mississippi) to grant defendant's motion to dismiss her personal injury suit for failure to comply with notice requirements.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was injured when a county school bus collided with her vehicle. After handling the insurance claim herself, she hired an attorney for the personal injury claim. The attorney mailed a notice of claim letter to the appropriate executive officer of the governmental entity and all appropriate parties had notice of the claim from the date of the accident as well as constructive notice of the personal injury claim. The defendant county filed a motion to dismiss arguing that the plaintiff had not strictly complied with the Mississippi Tort Claims Act, Miss. Code. Ann. § 22-56-22, which required that notice be delivered by hand or certified mail. The appellate court held that the plaintiff had substantially complied with the notice requirements when her attorney sent the letter which had many of the requisite details, but the plaintiff could also show that she had previously notified the insurance carrier and several other persons with authority to investigate the incident. The court held that the notice requirement was designed to give the appropriate parties a chance to investigate claims against them and that these parties had that chance.


OUTCOME: The granting of defendant's motion to dismiss for failure to comply with notice requirements was reversed because she had substantially complied with the requirements thereby giving the opposing party sufficient opportunity to investigate.
